Editor's note- See chapter 52, Zoning, for provisions regarding building permits. 
State Law reference- Municipal authority to regulate housing and other structures, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.001 et seq.; building and rehabilitation codes, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.211 et seq.; verification of builder registration required for issuance of local building permit, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.906; regulation of municipal public buildings and grounds generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 281.001 et seq., 301.001 et seq.; plumbing inspector, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.011; plumbing regulations, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.012; dangerous buildings, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.002. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 10-1. - Building and technical codes adopted by reference. 
(a)  The following building and technical codes are adopted by the city subject to those provisions amended or excepted in this chapter, if any: 
(1)  ICC International Building Code, 2000 Edition. 
(2)  ICC International Residential Code for One- and Two-Family Dwellings, 2000 Edition. 
(3)  ICC International Plumbing Code, 2000 Edition. 
(4)  ICC International Mechanical Code, 2000 Edition. 
(5)  ICC International Fuel Gas Code, 2000 Edition. 
(6)  NFPA National Electrical Code, 2002 Edition. 
(b)  In this section, ICC refers to the International Code Council and NFPA refers to the National Fire Protection Association, publishers of the codes adopted in this section. 
(c)  Subsequent editions or amendments to the adopted publications and state amendments and errata shall not become effective unless specifically adopted by the city council. 
(d)  A copy of each adopted code of technical regulations, as well as the adopting ordinance, shall be authenticated and recorded by the clerk and kept on file in the office of the clerk where they shall be available for public inspection. 
Editor's note- See chapter 18, Fire Prevention and Protection, for provisions relative to the city's fire code. 
Sec. 10-2. - Amendments and exceptions to the adopted building code. 
    The ICC International Building Code adopted in this chapter is amended in the following respects: 
(1)  Section 107.1, Chapter 1, Administration of the International Building Code, is amended by adding: 
"In addition to a construction building permit, a temporary housing permit may be authorized for the use, on premises, of a recreational vehicle or manufactured home as a residential unit, provided such use of temporary housing, in residential zoned districts, shall be limited to single family housing for the real property owners only, be located on the permitted property, or on property owned or leased by the permittee adjacent to the permitted property, and be valid for the term of the construction building permit period not to exceed six months, and may be renewed once for a second six-month period. Such temporary housing use shall completely cease upon completion of construction or on the expiration of the time limit stated in the permit whichever occurs first." 
(2)  Section 113, Violation of the International Building Code, is deleted and amended to provide that: 
"Any person who shall violate any provision of this building code, or fail to comply therewith, or with any one of the requirements thereof, or who shall erect, construct, alter, demolish or remove any structure in violation thereof shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and shall upon conviction thereof, be punished as provided in section 1-6. Each such person shall be deemed guilty of a separate offense for each day or portion thereof during which any violation of any of the provisions of the Code is committed or continued." 
(Code 1973, §§ 5-1, 5-2; Ord. No. 924, §§ 1, 2, 14, 7-10-1967; Ord. No. 932, § 1, 8-10-1967; Ord. No. 949, § 1, 12-10-1968; Ord. No. 1005, § 1, 5-12-1971; Ord. No. 1086, 10-11-1973; Ord. No. 1171, § 1, 11-25-1976; Ord. No. 1272, § 1, 8-12-1980; Ord. No. 1420, §§ 1, 2, 12-10-1985; Ord. No. 1612, 11-9-1993; Ord. No. 1667, 1-9-1996; Ord. No. 1749, 11-9-1999; Ord. No. 1798, 5-14-2002) 
Sec. 10-3. - Codes remedial in nature. 
    The city's technical codes are remedial in nature, and shall be construed to secure the beneficial interests and purposes thereof, which are public safety, health, and general welfare through structural strength, stability, sanitation, adequate light and ventilation, and safety to life and property from fire and other hazards attributed to the built environment, including alteration, repair, removal, demolition, use and occupancy of buildings, structures, or premises, and by regulating the installation and maintenance of all electrical, gas, mechanical and plumbing systems (herein service systems). 
Sec. 10-4. - Quality control. 
    Quality control of materials and workmanship is not within the purview of this Code except as it relates to the purposes stated herein. 
Sec. 10-5. - Liability of city. 
    The inspection or permitting of any building, system or plan under the requirements of this Code shall not be construed in any court as a warranty of the physical condition of such building, system or plan or their adequacy. Neither the city nor any employee thereof shall be liable in tort for damages for any defect or hazardous or illegal condition or inadequacy in such building, system or plan, nor for any failure of any component of such, that may occur subsequent to such inspection or permitting. 
Sec. 10-6. - Conflict of regulations. 
    If sections of the technical codes, this Code, and/or state or federal law or regulation specify different materials, methods of construction or other requirements, the most restrictive shall govern. If there is a conflict between a general requirement and a specific requirement, the specific requirement shall be applicable. 
Sec. 10-7. - Referenced standards. 
    Standards referenced in the text of the technical codes shall be considered an integral part of the codes. If specific portions of a standard are denoted by code text, only those portions of the standard shall be enforced. Where code provisions conflict with a standard, the code provisions shall be enforced. Permissive and advisory provisions in a standard shall not be construed as mandatory. 
Sec. 10-8. - Requirements not covered by code. 
    Any requirements necessary for the strength, stability or proper operation of an existing or proposed building, structure, electrical, gas, mechanical or plumbing system, or for the public safety, health and general welfare, not specifically covered by this of the other technical codes, shall be determined by the building official. 
Sec. 10-9. - Alternate materials and methods. 
    The provisions of the technical codes are not intended to prevent the use of any material or method of construction not specifically prescribed by them, provided any such alternate has been reviewed by the building official. The building official shall approve any such alternate, provided the building official finds that the alternate for the purpose intended is at least the equivalent of that prescribed in the technical codes, in quality, strength, effectiveness, fire resistance, durability and safety. The building official shall require that sufficient evidence or proof be submitted to substantiate any claim made regarding the alternate. 
Secs. 10-10-10-36. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ADDITIONAL LOCAL REQUIREMENTS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 10-37. - Barbed wire fences. 
    It is unlawful for any person to make or erect, or cause to be made or erected, within the city any barbed wire fence, or any fence of similar material, around or upon any lot owned by him or in his charge. 
(Code 1973, § 5-9; Ord. No. 1102, § 1) 
Secs. 10-38-10-62. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ELECTRICAL 

Sec. 10-63. - When electrical permit is not required. 
    Notwithstanding any requirement for electrical permits provided in any of the building and technical codes adopted by the city in this chapter, no permit is required for: 
(1)  The installation of electric wiring, devices or equipment installed for or by the electric department of the city, or for or by a public utility corporation operating under a franchise from the city to transmit and sell electric energy, provided that such wiring, devices or equipment are for the use of the electric department or the corporation in its operation as a public utility as provided for in its franchise. 
(2)  The replacement of any electrical fixtures or appliances that requires no change in the electric wiring for such fixture or appliance. 
(3)  The installation of wiring, devices or equipment for communications or any signaling systems operating at 50 volts or less. 
(Code 1973, § 5-27; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-64. - Electrical work that may be performed by persons not registered as contractors. 
    The following acts, work and conduct shall be expressly permitted in the city without necessity of registration as a contractor under this chapter: 
(1)  Electrical work done by a property owner on property owned and occupied or to be occupied as the property owners homestead; provided, however, that all such work or service shall be subject to permit, inspection and approval in accordance with the terms of this chapter and the codes adopted hereunder. 
(2)  Installation of service entrance only to a manufactured home performed by occupant-homeowner, subject to permit, inspection and approval. 
(3)  Electrical work done by persons engaged by any public service company in the construction and maintenance of their public utility systems. 
(Code 1973, § 5-37; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-65. - Tampering with public electrical service equipment. 
    It is unlawful for any person to cut, move or attach to any wire, switch or other property belonging to or controlled by any public service corporation or municipal electric department, or cause the same to be done, unless by permission from such corporation or municipal electric department so owning such wire, switch or other property. 
(Code 1973, § 5-30; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-66. - Liability for damage. 
    This division shall not be construed to relieve from or lessen the responsibility of any person installing, operating or controlling any electric wiring or electrical apparatus for damages to anyone thereby, or for full and faithful performance of the contract, nor shall the city be held as assuming any liability by reason of the inspection authorized herein or certificate or permit issued pursuant to the provisions of this division. This division shall also not be construed to relieve the electrician of his responsibility for any defective work that may have been concealed or escaped the notice of the electrical inspector. 
(Code 1973, § 5-31; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-67. - Meters and circuits. 
(a)  The city electric department shall designate the location of the meter. Dwelling meter loops shall be at an outside point which will be readily accessible to meter readers and testers at all times. Meter loops for other than residence occupancy shall be at a point readily accessible to meter readers and testers during all business hours and shall be outside the building except by special permission from the city electric superintendent. 
(b)  Where possible all meter loops shall be so placed and maintained that no meter dial will be more than 61/2 nor less than 51/2 feet above the permanent standing surface below the meter dial. The meter loop location shall provide free space for testing and servicing of not less than 24 inches in front of each meter and not less than 24 inches in width and in no case of less width than the total width of all meters and metering equipment at each location. No meter loop shall be placed in a washroom, toilet room, storage closet or any similar location, or over plumbing fixtures, machinery or other interfering obstructions. 
(c)  Where two or more meter outlets are grouped or are on the same building, each meter outlet shall be neatly and permanently marked to show the location it serves. Where one or more meter outlets are added to a group or on a building, the person making the addition shall identify the old and the added outlets. 
(d)  Electricians shall install the complete meter loop ready to attach the service with the exception of larger customers where the city electric department may install the necessary current or potential transformers. 
(e)  Required service disconnection means shall be readily accessible and located outdoors immediately after the meter, on all services rated at 200 amps or less. 
(Code 1973, § 5-51; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998; Ord. No. 1798, 5-14-2002) 
Secs. 10-68-10-90. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - FUEL GAS 

Sec. 10-91. - Shut off and disconnection for violations and unsafe conditions. 
(a)  At the direction of the gas inspector, the company distributing gas in the city shall refuse to furnish gas or gas service to any house, building or structure in the city, and shall shut off and disconnect its gas supply or gas connection at any time and in any manner when it may appear to the gas inspector that the installation of any house piping, appliances, fixtures or apparatus, or the construction or maintenance of same, is unsafe or in violation of this chapter. 
(b)  The gas inspector is authorized and empowered to shut off the gas supply when such conditions appear to exist and shall notify the gas company and consumer of his action, and no person shall again turn on the gas supply except with the permission of the gas inspector; however, nothing herein shall be construed so as to relieve the gas consumer from the obligation of making all gas installations and connections in compliance with the provisions hereof. 
(Code 1973, § 5-83; Ord. No. 1133, § 14, 7-5-1927) 
Sec. 10-92. - Approval of gas inspector required for gas turn-on; issuance of certificate of approval. 
(a)  It is unlawful for any gas company, its agents or employees to turn natural gas into the pipes in any building or on any premises situated in the city until it has been furnished a certificate from the gas inspector as herein provided for. 
(b)  Should the gas inspector find that the gas fixtures and fittings on the premises and in the building have been installed in the manner provided for herein, he shall issue a certificate of approval, the same to be in triplicate, and officially signed by him giving authority for the turning on of natural gas into the pipes in such building and on such premises. One certificate shall be furnished to the gas company supplying natural gas, one to the owner of the premises and building and one to be kept on file in the office of the city secretary. 
(Code 1973, §§ 5-84, 5-85; Ord. No. 1133, § 13, 7-5-27) 
Secs. 10-93-10-112. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - UNSAFE BUILDING ABATEMENT CODE 

Sec. 10-113. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Building means any structure or part thereof erected for the support, shelter, enclosure of persons, animals, chattels, or property of any kind. 
    Building official means the designated authority charged with the administration of the building inspection department, or his duly authorized representative. 
    Code enforcement official means the designated authority charged with enforcement of this division, or his duly authorized representative. 
    Dwelling means any building which contains one or more dwelling units used, intended, or designed to be built, used, rented, leased, let or hired out to be occupied, or which is occupied for living purposes. 
    Dwelling unit means a single unit providing complete independent living facilities for one or more persons including permanent provisions for living, sleeping, eating, cooking, and sanitation. 
    Habitable room means a space in a structure for living, sleeping, eating, or cooking. Bathrooms, closets, storage or utility rooms, and similar rooms are not considered habitable rooms. 
    Nuisance includes, but is not limited to, the following: 
(1)  Any public nuisance known at common law or in equity jurisprudence; 
(2)  Any attractive nuisance which may prove detrimental to others, whether a structure, in a building, on the premises of a building, or lot. This includes any abandoned excavations, wells, shafts, basements or cellars, abandoned refrigerators, appliances, building materials, trash or debris, or structurally unsound structures; 
(3)  That which is dangerous to life or detrimental to health; or 
(4)  Any condition which causes a substantial or unreasonable interference with the use and enjoyment of one's property. 
    Structure means that which is built or constructed, an edifice or building of any kind, any piece of work artificially built up or composed of parts joined together in some definite manner, or any part thereof. 
    Unsafe building means any building or structure that has any of the following conditions: 
(1)  The building, structure, or portion thereof is liable to fully or partially collapse. 
(2)  The structure or any part thereof was constructed or maintained in violation of any provision of an applicable city building code, or any other applicable ordinance, law, or code of the city, county, or state. 
(3)  Any means of egress or portion thereof that is of inadequate size or arrangement, dilapidated, in a state of disrepair, or inoperable such that means of egress could be rendered unsafe in case of fire or panic. 
(4)  The foundation or any structural members are 25 percent or more damaged, deteriorated, improperly anchored, or stressed, or ineffective in supporting the imposed loads or maintaining proper clearances from finish grade as required by the minimum standards for housing. 
(5)  Any walls or other vertical structural members which list, lean, or buckle to such an extent that a plumb line passing through its center of gravity falls outside the middle third of its base. 
(6)  The nonsupportive, protective coverings of walls, roofs, ceilings, or floors are 50 percent or more damaged or deteriorated, or ineffective in protecting the structure or inhabitants from weather, vermin, insects, decay, or other causes of structural damage or disease. 
(7)  The structure or any part thereof has been damaged by fire, water, earthquake, wind, vandalism, or other cause to such an extent that it has become either a nuisance or dangerous to the public health, safety, or welfare. 
(8)  Any structure or part thereof that is in such a condition as to constitute a nuisance. 
(9)  The structure has inadequate lighting, ventilation, or sanitation facilities, as required by state or local authorities for certain occupancies. 
(10)  The structure or any part thereof is designed for, or being used or occupied in the commission of a crime. 
(11)  The structure or any part thereof is a fire hazard, or is substandard, dilapidated, or otherwise unfit for human habitation, and is a hazard to public health, safety, or welfare. 
(12)  Any unsecured unoccupied building. 
(13)  Any residential lot, dwelling or dwelling unit not in full compliance with the city's minimum standards for housing. 
    Unsecured unoccupied building means any structure which currently has no legitimate occupant or tenant and which has missing, unlocked, or inoperable doors, windows, or other unsecured openings into the building through which unauthorized entry can be made. 
(Code 1973, § 5-90.04; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-114. - Minimum standards for housing; responsibility of owner. 
    No person shall occupy or permit to occupy any dwelling or dwelling unit for the purpose of living, sleeping, cooking, or eating which is not in compliance with any of the following minimum requirements. 
(1)  Property standards. 
a.  All residential lots shall be free of holes, excavations, sharp protrusions, or other objects or conditions reasonably capable of causing injury to a person. 
b.  All wells, cesspools, or cisterns shall be securely covered or closed. 
c.  Proper drainage shall be provided to prevent standing water or flooding on the land. 
d.  All dead trees or tree limbs that are reasonably capable of causing injury shall be removed. 
e.  All water and sewer lines or conduits shall be properly maintained in a clean and sanitary working condition and free of leaks as required by state and local plumbing standards. 
f.  Property shall be kept clear of any open storage of vehicle parts, used tires, ice boxes, refrigerators, water heaters, stoves, ovens, glass, building material, rubbish, rubble, garbage, and similar material. 
g.  In addition, property shall be kept clear of any junked vehicle(s) as defined by V.T.C.A., Transportation Code ch. 683. 
(2)  Structural standards. 
a.  In all apartments, apartment houses, dwellings, and dwelling units there shall be provided safe, unobstructed, and adequate means of egress leading to a safe and open area at ground level. Every bedroom shall have at least one window or opening which can easily be opened and facing directly to the outside. The total of openable window or opening area in every bedroom leading outside shall be not less than 5.7 square feet. 
b.  All dwellings and dwelling units shall have appropriate and adequate protection from deterioration, and exposure to the elements, which shall include, but not be limited to, paint, water-proofing, and properly installed siding, wall coverings, roofing, ceilings, flooring, and flashing, without holes, cracks, rot, insect damage, leaks, or any other condition which could cause damage to the structure or parts. 
c.  Railings and flooring for stairs, steps, balconies, porches, and elsewhere shall be maintained and free of holes, rot, cracks, and decay so as to be a safe means of egress in panic or emergency. 
d.  Attics, basements, cellars, and crawl spaces shall be adequately ventilated and properly drained as specified in the city building code. Floor and wall framing members subject to rot or insect damage of any dwelling shall maintain a clearance to ground of not less than 16 inches, except for girders which shall maintain a clearance to ground of not less than ten inches. 
e.  Fireplaces, flues, heat exchangers, chimneys, and other exhaust venting shall be in proper working order and maintain proper clearances from combustible material. 
f.  Broken or missing windows, holes, breaks, and loose surface materials on floors, walls, and ceilings shall be properly repaired or replaced with like materials. 
g.  All exterior doors, windows, skylights and associated locks and hardware shall be weathertight and kept in good working order. 
h.  Ceiling height in any room of any dwelling shall be not less than seven feet from finish floor level. 
(3)  Utility standards. 
a.  Each occupied dwelling unit shall have all required plumbing fixtures properly maintained and connected to the public water and sewer as provided in the city's building and technical codes. 
b.  Each occupied dwelling unit within 300 feet of available electric utility supply shall have all required electrical outlets and equipment connected to such electric supply. 
c.  Heating equipment which is capable of maintaining a constant temperature of at least 68 degrees Fahrenheit throughout any dwelling, or a utility connection for such equipment in each habitable room, shall be installed and maintained. Unvented fuel heaters are prohibited except for heaters listed for unvented use. Unvented fuel heaters are prohibited in any bedroom. 
(4)  Health standards. 
a.  All premises, indoors and out of doors, shall be kept free of rodents and vermin. 
b.  All dwelling units which do not have a central air conditioning system shall have screens on all exterior openable windows, and shall have a screen door with a self-closing device on all exterior doors except for the main entrance door. 
c.  Accessory buildings, vacant structures, and dwellings, or portions thereof, shall be kept free from rubbish and garbage. 
d.  Every toilet room, bathroom, and kitchen floor surface shall be constructed and maintained so as to be substantially impervious to water and so as to permit such floor to be kept in a clean and sanitary condition. 
(5)  Sanitary facilities. 
a.  Every dwelling unit shall contain at least one kitchen sink, one tub or shower, one lavatory, and one water closet, all in good working condition and properly connected to the public water and sewer system. All fixtures and piping shall be properly installed and kept free from defects, leaks and obstructions. 
b.  All required plumbing fixtures shall be located within the dwelling unit and be accessible to the occupants of the same. The water closet and the tub or shower shall be located in a room affording privacy to the user and shall have a minimum total floor area of 25 square feet. 
c.  Every dwelling unit shall have connected to the kitchen sink, lavatory, and tub or shower an adequate supply of both cold water and hot water connected to the public water system. 
d.  Every dwelling shall have a water heater properly installed and maintained and capable of heating incoming water to a temperature of 120 degrees Fahrenheit and capable of storing not less than 30 gallons of heated water. 
e.  Every dwelling unit shall have garbage disposal facilities or garbage storage containers as specified by chapter 38. 
(6)  Fire protection. 
a.  No person shall occupy any dwelling unit which is not in compliance with the city fire prevention code. 
b.  Every dwelling unit shall have at least one approved, listed, properly installed and maintained smoke detector in good working condition. 
c.  All cooking, lighting, and heating equipment shall be installed and maintained in accordance with building, electrical, mechanical, gas, and fire prevention codes of the city. Portable cooking and lighting equipment employing flame is prohibited indoors. 
(7)  Light and ventilation. 
a.  Every habitable room shall have at least one window which is easily opened and facing directly to the outdoors. The minimum total, openable window area shall be 5.7 square feet or eight percent of the total room floor area. Yearround mechanically ventilated air conditioning systems may be substituted for windows in rooms other than rooms used for sleeping. 
b.  Bathrooms shall comply with the light and ventilation requirements when not equipped with approved exhaust ventilators. 
(8)  Electric lights and outlets. 
a.  Where there is electric service available to the dwelling, every habitable room shall have at least two separate and remote convenience outlets. In addition, bedrooms shall have at least one wall switch controlled ceiling or wall type light fixture. Kitchens shall have at least three separate and remote small appliance outlets and at least one wall switch controlled ceiling or wall type light fixture. Every hall, water closet compartment, bathroom, laundry room, room containing furnace, and room containing electrical service panel or equipment shall contain at least one electrical light fixture to adequately illuminate equipment and facilities. In bathrooms, the light fixture shall be controlled by a wall switch. Every bathroom and laundry room shall contain at least one convenience outlet. 
b.  All fixtures, receptacles, equipment, and wiring shall be installed and maintained in a state of good repair, safe, and capable of being used, and shall be connected to the available electrical utility source. 
c.  Where the determination is made, upon examination of the existing electrical service supply, that such electrical service supply is obsolete or is being used in such a manner as would constitute a hazard to the occupants or would otherwise constitute a hazard to life or property, a correction shall be in order and the city electrical code shall apply. 
(9)  Space requirements. 
a.  Each dwelling unit shall contain at least 150 square feet of habitable floor area for the first occupant and at least 90 square feet of additional habitable floor area for each additional occupant. 
b.  In each dwelling unit of two or more rooms, each room occupied for sleeping purposes shall contain at least 64 square feet of floor area for one occupant and an additional 50 square feet of floor area for each additional occupant. 
c.  Children under 12 months of age shall not be considered occupants, and one-half of the area requirements shall apply to children under 12 years of age for purposes of additional occupants in subsection (9)a of this section and general occupants in subsection (9)b of this section. 
(Code 1973, § 5-90.06; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994; Ord. No. 2141, § 1, 4-10-2018) 
Sec. 10-115. - Inspection. 
    For the purpose of ascertaining whether violations of this division exist, the code enforcement official, or any other person authorized by the building and standards commission, is authorized at a reasonable time, without a search warrant, to inspect: 
(1)  The exterior of a structure and premises which contain no structure; and 
(2)  The interior of a structure, if unsecured and abandoned, or if the permission of the owner, occupant, or person in control is given. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.18; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-115A. - Inspection prior to reconnection. 
    It is unlawful for any city employee or agent to turn on city utility services to any premises in the city if that premises has had utilities/services disconnected for two or more business days until the city inspector/code enforcement officer has completed an inspection and has determined the property meets the minimum housing standard as adopted by the City of Yoakum. 
(Ord. No. 2119, § 1, 12-13-2016) 
Sec. 10-116. - Disconnecting public utilities. 
    The code enforcement official may request that public utilities be disconnected: 
(1)  In order that demolition or removal may be accomplished without delay in those cases where the structure is vacant and has been ordered demolished or removed; or 
(2)  If a condition exists, relating to the utility, which constitutes a threat to health or safety, and if after written notice to the owner, providing a reasonable period of time to correct the condition, the owner fails or refuses to do so within such period. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.20; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-117. - Assessment. 
(a)  Expenses and costs incurred by the city under this division shall be charged to the owner of the unsafe structure or premises on which the costs were incurred. Charges may include but are not limited to the expenses of inspection or testing by third parties, photography, newspaper publication costs, title search fees, attorney fees, costs incurred in identifying, locating, or contacting the owner, mortgagee, and lienholders, labor and equipment costs for preparation of the premises, work to secure, repair, vacate, remove, demolish, cleanup and removal of debris, landfill and waste disposal costs. An administrative fee of $100.00 or ten percent of the expenses and costs, whichever is greater, shall be added to the costs. 
(b)  The city council shall certify the expenses incurred in implementing provisions of this division for billing to the owner of the property. The bill becomes an account receivable upon completion and shall be due within 30 days. 
(c)  If, after 30 days from billing, payment in full has not been made, the city shall assess the expenses on, and have a lien against, the property on which the expenses occurred, unless it is a homestead as protected by the state constitution. 
(d)  Notice of the lien shall be provided to the property owner and the county clerk in a form approved by the city attorney. 
(e)  The city's lien is a privileged lien subordinate only to tax liens and all previously recorded bona fide mortgage liens attached to the real property to which the city's lien attaches. Such lien shall bear interest at the rate of ten percent per annum until paid. 
(f)  The lien shall be extinguished if the property owner or another person having interest in the legal title to property reimburses the city for the total amount due. 
(g)  This remedy shall be available to the city in addition to any penal or other remedy provided by law or equity which the city, state or any other person may have to remedy an unsafe property condition. 
(h)  The city may also direct the city attorney to bring a civil action in a court of competent jurisdiction to collect the amount due plus all associated costs and fees. The city attorney is authorized to make use of whatever legal or equitable remedies available to collect the monies due. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.22; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-118. - Prohibited acts. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupants of an unsafe condition to fail or refuse to comply with any order of the code enforcement official or the commission panel. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct or interfere with the implementation of any action required or permitted by the code enforcement official or commission panel. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person to remove any posted notice including any unsafe structure placard without written permission of the code enforcement official, or for any person to enter the structure except for the purpose of making the required inspections, repairs or demolishing the same. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of any property to move or relocate any prebuilt building older than ten years for any use except for accessory storage uses. 
(e)  It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of any property to move or relocate any manufactured home older than ten years within the city. Previously owned manufactured homes are subject to inspection by the code enforcement official prior to placement to insure conformance with the minimum standards for housing (see section 10-114 of the City of Yoakum Code of Ordinances). 
(Ord. No. 2075, § 1, 12-9-2014; Ord. No. 2146, § 1, 7-10-2018) 
Sec. 10-119. - Penalties. 
    Any person, agent, firm, or corporation who violates any provision of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction shall be fined any sum up to $2,000.00. Each day such violation exists shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.26; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994; Ord. No. 2075, § 1, 12-9-2014) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2075, § 1, adopted December 9, 2014, renumbered § 10-118 as § 10-119. 
Secs. 10-120-10-142. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 10-143. - Violations; penalties and other remedies. 
(a)  General fine; continuing violations. Any person violating this chapter shall, upon conviction, be subject to a fine of up to $2,000.00. Each day such violation exists shall constitute a separate offense. 
(b)  Fine for prohibited pollutant discharges. Any violation relating to point source effluent limitations or the discharge of a pollutant, other than from a nonpoint source, into a sewer system, including a sanitary or stormwater sewer system, owned or controlled by the city is, upon conviction, punishable by a fine not to exceed $5,000.00 per day. 
(c)  Civil action. The city may also direct the city attorney to bring a civil action in a court of competent jurisdiction to enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
(d)  Enforcement of provisions related to nuisance structures and unsafe structures. 
(1)  Expenses incurred by city in curing violations charged to property owner. Expenses and costs incurred by the city in proceedings arising from violation of the adopted existing buildings and property maintenance codes shall be charged to the owner of the unsafe structure or premises on which the costs were incurred. Charges may include, but are not limited to, the expenses of inspection or testing by third parties, photography, newspaper publication costs, title search fees, attorney fees, costs incurred in identifying, locating, or contacting the owner, mortgagee, and lienholders, labor and equipment costs for preparation of the premises, work to secure, repair, vacate, remove, demolish, cleanup and removal of debris, landfill and waste disposal costs. An administrative fee of $100.00 or ten percent of the expenses and costs, whichever is greater, shall be added to the costs. 
(2)  Certificate of expenses. The city council or building and standards commission shall certify the expenses incurred in implementing provisions regarding unsafe structures for billing to the owner of the property. The bill becomes an account receivable upon completion and shall be due within 30 days. 
(3)  Failure of owner to pay expenses; lien for expenses. If after 30 days from billing, payment in full has not been made, the city shall assess the expenses on, and have a lien against, the property on which the expenses occurred, unless it is a homestead as protected by the state constitution. Notice of the lien shall be provided to the property owner and the county clerk in a form approved by the city attorney. 
(4)  City's lien is privileged; interest; payment of lien. The city's lien is a privileged lien subordinate only to tax liens and all previously recorded bona fide mortgage liens attached to the real property to which the city's lien attaches. Such lien shall bear interest at the rate of ten percent per annum until paid. The lien shall be extinguished if the property owner or another person having interest in the legal title to property reimburses the city for the total amount due. 
(5)  Procedure is cumulative to all other remedies available to city. This remedy shall be available to the city in addition to any penal or other remedy provided by law or equity which the city, state or any other person may have to remedy an unsafe property condition. 
(6)  Alternative civil action for collection. The city may also direct the city attorney to bring a civil action in a court of competent jurisdiction to collect the amount due plus all associated costs and fees. The city attorney is authorized to make use of whatever legal or equitable remedies available to collect the monies due. 
(Code 1973, §§ 5-91.22, 5-91.26; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-144. - Double permit fees for construction initiated without required permit. 
(a)  Persons not securing a permit as required by the codes adopted by the city prior to beginning work shall pay as a penalty, in addition to all other applicable penalties, double the applicable permit fee. Permit fees shall be in the amount provided in the city fee schedule. 
(b)  The payment of such double fee shall not relieve any persons from fully complying with the requirements of the code in the execution of the work nor from any other penalties prescribed herein, including, without limitation, penalties as provided in section 1-15 for violation of this chapter. 
(Code 1973, § 5-2.1; Ord. No. 1420, § 3, 12-10-1985; Ord. No. 1798, 5-14-2002) 
Sec. 10-145. - Electrical inspector. 
(a)  Position created. The electrical inspector position is created and may be one and the same as the building codes combination inspector. 
(b)  Appointment; qualifications. The electrical inspector shall be a city employee under the direction and supervision of the director of public works and utilities. The city manager shall approve employment, suspension and termination of the electrical inspector. The electrical inspector shall be well versed in the rules and requirements of the city's electrical and other related codes. 
(c)  Conflict of interest. The electrical inspector shall not engage in the business of master electrician, either directly or indirectly, within the city. 
(d)  Powers and duties. The powers and duties of the electrical inspector, and his assistants when so designated by the city manager, shall be as follows: 
(1)  To have entire supervision over the electrical inspection of all electrical work within the city. 
(2)  Upon application on proper forms for the installation of electrical wiring, devices and equipment, and upon payment of the required fees, to make inspections of all new electrical installations and make reinspections of any existing electrical installations at such time as he may deem necessary for the purpose of safeguarding of life and property within the city. 
(3)  Have the right to enter any building during reasonable hours in the discharge of his official duties for the purpose of making any inspection or test of any electrical wiring, device and equipment therein. Where such installations are found dangerous to life or property or to the work of the fire department or otherwise not in conformity with the ordinances of the city, he is empowered to disconnect such parts of installations or to order disconnection of electric service to any building after giving notice in writing to the parties concerned, and such defective electrical wiring shall not be again connected until made safe as directed by the electrical inspector. 
(4)  To decide all disputed questions pertaining to the installation of all electric wiring, devices and equipment, which shall be interpreted by the electrical inspector by taking into consideration the National Electrical Code, and in the light of the standards generally recognized by the trade concerning the safe and proper installation of electrical wiring, devices and equipment. 
(e)  Interference with by others. It is unlawful for any person to interfere with the electrical inspector or his assistants in the discharge of their duties or to prevent or in any manner attempt to prevent them from carrying out the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1973, §§ 5-21-5-24; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-146. - Gas inspector. 
(a)  Position created; duties generally. The office of gas inspector is created. The city fire marshal or other person designated by the city manager shall perform the duties of such gas inspector. He shall have charge, supervision and control of all matters, rules and regulations pertaining to the installation of natural gas in the city. 
(b)  Duty to inspect; no city liability arises by inspection. It shall be the duty of the gas inspector to go upon any premises in which the use of natural gas is to be installed and to examine all pipings, fittings, and connections placed in the buildings and on the premises, either by the gas company or by any gas fitter, and to see that all rules and regulations have been complied with; but the city shall in no event ever be liable to any person for the manner in which such work of supervision, inspection or reinspection is performed by such gas inspector, or the authorized agents thereof, or for failure to perform such service. 
(c)  Right of entry for inspection. The gas inspector is given full authority to enter any building, structure, house or premises, whether public or private, at all reasonable times for the purpose of inspection. 
(Code 1973, §§ 5-81, 5-82; Ord. No. 1133, § 13, 7-5-1927) 
Sec. 10-147. - Inspection authority. 
    For the purpose of ascertaining whether violations of this chapter exist, the code enforcement official, or any other person authorized by the building and standards commission, is authorized at a reasonable time, without a search warrant, to inspect the exterior of a structure, premises which contain no structure, the interior of an unsecured and abandoned structure, the interior of an occupied structure with permission of the owner, occupant, or person in control of the structure. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.18; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-148. - Disconnecting public utilities. 
    The code enforcement official may request that public utilities be disconnected: 
(1)  So that demolition or removal may be accomplished without delay in those cases where the structure is vacant and has been ordered demolished or removed; or 
(2)  If a condition exists relating to the utility that constitutes a threat to health or safety, and if after written notice to the owner, providing a reasonable period of time to correct the condition, the owner fails or refuses to do so within such period. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.20; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Secs. 10-149-10-179. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - BUILDING AND STANDARDS COMMISSION 

Sec. 10-180. - Authority shared with city council. 
    The city council may act as the building and standards commission and exercise all authority granted to the building and standards commission under this division including, without limitation, holding public hearings regarding alleged violations of the city's building and technical codes. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.00(a); Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-181. - Membership; vacancies; rules; meetings. 
(a)  Regular member panels. The building and standards commission shall consist of one or more five-member panels to be appointed for terms of two years. As near as practical, members shall be qualified in one or more of the fields of fire prevention, building construction, sanitation, health, and public safety. 
(b)  Alternate members. The city council may appoint eight or more alternate members to serve in the absence of one or more regular members when requested to do so by the city manager. The alternate members serve for the same term and are subject to removal in the same manner as regular members. A vacancy is filled in the same manner as a vacancy is filled among the regular members. 
(c)  Removal; filling vacancies. The city council may remove a commission member for cause on a written charge. Before a decision regarding removal is made, the city council must hold a public hearing on the matter if requested by the commission member subject to the removal action. A vacancy shall be filled for the unexpired term. 
(d)  Rules of order; appointment of officers. A majority of the entire commission shall establish rules of order and the appointment of at least a chairperson, vice-chairperson, and secretary and duties thereof. The rules of order shall be in compliance with the provisions of this division. 
(e)  Meetings; oaths; authority to compel attendance of witnesses. Meetings of the commission shall be held at the call of the chairperson and at other times as determined by the commission. All meetings held by the commission shall be open to the public. Each chairperson of a panel, or in his absence, the acting chairperson, may administer oaths and compel the attendance of witnesses. 
(f)  Minutes and other records. The commission shall keep minutes of its proceedings showing the vote of each member on each question or the fact that a member is absent or fails to vote. The commission shall keep records of its examinations and other official actions. The minutes and records shall be filed immediately in the office of the commission as public records. 
(Code 1973, §§ 5-91.00(b)-(e), 5-91.02(b), (e), (f); Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-182. - Powers and duties generally. 
    The commission is authorized to hold public hearings to determine compliance with, or alleged violations of, city building and technical codes, including minimum property maintenance requirements. The commission shall also hear appeals from persons aggrieved by orders or decisions of city officials made in enforcement of this chapter. The commission may further make recommendations to the city council as to any needed modifications, amendments, and changes in this chapter, and shall carry out such other duties as may be required from time to time by the city council or state law. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.00(a), (f); Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-183. - Hearing authority and procedure. 
(a)  Minimum number of members in review panel. All cases heard by the commission may be heard by any panel, but at least four members of any panel must hear a case. 
(b)  Concurring vote of four members required. The concurring vote of four members of the commission is necessary to take any action under this article and any other ordinance under its jurisdiction adopted by the city. 
(c)  Code enforcement official must appear at hearing. The code enforcement official shall present all cases initiated by the city to be heard by the commission. 
(d)  Evidence, testimony and defense. There shall be provided ample opportunity at the public hearing for the presentation of evidence or testimony by respondents, persons opposing charges, and the code enforcement official relating to alleged violations of this chapter. 
(e)  Time and method of giving notice of hearing. Notice of all proceedings before the commission must be given: 
(1)  By certified mail, return receipt requested, to the record owners of the property affected, and each holder of a recorded lien against the affected property, as shown by the records in the office of the county clerk of the county in which the affected property is located if the address of the lienholder can be ascertained from any applicable instruments on file in the office of the county clerk; 
(2)  To all unknown owners, by posting a copy of the notice on the front door of each improvement situated on the affected property, or as close to the front door as practical; and 
(3)  By publication in a newspaper of general circulation within the city on one occasion. 
The notice shall be mailed, published, and posted on or before the tenth day before the date of the hearing before the commission and must state the date, time, and place of the hearing. 
(f)  Filing copy of notice in official real property records. The commission may file notice of a proceeding before a commission panel in the official public records of real property in the county in which the affected property is located. The notice must contain the name and address of the owner of the affected property if that information can be determined from a reasonable search of the instruments on file at the office of the county clerk, a legal description of the affected property, and a description of the proceeding. The filing of the notice is binding on subsequent grantees, lienholders, or other transferees of an interest in property who acquire such interest after the filing of the notice and constitutes notice of the proceeding on any subsequent recipient of any interest who acquires such interest after the filing of the notice. 
(g)  Final determination by commission. The commission may: 
(1)  Declare a structure or premises substandard, dangerous, or otherwise in violation of this chapter. 
(2)  Order an unsafe condition be abated, vacated, secured, repaired, removed or demolished within a fixed period. 
(3)  Order, in appropriate cases, the immediate abatement, vacation, securing, repairing, removal, or demolition of the unsafe condition, the entry onto private property to secure such abatement if it is determined that conditions exist on the property that constitutes a violation of this article or any other ordinance within its jurisdiction, and order action to be taken as necessary to remedy, alleviate, or remove any unsafe structure found to exist. 
(4)  Issue orders or directives to any peace officer of the state, including a sheriff or constable or the chief of police of the city, to enforce and carry out the lawful orders or directives of the panel. 
(5)  Determine the amount and duration of the civil penalty the city may recover as provided in this article. 
(h)  Notice of final determination. The commission shall: 
(1)  Promptly send by first class mail, certified return receipt requested, a copy of any final decision and order to all persons to whom notice is required to be sent under this section; and 
(2)  Publish an abbreviated copy of the order one time in a newspaper of general circulation in the city, within ten calendar days after the date of the mailing of the copy as required in this section, including street address or the legal description of the property, the date of hearing, a brief statement indicating the results of the order, and instructions stating where a complete copy of the order may be obtained. A copy shall be filed in the office of the city clerk. 
(i)  Effect of final determination; civil penalties. A determination made under this article is binding and constitutes prima facie evidence of the penalty in any court of competent jurisdiction in a civil suit brought by the city for final judgment in accordance with the established penalty. To enforce any civil penalty under this article, the city clerk must file with the district clerk of the county in which the city is located a certified copy of the order of the commission panel establishing the amount and duration of the penalty. No other proof is required for a district court to enter final judgment on the penalty. If no appeals are taken from the decision of the commission panel within the required period, the decision of the commission panel is, in all things, final and binding. 
(j)  Rehearing and reconsideration; stay of proceedings. Any owner, lienholder, or mortgagee of record jointly or severally aggrieved by any decision or order of a commission panel may request a single rehearing of the case by a second, existing, duly appointed commission panel, or if no such panel exists, the same may request reconsideration from the first panel. The request must be in writing, addressed to the commission, specifying the grounds for the request, and received by the commission or postmarked on or before the tenth day after the mailing of the notice required under this article. The rehearing or reconsideration panel shall consider the grounds for the request for rehearing or reconsideration and may approve or deny the request. Only the approval of the request for rehearing or reconsideration stays all other proceedings. 
(k)  Appeal. After a final decision of the commission under this article, any owner, lienholder, or mortgagee of record remaining jointly or severally aggrieved by the final decision of the commission may appeal the decision to a court of competent jurisdiction in accordance with state law. 
(Code 1973, §§ 5-91.02(a), (c), (d), 5-91.04, 5-91.06, 5-91.08-5-91.10, 5-91.14; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-184. - Parties against whom judgment is issued; standing to challenge judgment. 
    An abstract of judgment shall be issued against all parties found to be owners of the subject property or in possession of that property. A lienholder does not have standing to bring a proceeding under this article on the ground that the lienholder was not notified of the proceedings before the commission panel or was unaware of the condition of the property, unless the lienholder had first appeared before the commission panel and entered an appearance in opposition to the proceedings. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.12; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 10-185. - Alternative authority for city to proceed in municipal court. 
    This article does not affect the ability of the city to proceed under the jurisdiction of the municipal court. 
(Code 1973, § 5-91.16; Ord. No. 1618, 4-12-1994) 
Secs. 10-186-10-208. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - CONSTRUCTION BOARD OF ADJUSTMENTS AND APPEALS 

Sec. 10-209. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Builder means one that builds, who contracts for and supervises the construction of buildings. 
    Building industry representative means one who sells building supplies. 
    Code official means the city's building, plumbing, electrical, and mechanical code enforcement officer or one charged with enforcement of codes or ordinances. 
    Contractor means one that provides materials and services at a specified price for the construction of buildings. 
    Design professional means a registered professional engineer or architect. 
    Health or medical professional means the city's appointed health officer, medical doctor, dentist, or physician's assistant. 
    Legal professional means an attorney. 
(Code 1973, § 5-122; Ord. No. 1674, §§ I, 2, 5-14-1996) 
Sec. 10-210. - Established. 
    The city has established a construction board of adjustments and appeals, which consists of seven members and two alternates. The board shall be appointed by the city council. 
(Code 1973, § 5-123; Ord. No. 1674, § II, 5-14-1996) 
Sec. 10-211. - Membership, officers, meetings and rules of procedure. 
(a)  Regular members. The board shall consist of seven members composed of, to the extent possible, individuals with knowledge and experience regarding the city building code, plumbing code, electrical code, mechanical code, and backflow prevention and cross-connection control. The membership should also include, to the extent possible, design professionals, contractors, builders, legal professionals, and health or medical professionals. 
(b)  Alternate members. In addition to the regular members, there should be two alternate members, one member at large from the building industry and one member at large from the public. 
(c)  Conflict of interest. No board member shall act in a case in which he has a personal or financial interest. 
(d)  Terms. The terms of office of the board members shall be staggered so that no more than one-third of the board is appointed or replaced in any 12-month period. The two alternates, if appointed, shall serve one-year terms. 
(e)  Vacancies. Vacancies shall be filled for an unexpired term in the manner in which original appointments are required to be made. 
(f)  Removal from office for failure to attend meetings. Continued absence of any member from required meetings of the board shall, at the discretion of the applicable governing body, render any such member subject to immediate removal from office. 
(g)  Quorum and voting. A simple majority of the board shall constitute a quorum. In varying any provision of this article, the affirmative votes of the majority present, but not less than three affirmative votes, shall be required. In modifying a decision of the code official, not less than four affirmative votes, but not less than a majority of the board, shall be required. In the event that regular members are unable to attend a meeting, the alternate members, if appointed, shall vote. 
(h)  Officers. The board members shall elect from its membership a chairperson, vice-chairperson, and secretary. The election shall be held at the first meeting following the annual term appointments. The secretary of the board shall make a detailed record of all of its proceedings, which shall set forth the reasons for its decision, the vote of each member, the absence of a member, and any failure of a member to vote. 
(i)  Procedural rules and regulations. The board shall establish rules and regulations for its own procedure not inconsistent with the provisions of this article. 
(j)  Meetings. The board shall meet on call of the chairperson. The board shall meet within 30 calendar days after notice of appeal has been received. 
(k)  Powers and duties generally. The board shall have the authority to hear appeals of decisions and interpretations of the code official and consider variances of the technical building, plumbing, electric, and mechanical codes, including backflow prevention and cross-connection control regulations in the manner provided in this article and by state law. 
(Code 1973, §§ 5-124, 5-125, 5-127(a); Ord. No. 1674, §§ III, IV, 5-14-1996) 
Sec. 10-212. - Matters that may be appealed to the board. 
    The owner of a building, structure or service system, or his duly authorized agent, may appeal a decision of the code official to the construction board of adjustments and appeals whenever any one of the following conditions are claimed to exist: 
(1)  The code official rejected or refused to approve the mode or manner of construction proposed to be followed or materials to be used in the installation or alteration of a building, structure or service system. 
(2)  The provisions of the applicable code or ordinance do not apply to the specific case. 
(3)  That an equally good or more desirable form of installation can be employed in any specific case. 
(4)  The true intent and meaning of the applicable code or ordinance, or any of the regulations thereunder, have been misconstrued or incorrectly interpreted. 
(Code 1973, § 5-126(a); Ord. No. 1674, § V, 5-14-1996) 
Sec. 10-213. - Notice of appeal to board. 
(a)  Form and time for filing. Notice of appeal to the board shall be in writing, addressed to the board and filed within 30 calendar days after the decision is rendered by the code official. Appeals shall be in a form acceptable to the board. 
(b)  Time for appeal may be shortened for unsafe or dangerous buildings or service systems. In the case of a building, structure or service system which, in the opinion of the code official, is unsafe, unsanitary or dangerous, the code official may, in his order, limit the time for such appeals to a shorter period. 
(Code 1973, § 5-126(d); Ord. No. 1674, § V, 5-14-1996) 
Sec. 10-214. - Authority of board to grant variances. 
(a)  Required findings. The construction board of adjustments and appeals, when so appealed to and after a hearing, may vary the application of any provision of the applicable code or ordinance to any particular case when, in its opinion, the enforcement thereof would do manifest injustice and would be contrary to the spirit and purpose of this or the technical codes or public interest, and also finds that: 
(1)  Special conditions and circumstances exist which are peculiar to the building, structure or service system involved and which are not applicable to others; 
(2)  The special conditions and circumstances do not result from the action or inaction of the applicant; 
(3)  Granting the variance requested will not confer on the applicant any special privilege that is denied by the applicable code or ordinance to other buildings, structures or service system; 
(4)  The variance granted is the minimum variance that will make possible the reasonable use of the building, structure or service system; and 
(5)  The grant of the variance will be in harmony with the general intent and purpose of the applicable code or ordinance and will not be detrimental to the public health, safety and general welfare, and shall be in conformance with state and federal requirements. 
(b)  Conditional variances. In granting the variance, the board may prescribe a reasonable time limit within which the action for which the variance is required shall be commenced or completed, or both. In addition, the board may prescribe appropriate conditions and safeguards in conformity with the applicable code or ordinance. Violation of the conditions of a variance shall be deemed a violation of the applicable code or ordinance. 
(Code 1973, § 5-126(b), (c); Ord. No. 1674, § V, 5-14-1996) 
Sec. 10-215. - Final decisions. 
(a)  To be entered without delay. The board shall in every case reach a decision without unreasonable or unnecessary delay. 
(b)  Reasons for decision to be included. Each decision of the board shall include the reasons for the decision. 
(c)  Duty of city official to comply with decision. If a decision of the board reverses or modifies a refusal, order, or disallowance of the code official or varies the application of any provision of this article, the code official shall immediately take action in accordance with such decision. 
(d)  Decision to be filed in the office of the code official. Every decision shall be promptly filed in writing in the office of the code official and shall be open to public inspection. 
(e)  Notice to parties and public. A certified copy of the decision shall be sent by mail or otherwise to the appellant and a copy shall be kept publicly posted in the office of the code official for two weeks after filing. 
(f)  Decisions final subject to remedies at law or in equity. Every decision of the board shall be final, subject however to such remedy as any aggrieved party might have at law or in equity. 
(Code 1973, § 5-127(b); Ord. No. 1674, § VI, 5-14-1996) 
Sec. 10-216. - Role of city council regarding questions of interpretation and enforcement. 
(a)  It is the intent of this chapter that all questions of interpretation and enforcement shall be first presented to the administrative official, and that such questions shall be presented to the board of adjustments only on appeal from the decision of the city inspector, and that recourse from the decisions of the board of adjustments shall be to the courts as provided by state law. 
(b)  It is further the intent of this chapter that the duties of the city council in connection with this chapter shall not include hearing and deciding questions of interpretation and enforcement that may arise. The procedure for deciding such questions shall be as provided in this article. Under this chapter the city council shall have only the duties of considering and adopting or rejecting proposed amendments or the repeal of this chapter, as provided by law, and establishing fees as provided in this article. 
(Ord. No. 1500, § 12, 1-10-1989) 
Secs. 10-217-10-232. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - EXAMINATION AND LICENSING OF ELECTRICIANS 

Sec. 10-233. - Examining and supervising board of electricians created; membership. 
    There is created a board for the examination of electricians within the city, to be known as the examining and supervising board of electricians. The board shall consist of five members. One member shall be the fire marshal of the city, one member shall be the electrical superintendent, two members shall be master electricians licensed and bonded with the city, and one shall be a citizen at large member. The members of the board shall be appointed by the mayor, subject to the approval by the city council. The members of such board shall continue to act as the examining and supervising board of electricians until their successors have been appointed and such appointments approved by the city council. If for any reason a vacancy is created on the board, the mayor shall appoint a new member. Such appointment shall not become effective until approved by the city council. 
(Code 1973, § 5-33; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-234. - Compensation. 
    Members of the examining and supervising board of electricians shall receive no compensation for their services on the board other than the fees which may be allowed them by the city council for conducting examinations of applicants for licenses. 
(Code 1973, § 5-34; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-235. - Conducting examinations, waiving. 
(a)  The board created above may fix dates at reasonable times for having applications for examinations for licenses, and may pass upon all persons engaged in the electrical business as master electricians, journeyman electricians and maintenance electricians. 
(b)  A nonrefundable fee shall be assessed on all applicants' license. The fee for a master's examination or a journeyman and maintenance examination shall be as set from time to time by the city council, in the manual of fees and service charges of the city. 
(c)  The examining and supervising board of electricians may waive the requirements of an examination upon presentation to the board of evidence of experience and education which clearly shows the applicant's qualification for the type of license for which applied. The board shall have the complete control in establishing qualifications required for the type of license for which applied. Such licenses may be renewable, nonrenewable, or designated for specific projects. 
(Code 1973, § 5-35; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-236. - Issuance of license. 
(a)  Whenever an applicant successfully meets the requirements prescribed by the board, the board shall issue a license to such person and shall record the issuance of such license in a book to be kept for such purpose. No license shall be issued to a master electrician until the required bond is filed and license fee paid. An electrician's license shall not be issued to any previous holder of one which has been revoked, except upon a new application, approved by the examining board. 
(b)  For the purpose of this article, a valid electrician's license issued by the state meets all of the requirements of a city-issued electrician's license herein, and is accepted in lieu of such city-issued license, and entitles such license holder to do work within the scope of the electrical license in accordance with all electrical codes and regulations of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 5-38; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998; Ord. No. 1869, § 1, 3-8-2005) 
Sec. 10-237. - License period, renewal authorized. 
    All renewable licenses expire on each December 31. Such licenses must be renewed each year prior to expiration. Holders of licenses which have expired must apply for new licensing in the same manner as new license applicants. 
(Code 1973, § 5-40; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-238. - License not transferable, illegal use of licensee's name. 
    No license shall be transferable and no holder thereof shall allow his name to be used by any other party, either for the purpose of doing work or obtaining a permit under penalty of forfeiture of his license and punishment as provided in section 1-15. 
(Code 1973, § 5-41; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-239. - Scope of master electrician's license. 
    A master electrician's license shall entitle the holder thereof to engage in the business of installing wiring and electrical apparatus inside or on any building for use in connection with electric light, heat or power within the city, and installing wiring and electrical apparatus inside or on any building for use in connection with electric light, heat or power outside the city if the property is served by the municipal electric system. 
(Code 1973, § 5-42; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Sec. 10-240. - Suspension and revocation of license. 
    The electrical inspector shall have the right and authority to suspend the license of any electrician, upon the violation of any portion of this chapter, and the electrical inspector shall, upon suspension, file with the city clerk a statement setting forth the reasons for such suspension, a copy of such report to be filed with the clerk, to be delivered to the electrician. Any electrician aggrieved by such suspension, may file a written appeal to city council within ten days of receipt of suspension notice. Presentation and consideration of the appeal shall be presented to city council at their next regular scheduled meeting. The city council may affirm or rescind such suspension or revoke the license and order the forfeiture of a master electrician bond. In the event that the master electrician whose license has been suspended fails or refuses to appeal to the city council within ten days from the date of such suspension the city clerk shall place before the city council the report of the electrical inspector at the next regular meeting for action by the city council to revoke the suspension or to revoke the license and forfeit the bond as herein provided. 
(Code 1973, § 5-43; Ord. No. 1719, 5-12-1998) 
Chapter 12 - BUSINESSES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal regulation of miscellaneous businesses, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 215.002 et seq.; home rule municipal authority to license any lawful business or occupation that is subject to its police powers, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 215.075; municipal authority to regulate sexually oriented business, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 243.001 et seq.; uniformity required in the issuance of local permits, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 245.001 et seq.; occupations generally, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 1.001 et seq.; Food, Drug and Cosmetic Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 431.001 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 12-1-12-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - OCCUPATION TAXES 

Sec. 12-19. - Levy generally. 
    There is levied and shall be collected and apportioned to the general current expense fund an annual occupation tax on every person engaged in any calling, profession, trade or occupation, who is taxed by the state, an occupation tax of one-half of the amount that is levied by the state on such callings, professions, trades or occupations, except those which, under the laws of the state, are exempt from city occupation taxes. 
(Code 1973, § 13-1; Ord. No. 1012, § 2, 6-8-1971) 
State Law reference- Authority for levy of occupation taxes by municipalities, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 302.101. 
Sec. 12-20. - Due dates. 
    Occupational license taxes shall be due and payable from October 1 to January 31, unless otherwise provided by the city council. 
(Code 1973, § 13-2; Ord. No. 1012, § 3, 6-8-1971) 
Secs. 12-21-12-43. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PEDDLERS, SOLICITORS AND ITINERANT VENDORS[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to license, tax, suppress or otherwise regulate hawkers and peddlers, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 215.031; cancellation of certain home solicited consumer transactions, V.T.C.A., Business and Commerce Code § 601.001 et seq.; certain peddlers regarded as retailers for purposes of sales and use taxes, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 151.024. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 12-44. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Commodities, goods or merchandise means personal property of any nature whatsoever. 
    Itinerant vendors. 
(1)  The term "itinerant vendors" means any individual, firm, organization or corporation, as well as their representatives, agents and employees, who engages in a business in the city of selling, or offering for sale, any goods or merchandise, or exhibiting the same for sale or for the purpose of taking orders for the sale thereof, who displays, exhibits, sells or offers for sale such goods, merchandise or services upon or from a truck or other vehicle within the city, or who temporarily hires, rents, leases or occupies any room or space in any building, structure or other enclosure, or any vacant lot in the city upon which such business is to be operated or conducted. 
(2)  The term "itinerant vendors" shall not include individuals connected with a noncommercial or nonprofit purpose or cause. 
    Noncommercial or nonprofit purpose or cause means a purpose or cause not created, existing or espoused for the generation of a profit or the remuneration of individuals, including, but not limited to, the religious or charitable solicitation of contribution, seeking political support or contributions, the promotion of civic causes, the promotion of conservation of resources or animals, or advocating a philosophy or religion. 
    Peddler means any individual, firm, organization or corporation, as well as their representatives, agents and employees, who engages in the business in the city of selling, offering for sale or exhibition for sale of any commodity or service, from house to house, or from place to place and not from one established spot. Delivery of the commodity or service is made or to be made at the time of sale. Collection of the sales price at time of sale or later is immaterial. The term "peddler" shall not include individuals connected with a noncommercial or nonprofit purpose or cause. 
    Services means the performance of labor for the benefit of another, or at another's command. 
    Solicitor or canvasser means any individual, firm, organization or corporation, as well as their representatives, agents and employees, who engages in the business in the city of taking orders for future delivery of commodities or services, or solicits subscriptions, orders contributions or any kind of support, for remuneration or gain, from house to house, or from place to place. The term "solicitor" or "canvasser" shall not include individuals connected with a noncommercial or nonprofit purpose or cause. 
    Temporary business means the business use of any real property in the city for which definite written arrangements with the owner have not been made for occupancy of the premises for a term in excess of 90 days. Definite arrangements would include, without being limited to, a lease agreement or other document conveying an enforceable right of occupancy. 
(Code 1973, § 13-50) 
Sec. 12-45. - Exemptions. 
(a)  A vendor who sells or exhibits for sale commodities, goods, merchandise or services to persons engaged in the business of buying, selling and dealing in the same within the city is exempt from the coverage of this article. 
(b)  Citizens conducting nonprofit, fundraising activities, who represent a bona fide local civic, religious, humanitarian or youth organizations located inside the city limits or extraterritorial jurisdiction, are exempt from the provisions of this article. 
(c)  Farmers who raise and produce what they offer for sale are exempt from the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1973, § 13-51; Ord. No. 1474, 10-13-1987; Ord. No. 1987, § 1, 6-14-2011) 
Sec. 12-46. - Garage sales. 
    Garage sale operators are not required to register pursuant to this article. However, garage sales in the city shall be limited to two such sales per year, per location or individual. No sale shall be conducted for more than three days. 
(Code 1973, § 13-51; Ord. No. 1474, 10-13-1987; Ord. No. 1987, § 1, 6-14-2011) 
Sec. 12-47. - Prohibited acts. 
    It is unlawful for any peddler, solicitor, canvasser or itinerant vendor to: 
(1)  Conduct a business or related activities in the city without a valid registration certificate, as required by this article. 
(2)  Conduct a business or related activities in the city without a valid identification card, as required by this article. 
(3)  Conduct a business or related activities without visibly displaying the identification card issued to that individual. 
(4)  Alter a registration certificate or identification card issued by the city. 
(5)  Conduct a business or related activities within the city after the expiration of the registration certificate issued by the city. 
(6)  Conduct a business or related activities within the city different than described in the registration statement required by this article. 
(7)  Provide false, inaccurate or misleading information in the registration statement. 
(8)  Use a vehicle in the conduct of a business or related activities not identified in the registration statement. 
(9)  Conduct a business from a location within the city not listed in the registration statement. 
(10)  Conduct a business selling, offering for sale, exhibiting for sale, or taking of orders for delivery of any commodities, goods, merchandise or services not listed and described in the registration statement. 
(11)  Sell, assign or transfer, or any attempted sale, assignment or transfer, of a registration certificate or identification card. 
(12)  Conduct a business on any public sidewalk, public street right-of-way, or other public property within the city, without written authorization from the city clerk.
