Manufactured homes placed or substantially improved on sites in an existing manufactured home park or subdivision within Zones A1-30, AH and AE on the community's FIRM that are not otherwise subject to the provisions of this section shall be elevated so that either the lowest floor of the manufactured home is at least one foot above the base flood elevation or the manufactured home chassis is supported by reinforced piers or other foundation elements of at least equivalent strength that are no less than 36 inches in height above grade and be securely anchored to an adequately anchored foundation system to resist flotation, collapse, and lateral movement. 
(Code 1973, § 81/2-18; Ord. No. 1976, § 18, 11-9-2010) 
Sec. 16-72. - Standards for subdivision proposals. 
(a)  All subdivision proposals, including the placement of manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall be consistent with the requirements of this article. All proposals for the development of subdivisions, including the placement of manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall meet floodplain development permit requirements of this article. 
(b)  Base flood elevation data shall be generated for subdivision proposals and other proposed development, including the placement of manufactured home parks and subdivisions greater than 50 lots or five acres, whichever is lesser, if not otherwise provided pursuant to this article. 
(c)  All subdivision proposals, including the placement of manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall have adequate drainage provided to reduce exposure to flood hazards and shall have public utilities and facilities, such as sewer, gas, electrical and water systems, located and constructed to minimize or eliminate flood damage. 
(Code 1973, § 81/2-19; Ord. No. 1976, § 19, 11-9-2010) 
Chapter 18 - FIRE PROTECTION AND PREVENTION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal fire protection generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 342.001 et seq.; municipal authority to adopt and enforce fire regulations, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 342.003; fire control and prevention generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 344.001 et seq.; regulation of fireworks, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.001 et seq.; fire escapes, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 791.002; city fire loss lists, V.T.C.A., Insurance Code § 2003.051; arson, V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 28.02; prescribed burning standards, V.T.C.A., Natural Resources Code § 153.047. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 18-1. - Arson award. 
    The city offers a reward of $250.00 for information leading to the arrest and conviction of any person found guilty of committing the crime of arson within the city. This reward is a standing offer and shall be paid out of the general fund of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 8-1; Ord. No. 1799, § 1, 5-14-2002) 
Secs. 18-2-18-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - FIRE CODE 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 18-21. - International Fire Code. 
(a)  Adopted. The city has adopted the 2000 International Fire Code, which is incorporated in this section, with the exceptions provided in this section. 
(b)  Penalties for violations. Penalties for violating any provision of the fire code adopted in this section shall be as provided in section 1-15. 
(c)  Terms defined. Wherever the term "municipality" is used in the adopted fire code, it shall be held to mean this city. Wherever the term "code official" is used in the adopted fire code, it shall be held to mean the fire marshal of this city. Wherever the term "fire marshal" is used in the adopted fire code, it shall be held to mean the city fire chief as a city employee under the direction and supervision of the city manager. 
(d)  Amendment. Section 108.1 (board of appeals established) of the adopted fire code is amended to provide: "Whenever the fire marshal shall disapprove an application or refuse to grant a permit applied for, or when it is claimed that the provisions of the code do not apply or that the true intent and meaning of the code have been misconstrued or wrongly interpreted, the applicant may appeal from the decision of the fire marshal to the construction board of adjustments and appeals." 
(e)  Enforcement by fire marshal. The fire code adopted in this section shall be enforced by the city fire marshal. 
(Code 1973, §§ 8-4-8-7; Ord. No. 1799, §§ 4-7, 5-14-2002) 
Secs. 18-22-18-45. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ADDITIONAL LOCAL REGULATIONS 

Sec. 18-46. - Open fires. 
    No open fires for the burning of trash or rubbish within the city are permitted at any time. The term "open fire" includes any fire other than in a stove or furnace which will completely enclose the fire and that is equipped with a flue sufficient to prevent sparks from being blown. 
(Code 1973, § 10-14; Ord. No. 562, 12-8-1949; Ord. No. 767, 2-1-1960) 
Sec. 18-47. - Fireworks. 
    No person shall cast, throw or fire any squib, rocket, cracker, torpedo, grenade, cap or cartridge, or other combustible fireworks of any kind in the city. No person shall exhibit or have in his possession with intent to give away or sell or offer for sale any squib, rocket, cracker, torpedo, grenade or other combustible fireworks of any kind in the city. No fireworks shall be stored within the city. 
(Code 1973, §§ 8-2, 8-3; Ord. No. 1799, §§ 2, 3, 5-14-2002) 
State Law reference- Regulation of fireworks and fireworks displays, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.001 et seq.; authority for local ordinances regulating fireworks, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.004; fireworks safety and education program, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.253. 
Chapter 20 - HEALTH AND PUBLIC WELFARE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Health and the safety of food, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 431.001 et seq.; municipal regulatory authority concerning food service employees not preempted by state regulation, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 438.031 et seq.; municipality which is member of public health district not prohibited from regulating or administering permit system concerning food service establishments, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 437.004(d); municipal public safety generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 341.001 et seq.; practices related to health and safety, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 1951.001 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 20-1-20-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TOBACCO SMOKING/ELECTRONIC CIGARETTES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Smoking tobacco in certain locations prohibited, V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 48.01; Texas Clean Air Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 382.001 et seq.; authority of municipalities to enact and enforce ordinances regarding air pollution, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 382.113. 

Sec. 20-19. - Smoking prohibited in public buildings. 
(a)  It is unlawful for any person to perform the following acts in any public building in the city or within 12 feet of any entrance to any public building: to smoke or light, or carry while lighted, any cigarette, electronic cigarette and/or e-cigarette, cigar, pipe or any tobacco smoking device: 
(1)  It is unlawful for any owner or operator of any public building to allow the operation of that building, including food establishments, unless a no smoking sign or international no smoking symbol is posted at a location clearly visible to a person entering the building. 
(2)  It is unlawful for any owner or operator of any building to place or allow to be placed any ashtrays, smoking paraphernalia or signs that indicate smoking is permitted in any public building or within 12 feet from an entrance to any public building. 
(b)  In this section, the term "public building" means any building other than a building used as a private residence, or the outdoor seating facilities of any city owned property. If portions of a building are used as a private residence and another portion of the building is used for business purposes or commercial activities, then the term "public building," as used herein, shall apply to the portions of the building used for business purposes or commercial purposes, but not the portion used solely as a residence. 
(c)  It shall be an affirmative defense to prosecution under this section if the establishment in which a prohibited activity occurred was a bar at the time of the alleged offense. For purposes of this section, a bar is an establishment that derives more than 65 percent of its revenue from the sale of drinks containing alcohol. 
(Code 1973, § 5-141; Ord. No. 1922, § 1, 5-12-2007; Ord. No. 2110, 5-10-2016) 
Sec. 20-20. - Definitions. 
    Smoke or smoking as used herein shall mean and includes the carrying, possessing or holding of a pipe, cigarette, tobacco product, electronic cigarette or e-cigarette or liquid nicotine of any kind which is burning or emitting a vapor. 
    Electronic cigarette and/or e-cigarette as used herein shall mean any electronic device composed of a mouthpiece, heating element, battery and electronic circuits that provides, or is manufactured or intended to provide, a vapor of liquid nicotine and/or other substances mixed with propylene glycol and/or other substances delivered or deliverable to the user that he/she can inhale in simulation of smoking. This term shall include every version and type of such devices whether they are manufactured or marketed as electronic cigarettes, e-cigarettes, electronic cigars, e-cigars, electronic pipes, e-pipes or under any other product name or description. 
(Ord. No. 2110, 5-10-2016) 
Secs. 20-21-20-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - FOOD AND FOOD ESTABLISHMENTS 

Sec. 20-51. - Definition of director; charges for inspection; state rules adopted. 
(a)  The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Director means the director of the Victoria City-County Health Department, or an authorized representative of such director. 
(b)  Charges for inspection shall be as set from time to time by the director. 
(c)  For the purpose of establishing uniform rules and regulations, the city adopts sections 161 through 171 and sections 173 through 175 of chapter 229 of 25 Texas Administrative Code, which are promulgated by the Texas Board of Health, as amended; and such existing rules as adopted and enforced by the director to carry out the regulations within the jurisdiction of the city. 
(Code 1973, §§ 9-1, 9-3; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985; Ord. No. 1531, §§ 1-3, 7-10-1990) 
Sec. 20-52. - Compliance with article required. 
    No food establishment shall be operated within the city unless it conforms to the requirements of this article. 
(Code 1973, § 9-5; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Sec. 20-53. - Permit-Required. 
    It is unlawful for any person to operate a food establishment in the city who does not possess an unrevoked permit from the director. Such permit shall be posted in a conspicuous place. A person conducting an itinerant restaurant shall not be required to secure a permit. 
(Code 1973, § 9-6; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Sec. 20-54. - Same-Who may obtain. 
    Only persons who comply with the requirements of this article shall be entitled to receive and retain a permit to own or operate a food establishment or itinerant restaurant in the city. 
(Code 1973, § 9-7; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Sec. 20-55. - Same-Duration; fees. 
(a)  Food establishment permits shall be secured for the calendar year or each part thereof in which operations are to be conducted. 
(b)  The fees for food establishment permits are as prescribed in this article. Such fees are to help defray a part of the expenses necessary and incident to the enforcement of this article and are payable to the city clerk after approval is given the food establishment by the director. Upon proof of payment of such fee such permit shall be issued by the director. 
(c)  The fees for the respective food handling licenses shall be charged and collected by the city as set from time to time by the council in the Manual of Fees and Services Charges of the city. 
(Code 1973, §§ 9-8, 9-15; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Sec. 20-56. - Same-Suspension, revocation. 
(a)  When on inspection by the director he determines the owner or operator of a food establishment of this city to be in violation of the requirements of this article and a reinspection is made where required after the lapse of at least 24 hours and it is determined that such owner or operator remains in violation of the requirements of this article, and fails or refuses to voluntarily cease operation until such requirements are met, notice of institution of procedures to suspend or revoke such permit shall be given such owner or operator by the director. Such procedure shall be instituted by the director by filing a copy of his inspection report accompanied by his recommendation for either revocation or suspension of such permit with the city council. 
(b)  The city council may suspend or revoke the permit of such food establishment owner or operator after hearing has been held by such body on such report and recommendation of the director. 
(c)  Such hearing shall be held not less than five nor more than 15 days after such proceedings are instituted. The owner or operator of such food establishment shall be notified by such body of the time and place of such hearing at least three days prior to the date set for such hearing. 
(d)  In the event the director determines that a food establishment is creating an immediate threat to human life or health by remaining open, the director may suspend the food establishment permit of the owner or operator of such establishment and order that such establishment be closed on an emergency basis for a maximum period of 15 days and provide a post-suspension hearing in accordance with this section. 
(Code 1973, § 9-9; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Sec. 20-57. - Same-Reinstatement. 
    Any food establishment owner or operator, the permit of whose establishment has been suspended or revoked, may at any time make application to the director for reinstatement of the permit. Within one day after the receipt of such application stating that the violated provision or provisions of this article have been complied with, the director shall make an inspection, and thereafter as many additional inspections as is necessary to ensure himself that the requirements of this article are not being violated, and shall reinstate such permit immediately when such violated provision or provisions of this article have been complied with. 
(Code 1973, § 9-10; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Sec. 20-58. - Examination, sampling and condemnation of food. 
    Samples of food and other substances may be taken and examined by the director as often as may be necessary for the detection of unwholesomeness, misbranding or adulteration. The director may condemn or forbid the sale of, or cause to be removed or destroyed, any food which such examination proves to be unwholesome or adulterated. 
(Code 1973, § 9-11; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Sec. 20-59. - Inspections. 
    At least once every six months the director shall inspect every food establishment within the city. In case the director discovers the violation of any item of sanitation, the owner or operator of the establishment in which the violation was discovered shall be liable to the suspension of permit and the penalties provided in section 9-16. The director shall notify the owner or operator of any such establishment in which such violation is discovered by leaving a copy of the inspection report at such establishment stating the nature of violation. The director shall make a second inspection after the lapse of such time as he deems necessary for the defect to be remedied, provided such second inspection shall not be made before the lapse of 24 hours after the first inspection when violation was found. 
(Code 1973, § 9-12; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Sec. 20-60. - Access to premises and records. 
    Any person operating a food establishment shall, upon request of the director, permit access to all parts of the establishment and shall permit copying of any or all records of food purchased. 
(Code 1973, § 9-13; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Sec. 20-61. - Penalty. 
    Any person who violates any of the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a Class C misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof unless, otherwise provided in a special section of this article, shall be punished by a fine not to exceed $200.00 and each day of violation of this article shall be considered a separate offense. 
(Code 1973, § 9-16; Ord. No. 1398, 2-12-1985) 
Chapter 22 - HUMAN RELATIONS AND SOCIAL SERVICES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Texas Fair Housing Act, V.T.C.A., Property Code § 301.001 et seq.; rights and responsibilities of persons with disabilities, V.T.C.A., Human Resources Code § 121.001 et seq.; health and human services, V.T.C.A., Human Resources Code § 131.001 et seq.; rights of the elderly, V.T.C.A., Human Resources Code § 102.003; fair campaign practices, V.T.C.A., Election Code § 258.004. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 22-1-22-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - FAIR HOUSING 

Sec. 22-19. - Declaration of policy. 
    It is declared to be the policy of the city to bring about through fair, orderly and lawful procedures, the opportunity of each person to obtain housing without regard to race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status. It is further declared that such policy is established upon a recognition of the inalienable rights of each individual to obtain housing without regard to race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status, and further that the denial of such rights through considerations based on these protected classes is detrimental to the health, safety and welfare of the inhabitants of the city and constitutes an unjust denial or deprivation of such inalienable rights which is within the power and the proper responsibility of government to prevent. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-21; Ord. No. 1870, § 1, 5-10-2005) 
Sec. 22-20. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Director means the city manager or authorized assistant. 
    Discriminatory housing practice means an act which is unlawful under this article. 
    Dwelling means any building, structure or portion thereof which is occupied as, or designed and intended for occupancy as a residence by one or more persons and any vacant land which is offered for sale or lease for the construction or location thereof of any such building, structure or portion thereof. 
    Family means a single individual or a group of individuals living together under one common roof. 
    Major life activities means functions such as, but not limited to, caring for one's self, performing manual tasks, walking, seeing, hearing, speaking, breathing, learning and working. 
    Physical or mental handicap means any physical or mental impairment which substantially limits one or more major life activities. 
    Physical or mental impairment includes: 
(1)  Any physiological disorder or condition, cosmetic disfigurement or anatomical loss affecting one or more of the following body systems: neurological; musculoskeletal; special sense organs; respiratory, including speech organs; cardiovascular; reproductive; digestive; genitourinary; hemic and lymphatic; skin; and endocrine; or 
(2)  Any mental or psychological disorder, such as mental retardation, organic brain syndrome, emotional or mental illness, and specific learning disabilities. 
    Senior adult means a person 55 years of age or older. 
    To rent includes to lease, to sublease, to let and otherwise to grant for a consideration the right to occupy premises not owned by the occupant. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-22; Ord. No. 1870, § 2, 5-10-2005) 
Sec. 22-21. - Interpretation and effect. 
    This article shall in no way be interpreted as creating a judicial right or remedy which is the same or substantially equivalent to the remedies provided under Title VIII of the Civil Rights Act of 1968, commonly known as the Fair Housing Act, codified as 42 USC 3601 et seq., or the Federal Equal Credit Opportunity Act, codified at 15 USC 1691 et seq. All aggrieved parties shall retain the rights granted to them under such acts. In construing this article, it is the intent of the city council that the courts shall be guided by federal court interpretations of the federal law cited in this section. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-23; Ord. No. 1870, § 3, 5-10-2005) 
Sec. 22-22. - Discrimination in the sale or rental of housing. 
    Except as exempted, it is unlawful: 
(1)  To refuse to sell or rent after the making of a bona fide offer or to refuse to negotiate for the sale or rental of, or otherwise make unavailable or deny, a dwelling to any person because of race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status. 
(2)  To discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions, or privileges of a sale or rental of a dwelling or in the provision of services or facilities in connection therewith because of race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status. 
(3)  To make, print or publish, or cause to be made, printed or published, any notice, statement or advertisement with respect to the sale or rental of a dwelling that indicates any preference, limitation or discrimination based on race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status, or an intention to make any such preference, limitation or discrimination. 
(4)  To represent to any person because of race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status, that any dwelling is not available for inspection, sale or rental when such dwelling is in fact so available. 
(5)  To induce or attempt to induce any person to sell or rent any dwelling by representations regarding the entry or prospective entry into the neighborhood of a person of a particular race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-24; Ord. No. 1870, § 4, 5-10-2005) 
Sec. 22-23. - Discrimination in housing financing. 
    It is unlawful for any bank, building and loan association, insurance company, or other person whose business consists in whole or in part in the making of commercial real estate loans to deny a loan or other financial assistance to a person applying therefor for the purpose of purchasing, constructing, improving, repairing or maintaining a dwelling or to discriminate against him in the fixing of the amount, interest rate, duration or other terms or conditions of such loan or other financial assistance because of the race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status of such person or such persons associated therewith or because of the race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status of the present or prospective owners, lessees, tenants or occupants of the dwellings for which such loan or other financial assistance is to be made or given. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-25; Ord. No. 1870, § 5, 5-10-2005) 
Sec. 22-24. - Discrimination in providing brokerage service. 
    It is unlawful for any person to deny another person access to membership in, or participation in any multiple listing service, real estate brokers' organization, or other service, organization or facility relating to the business of selling and renting dwellings or to discriminate against another person in the terms or conditions of such access, membership or participation, on account of race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-26; Ord. No. 1870, § 6, 5-10-2005) 
Sec. 22-25. - Unlawful intimidation. 
    It is unlawful for any person to harass, threaten, harm, damage or otherwise penalize any individual, group or business because such individual, group, or business has complied with the provisions of this article or has exercised in good faith rights under this article, or has enjoyed the benefits of this article, or because such individual, group, or business has made a charge in good faith, testified in good faith, or assisted in good faith in any manner in any investigation, or in any proceeding hereunder or has made any report to the director. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-27; Ord. No. 1870, § 7, 5-10-2005) 
Sec. 22-26. - Exemptions and exclusions. 
(a)  Nothing in this article shall apply to: 
(1)  Any single-family house sold or rented by an owner, provided that: 
a.  Such private individual owner does not own more than three single-family houses at any one time; 
b.  If the owner does not reside in the house at the time of the sale or was not the most recent resident of such house prior to the sale, the exemption granted by this subsection shall apply only with respect to one such sale within any 24-month period; 
c.  Such bona fide private individual owner does not own any interest in, nor is there owned or reserved on such person's behalf, under any express voluntary agreement, title to or any right to all or any portion of the proceeds from the sale or rental of more than three such single-family houses at any one time; 
d.  The sale or rental is made without the use in any manner of the sales or rental facilities or the sales or rental services of any real estate broker, agent or salesman, or of such facilities or services of any person in the business of selling or renting dwellings, or of any employee or agent of any such broker, agent, salesman, or person; and 
e.  The sale or rental is made without the publication, posting or mailing of any advertisement or written notice in violation of this article; but nothing in this provision shall prohibit the use of attorneys, escrow agents, abstractors, title companies and other such professional assistance as necessary to perfect or transfer the title. 
(2)  Rooms or units in dwellings containing living quarters occupied or intended to be occupied by no more than four families living independently of each other, if the owner actually maintains and occupies one of such living quarters as his residence. 
(b)  For the purposes of subsection (a) of this section, a person shall be deemed to be in the business of selling or renting dwellings if: 
(1)  He has, within the preceding 12 months, participated as principal in three or more transactions involving the sale or rental of any dwelling or any interest therein; 
(2)  He has, within the preceding 12 months, participated as agent, other than in the sale of his own personal residence, in providing sales or rental facilities or sales or rental services in two or more transactions involving the sale or rental of any dwelling or any interest therein; or 
(3)  He is the owner of any dwelling designed or intended for occupancy by, or occupied by, five or more families. 
(c)  Nothing in this article shall prohibit a religious organization, association or society or a nonprofit institution or organization operated, supervised or controlled by or in conjunction with a religious organization, association or society from limiting the sale, rental or occupancy of dwellings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose to persons of the same religion or from giving preference to such persons, unless membership in such religion is restricted on account of race, color, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap, or familial status. 
(d)  Nothing in this article shall prohibit a private club not in fact open to the public, which as an incident to its primary purpose or purposes provides lodgings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose, from limiting the rental or occupancy of such lodgings to its members, or from giving preference to its members. 
(e)  Nothing in this article shall bar any person from owning and operating a housing accommodation in which rooms are leased, subleased or rented only to persons of the same sex, when such housing accommodation contains common lavatory, kitchen or similar facilities available for the use of all persons occupying such housing accommodation. 
(f)  Nothing in this article shall prohibit the sale, rental, lease or occupancy of any dwelling designed and operated exclusively for senior adults and their spouses, unless the sale, rental, lease or occupancy is further restricted on account of race, color, religion, sex, national origin, physical or mental handicap or familial status. 
(g)  Nothing in this article shall bar a person who owns, operates or controls rental dwellings, whether located on the same property or on one or more contiguous parcels of property, from reserving any grouping of dwellings for the rental or lease to tenants with a minor child or children; provided, however, in the event that the reserved area is completely leased or rented, the person owning, operating or controlling the rental dwelling may not refuse to rent or lease any other available dwelling to the prospective tenant on the basis of the tenant's status as parent or any other of the protected classifications set forth in this article. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-28; Ord. No. 1870, § 8, 5-10-2005) 
Sec. 22-27. - Violations. 
    No person shall violate any provision of this article, or knowingly obstruct or prevent compliance with this article. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-29; Ord. No. 1870, § 9, 5-10-2005) 
Sec. 22-28. - Enforcement. 
(a)  Generally. The director shall have the responsibility of administering and implementing this article. The director may delegate the authority to investigate and conciliate complaints to other designated city employees. 
(b)  Complaints. 
(1)  Any person who claims to have been injured by a discriminatory housing practice or who believes that he will be irrevocably injured by a discriminatory housing practice that is about to occur (hereinafter referred to as the charging party) may file a complaint with the director. Such complaints shall be in writing and shall identify the person alleged to have committed or alleged to be committing a discriminatory housing practice and shall state the facts upon which the allegations of a discriminatory housing practice are based. The director shall prepare complaint forms and furnish them without charge to any person upon request. 
(2)  The director shall receive and accept notification and referral complaints from the U.S. Attorney General and the secretary of housing and urban development pursuant to the provisions of the Title VIII of the Civil Rights Act of 1968, Public Law 90-284, commonly known as the Fair Housing Act of 1968, codified at 42 USC 3601 et seq., and shall treat such complaints hereunder in the same manner as complaints filed pursuant to subsection (b)(1) of this section. 
(3)  All complaints shall be filed within 180 days following the occurrence of an alleged discriminatory housing practice. Upon the filing or referral of any complaint, the director shall provide notice of the complaint by furnishing a copy of such complaint to the person named therein (hereinafter referred to as the respondent) who allegedly committed or were threatening to commit an alleged discriminatory housing practice. The respondent may file an answer to the complaint within 15 days of receipt of the written complaint. 
(4)  All complaints and answers shall be subscribed and sworn to before an officer authorized to administer oaths. 
(5)  If at any time the director shall receive or discover credible evidence and shall have probable cause to believe that any person has committed a discriminatory housing practice as to which no complaint has been filed or is about to be filed, the director may prepare and file a complaint upon his own motion and in his own name and such complaint shall thereafter be treated in the same manner as a complaint filed by a person aggrieved. 
(c)  Investigation and conciliation. 
(1)  Upon the filing or referral of a complaint as herein provided, the director shall cause to be made a prompt and full investigation of the matter stated in the complaint; provided, however, that before any charge becomes accepted for investigative purposes, the director or an investigator shall have personally reviewed with the charging party the allegations contained therein and shall have determined that the charge comes within the provisions of this article. In the event such review results in the determination that a particular charge does not come within the provisions of this article, the charging party shall be given a clear and concise explanation of the reasons why it does not. The respondent shall be provided with a notice of determination. 
(2)  If the director determines that there is not probable cause to believe that a particular alleged discriminatory housing practice has been committed, the director shall take no further action with respect to that alleged offense. 
(3)  During or after the investigation, but subsequent to the mailing of the notice of compliant, the director shall, if it appears that a discriminatory housing practice has occurred or is threatening to occur, attempt by informal endeavors to effect conciliation, including voluntary discontinuance of the discriminatory housing practice and to obtain adequate assurance of future voluntary compliance with provisions of this article. Nothing stated or done in the course of such informal endeavors may be made public by the director, the council, the investigator, the conciliator, the charging party, or the respondent, or be used as evidence in a subsequent proceeding without the written consent of all persons concerned. 
(4)  Upon completion of an investigation where the director has made a determination that a discriminatory housing practice has in fact occurred, if the director is unable to secure from the respondent an acceptable conciliation agreement, then the director must refer the case to the city attorney for prosecution in municipal court. The city attorney shall, after such referral, make a determination as to whether to proceed with prosecution of such complaint in municipal court. 
(5)  Upon determination by the city attorney to proceed with prosecution in municipal court, the respondent may appeal the determination to the city council by filing a written notice of appeal with the city clerk within ten days of notice of determination. The city council shall consider the grounds for the appeal and may approve or deny the request. 
(6)  If review by the city council determines that a discriminatory housing practice has in fact occurred, the city council shall attempt informal endeavors to effect conciliation, including voluntary discontinuance of the discriminatory housing practice and assurance of future voluntary compliance with provisions of this article. If informal endeavors fail, the city council shall instruct the city attorney to proceed with prosecution in municipal court. 
(d)  Penalty. If a discrimination housing practice is found to have in fact occurred and the case has been referred to municipal court, upon conviction the respondent shall be assessed a penalty per violation as provided for in section 1-15. 
(Code 1973, § 61/2-30; Ord. No. 1870, § 10, 5-10-2005) 
Chapter 24 - LAW ENFORCEMENT[1] 
(RESERVED)

Chapter 26 - NUISANCES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal authority for regulation of nuisances and disorderly conduct, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 217.001 et seq.; persons not to permit abandoned property to become public health nuisance, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 341.013; municipality authority to require the owner of a lot in the municipality to keep the lot free from weeds, rubbish, brush, and other environmental nuisances, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.001 et seq.; abatement of junked vehicle declared to be a public nuisance, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.071 et seq.; regulation of fireworks, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.001 et seq.; enhanced penalty for violation ordinances governing fire safety, zoning, or public health and sanitation, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 54.001(b); abatement of common and public nuisances, V.T.C.A., Civil Practice and Remedies Code § 125.001 et seq.; municipal authority regarding substandard buildings, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.001. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 26-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Brush means all trees or shrubbery under seven feet in height and less than three inches in diameter which are not maintained, cared for, or cultivated. 
    Debris means dirt, concrete, rocks, brick or other building materials not being used for on-site improvements pursuant to a duly issued building permit. 
    Junk means all worn-out, worthless, and discarded matter. 
    Lot means land within the property lines and all areas of public right-of-way adjacent to and extending beyond the property line of the lot: 
(1)  To the curbline of adjacent streets, where a curbline has been established; or 
(2)  Where the curbline is not established, to pavement edge, or where pavement is not established, to the active road bed; and 
(3)  To the center of adjacent alleys. 
    Objectionable, unsightly or unsanitary matter means organic or mineral matter or any composition or residue thereof. 
    Owner means any person owning any interest in a lot as indicated by the appraisal district records. 
    Rubbish means garbage, trash and other discarded articles and materials. 
    Stagnant water means water which stands upon premises in such a manner, and over such a period of time, that it is likely to become a breeding place for mosquitoes. 
    Trash means worthless or useless small things other than garbage, debris, brush and yard waste. 
    Weeds means a plant of no value or uncultivated vegetation that may become a harborage for pests. 
(Code 1973, § 10-25; Ord. No. 1763, 10-10-2000) 
Sec. 26-2. - Prohibited nuisances; applicability of provisions. 
(a)  The existence of brush; debris; junk; objectionable, unsightly or unsanitary matter; rubbish; stagnant water; trash; or weeds upon a lot in violation of this chapter is declared to constitute a public nuisance subject to the abatement procedures prescribed in this chapter. 
(b)  It is unlawful for any owner of any lot or parcel of land or portion thereof, occupied or unoccupied, improved or unimproved, to permit weeds or grass to grow to a height greater than 12 inches upon the premises. 
(c)  It is unlawful for any owner of any lot or parcel of land or portion thereof, to allow weeds, grass and trash to create a hazardous or unsafe condition that may interfere with passage on sidewalks, walkways, streets or public right-of-ways adjacent to the lot or property. 
(d)  It is unlawful for any owner of any lot or parcel of land, or portion thereof, occupied or unoccupied, improved or unimproved, to permit any junk, brush, trash, debris, rubbish, or any other objectionable, unsightly, or unsanitary matter of whatever nature to accumulate or be present upon any such lot or parcel of land. 
(e)  It is unlawful for any owner of any lot or parcel of land or portion thereof, occupied or unoccupied, improved or unimproved, to permit the open storage of any inoperative or unused ice box, refrigerator, stove, or similar items upon any such lot or parcel of land. 
(f)  It is unlawful for any owner of a lot to allow stagnant water to accumulate upon the surface of such lot. 
(g)  The provisions of this section shall not be applicable to: 
(1)  The area in excess of 50 feet from any lot line adjacent to public property or private property containing a habitable dwelling; 
(2)  Cultivated, agricultural or pasture land; or 
(3)  Land or facility use approved, permitted or licensed by the city. 
(Code 1973, § 10-26; Ord. No. 1763, 10-10-2000) 
Secs. 26-3-26-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ABATEMENT 

Sec. 26-23. - Duty to abate. 
    It shall be the duty of any owner of any lot or parcel of land or portion thereof, occupied or unoccupied, improved or unimproved, to cut, or cause to be cut, or remove such brush, weeds, grass, debris, rubbish, trash, junk, stagnant water, ice boxes, refrigerators, stoves, and any and all other objectionable, unsightly or unsanitary matter of whatever nature as often as may be necessary to comply with the provisions hereof. 
(Code 1973, § 10-27; Ord. No. 1763, 10-10-2000) 
Sec. 26-24. - Abatement. 
(a)  The city may notify the owner of any lot in writing of the existence of a violation of section 26-2 upon such lot. Such notice shall require the abatement of such violation within seven days of such notice. The notice may be given personally to the owner in writing, or by letter mailed to the owner at the owner's address as recorded in the appraisal district records of the appraisal district in which the property is located. 
(b)  If personal service cannot be obtained, notice can be given by publication once in any newspaper in the city, or by posting the notice on or near the front door of each building on the property to which the violation relates, or by posting the notice on a placard attached to a stake driven into the ground on the property to which the violation relates if the property contains no buildings. 
(c)  In a notice under this section, the city may inform the owner by regular mail and a posting on the property that if the owner commits another violation of the same kind or nature that poses a danger to the public health and safety on or before the first anniversary of the date of the notice, the city without further notice may correct the violation at the owner's expense and assess the expense against the property. If a violation covered by a notice under this section occurs within the one-year period, and the city has not been informed in writing by the owner of an ownership change, then the city without additional notice may do the work or make the improvements required. 
(d)  As additional authority to abate dangerous weeds, according to V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.008, the city may abate, without notice, weeds that have grown higher than 48 inches, that are an immediate danger to the health, life, or safety of any person. 
(Code 1973, § 10-28; Ord. No. 1763, 10-10-2000) 
Sec. 26-25. - Appeal; notice; hearing. 
(a)  Any persons aggrieved by any decision of the city inspector concerning interpretation or administration of this article may appeal such decision to the building and standards commission within seven days after personal notice, or notice by publication, or placard placement. 
(b)  The request must be in writing, addressed to the commission, specifying the grounds for the request, and received by the commission or postmarked on or before the seventh day after the prescribed notice is given. Such valid appeal stays all proceedings of abatement. 
(c)  The commission shall set a reasonable time for the hearing of the appeal, give public notice thereof, as well as due notice to the persons aggrieved and decide the same within a reasonable time. At the hearing, the aggrieved persons may appear in person or by agent or attorney. 
(Code 1973, § 10-29; Ord. No. 1763, 10-10-2000) 
Sec. 26-26. - Collection of cost. 
    The city may direct the city attorney to bring civil action in a court of competent jurisdiction to collect the amount due plus all associated costs and fees, including administrative fees. The city attorney is authorized to make use of whatever legal or equitable remedies are available to collect the monies due. The city may also direct the city attorney to bring a civil action in a court of competent jurisdiction to enforce the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1973, § 10-30; Ord. No. 1763, 10-10-2000; Ord. No. 1861, § 1, 12-14-2004) 
Sec. 26-27. - Corporate liability. 
    In case the owner or occupant of any lot or premises shall be a corporation, and shall violate any such provision, the president, vice-president, secretary, treasurer of such corporation, or any manager, agent or employee of such corporation shall be also severally liable for the penalties herein provided. 
(Code 1973, § 10-31; Ord. No. 1763, 10-10-2000) 
Chapter 28 - OFFENSES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Concurrent jurisdiction of municipal court concerning certain violations of state statutes, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 29.003(b); municipal authority for regulation of firearms and explosives, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 229.001; municipal regulation of discharge of firearms, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 229.002; municipal authority for regulation of nuisances and disorderly conduct, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 217.001 et seq.; juvenile curfews in general law municipalities, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 341.905; review of juvenile curfew orders or ordinances, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 370.002; municipal policy regarding enforcement of drug laws, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 370.003; municipality may not enact or enforce a law making conduct covered under state penal code an offense subject to criminal penalty, V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 1.08. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 28-1. - Police department authorized to enforce federal, state and local law. 
    The city police department is authorized and required to enforce all laws, statutes and ordinances as prescribed by federal, state or local requirements within the city. 
(Code 1973, § 14-42; Ord. No. 1613, § 2, 11-9-1993) 
Sec. 28-2. - Authority of city council to supersede prohibitions. 
    To the extent permitted by state law, any prohibition enumerated in this Code may be superseded by written authority of the city, or superseded in the exercise of official duty by any employee, agent, contractor or authorized personnel within the city. 
(Code 1973, § 14-46; Ord. No. 1613, § 6, 11-9-1993) 
Sec. 28-3. - Discharge of weapons within city prohibited; exceptions; penalty. 
    It is unlawful to discharge or fire any firearm, gun, pistol, air gun, or BB gun projecting lead or any missiles within the city, excepting in a regularly established and licensed shooting gallery; provided that this section shall not be construed to prohibit any officer of the law from discharging a firearm in the performance of his duty; nor to any citizen from discharging a firearm when lawfully defending person or property. 
(Code 1973, § 14-1; Ord. No. 1197, §§ 1, 2, 8-9-1977) 
Sec. 28-4. - Illegally placing advertising on poles. 
    It is unlawful for any person to place or allow to be placed any advertising cards or posters or other like material on any of the poles within the city or on any poles belonging to the city outside the city. 
(Code 1973, § 22-11; Ord. No. 769, § 11001, 11-9-1959) 
Secs. 28-5-28-26. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CONTROLLED SUBSTANCES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 28-27. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Controlled substance shall have the meaning ascribed to it by V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 481.002(5), or any amendments thereto. 
    Controlled substance analogue shall have the meaning ascribed to it by V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 481.002(6), or any amendment thereto. 
    Dangerous drug shall have the meaning ascribed to it by V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 483.001(2), or any amendment thereto. 
    Prohibited substance means a controlled substance, controlled substance analogue, dangerous drug, volatile chemical, or any combination thereof. Such prohibited substances are included by whatever official, common, usual, chemical, trade, street language, or slang name they may be designated. 
    Volatile chemical means abusable volatile chemical, as defined in V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 485.001(1). 
(Code 1973, § 14-41; Ord. No. 1613, § 1, 11-9-1993; Ord. No. 1619, § 1, 4-12-1994) 
Sec. 28-28. - What constitutes offense. 
    A person commits an offense if, with intent to acquire a prohibited substance, he requests, commands or attempts to induce another to sell, donate or otherwise transfer or deliver a prohibited substance to the person. 
(Code 1973, § 14-43; Ord. No. 1613, § 3, 11-9-1993) 
Sec. 28-29. - Conviction. 
    A person may not be convicted on the uncorroborated testimony of the person allegedly solicited and unless the solicitation is made under circumstances strongly corroborative of both the solicitation itself and the actor's intent that the other person act on the solicitation. 
(Code 1973, § 14-44; Ord. No. 1613, § 4, 11-9-1993) 
Sec. 28-30. - Defense. 
    It is no defense to prosecution under this article that no monetary or other consideration was tendered to the person solicited or that the person solicited was unable or unwilling to transfer or deliver a prohibited substance. It is an affirmative defense to any prosecution under this article that a solicitation is made in furtherance of a transaction that would not constitute a violation of any applicable law or that the solicitation is made by a peace officer or federal law enforcement officer in the lawful discharge of his duties or by a law enforcement agent acting in the lawful discharge of an official duty. 
(Code 1973, § 14-45; Ord. No. 1613, § 5, 11-9-1993) 
Sec. 28-31. - Penalty. 
    Violation of this article shall constitute a misdemeanor punishable upon conviction as provided in section 1-15. However, any conduct proscribed hereunder which also constitutes an offense under state law shall not be prosecuted under this article, but shall be prosecuted pursuant to and punishable as provided by the applicable state law. An offense under this article is not a lesser included offense under V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code chs. 481, 483 and 485. 
(Code 1973, § 14-47; Ord. No. 1613, § 7, 11-9-1993) 
Secs. 28-32-28-50. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - SALVIA AND SYNTHETIC CANNABINOIDS 

Sec. 28-51. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Illegal smoking material means any substance, however marketed, which can reasonably be converted for smoking purposes whether it is presented as incense, tobacco, herbs, spices or any blend thereof if it includes any of the chemicals or a comparable chemical as listed as synthetic cannabinoids. Included in this definition, without limitation, are products containing some or all of the above substances marketed under the name "K-2," "K-2 Summit," "K-2 Sex," "Genie," "Dacents," "Zohai," "Sage," "Spice," "KO Knock-out 2," "Mojo," "Pandora Potpourri," "Smoke", "Spice Gold," "Spice Diamond," "Yucatan Fire," "Red Dragon," "Skunk," "Solar Flare," "Pep Spice," "Fire n' Ice," and "Salvia Divinorum," or other alternative names. 
    Illegal smoking material paraphernalia means any paraphernalia, equipment or utensil that is used or intended to be used in smoking, ingesting or inhaling illegal smoking materials and shall include, but is not limited to, the following: 
(1)  Metal, wooden, acrylic, glass, stone, plastic or ceramic pipes with or without a screen, permanent screen, hashish head, or punctured metal bowl; 
(2)  Water pipes; 
(3)  Carburetion tubes or devices; 
(4)  Smoking or carburetion masks; 
(5)  Chamber pipes; 
(6)  Carburetor pipes; 
(7)  Electric pipes; 
(8)  Chillums; 
(9)  Bong; or 
(10)  Ice pipes or chillers. 
    Synthetic cannabinoids means substances listed in penalty group 2-A in V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 481.1031, and includes, without limitation: 
(1)  Products, by whatever trade name, that are treated, sprayed, or saturated with one or more of the chemicals lists in subsection (2) of this definition; and 
(2)  Any synthetic equivalent of the substance contained in the cannabis plant, or in the resinous extractives of the genus cannabis, or a synthetic substance, derivative, or its isomers with similar chemical structure or pharmacological activity such as: 
a.  Salvia divinorum or salvinorin A; all parts of the plant presently classified botanically as salvia divinorum, whether growing or not, the seeds thereof, any extract from any part of such plant, and every compound, manufacture, salts, derivative, mixture or preparation of such plant, its seeds or extracts; 
b.  2(1R,3S)-3-hydroxycyclohexyl-6, 6 dimethyl-3(2-methyloctan-2-yl)-6a, 7, 10, 10a-tetrahydrabenzocchromen-1-ol (also known as HU-211 or Dexanabinol); 
c.  1-pentyl-3(1-naphthoyl)indole; some trade or other names; (also known as JWH-018); 
d.  1-butyl-3-(1-naphthoyl)indole; some trade or other names; (also known as JWH-030); 
e.  1-pentyl-3-4(4-methoxynaphthoyl)indole (also known as JWH-081); 
f.  Phenol, CP 47, 497 and homologues, or 2- (1R,3S) hydroxycyclohexyl-5-(2-methyloctan-2-yl)phenol, where side chain n = 5, and homologues where side chain n = 4, 6 or 7; or 
g.  Any similar structural analogs. 
(Code 1973, § 14-61; Ord. No. 1977, § 1, 11-9-2010) 
Sec. 28-52. - Synthetic cannabinoids, illegal smoking products and paraphernalia prohibited. 
(a)  It is unlawful to use, purchase, sell, exchange, dispense, distribute, manufacture, or deliver synthetic cannabinoids, illegal smoking materials and illegal smoking material paraphernalia, and the possession of such materials in the city limited is prohibited. For purposes of this section, any form of delivery, including simple gift transfer, constitutes delivery and a violation of this section. 
(b)  It is unlawful for any person to use, possess, purchase, sell, offer to sell, give away, barter, exchange, dispense, deliver, distribute, or manufacture any synthetic cannabinoid or illegal smoking material to any person as defined in this article within the corporate limits of the city. 
(c)  It is unlawful for any owner or operator of any public building or business to sell, offer to sell, deliver to or to give any synthetic cannabinoid, illegal smoking material, or illegal smoking material paraphernalia to any person. 
(d)  It is unlawful for any person to have in his possession any illegal smoking paraphernalia with the intent to use it, to smoke, ingest, inhale or otherwise consume any synthetic cannabinoid or illegal smoking material. It is a violation of this section if a person is found in possession of illegal smoking paraphernalia and appropriate forensic testing is done on the paraphernalia showing traces of synthetic cannabinoid, or illegal smoking material are present on the illegal smoking paraphernalia. 
(Code 1973, § 14-62; Ord. No. 1977, § 1, 11-9-2010) 
Sec. 28-53. - Affirmative defenses to prosecution. 
    It is an affirmative defense to prosecution under this section that a synthetic cannabinoid, an illegal smoking product, or illegal smoking paraphernalia was: 
(1)  In the possession of a peace officer, or a person acting under the authority of a peace officer, acting in the performance of official duties. 
(2)  In the possession of or being used by a governmental entity for a health, research, education, or similar program. 
(3)  In the possession of or used by a person at the written direction or under a prescription issued by a licensed physician or dentist authorized to prescribe controlled substances within this state. 
(Code 1973, § 14-63; Ord. No. 1977, § 1, 11-9-2010) 
Secs. 28-54-28-79. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - MINORS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 28-80-28-101. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - CURFEW[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal authority to establish a juvenile curfew, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 341.905; requirement that juvenile curfew ordinances be reviewed and readopted every three years, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 370.002. 

Sec. 28-102. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Commercial establishment means any privately-owned place of business operated for a profit to which the public is invited, including, but not limited to, any place of amusement or entertainment. 
    Curfew hours mean: 
(1)  11:00 p.m. on any Sunday, Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday, or Thursday until 6:00 a.m. of that next day; 
(2)  12:01 a.m. until 6:00 a.m. on any Saturday or Sunday; and 
(3)  9:00 a.m. until 3:00 p.m. on any Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday, Thursday or Friday on days that the school in which the minor is enrolled is in session, unless the minor has school permission to be off-campus. 
    Direct route means the shortest path of travel through a public place to reach a final destination without any detour or stop along the way. 
    Emergency means, but is not limited to, a fire, a natural disaster, an automobile accident, or any situation requiring immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss of life. 
    Holding location means a place designated by the chief of police to whom a minor taken into custody for a violation of this section will be delivered to wait pickup by a parent or juvenile authorities. 
    Minor means any person under 17 years of age. 
    Parent means a person who is: 
(1)  A natural or adoptive parent of another person; 
(2)  A court-appointed guardian of another person; or 
(3)  At least 18 years of age and authorized by a parent or court-appointed guardian to have the care and custody of another person. 
    Public place means any street, alley, highway, sidewalk, plaza, building, or other place used by or open to the public, including, but not limited to, parking lots adjacent to commercial establishments. 
    Remain means to: 
(1)  Linger or stay unnecessarily; 
(2)  Walk, run, idle, wander, stroll, or aimlessly drive or ride about in or upon any public place; or 
(3)  Fail to leave premises when requested to do so by a police officer or the owner, operator, or other person in control of the premises. 
(Code 1973, § 14-21; Ord. No. 1578, § 1, 9-8-1992; Ord. No. 1929, § 3, 10-9-2007; Ord. No. 2116, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 28-103. - Offenses. 
    A minor commits an offense if he remains in any public place or on the premises of any establishment within the city during curfew hours. A parent of a minor commits an offense if he knowingly permits, or by insufficient control allows, a minor to remain in any public place or on the premises of any establishment within the city during curfew hours. 
(Code 1973, § 14-22; Ord. No. 1578, § 2, 9-8-1992; Ord. No. 2116, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 28-104. - Defenses. 
    It is a defense to prosecution under this division that the minor was: 
(1)  Accompanied by the minor's parent; 
(2)  On an errand at the direction of the minor's parent and was using a direct route; 
(3)  In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel; 
(4)  Engaged in a lawful employment activity, including, but not limited to, newspaper delivery, and was using a direct route; 
(5)  Involved in an emergency; 
(6)  On the sidewalk abutting the minor's residence or abutting the residence of a next-door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the police officer about the minor's presence; 
(7)  Attending an official school, civic or religious activity or returning home by a direct route from an official school, civic or religious activity; 
(8)  Exercising First Amendment rights protected by the federal constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech, and the right of assembly; 
(9)  Married or had been married or had disabilities of minority removed in accordance with state law; or 
(10)  Acting at the direction of a peace officer. 
(Code 1973, § 14-23; Ord. No. 1578, § 3, 9-8-1992; Ord. No. 2116, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 28-105. - Enforcement. 
(a)  A police officer, upon finding a minor in violation of this division, shall: 
(1)  Ascertain the name and address of the minor; 
(2)  Ascertain the name and address of the minor's parents; 
(3)  Issue to the minor a written warning that the minor is in violation of this division; 
(4)  Order the minor to go promptly home by a direct route; and 
(5)  Submit a copy of the warning to the city police department which shall send a letter by certified mail, return receipt requested, to the parent of the minor advising of the fact that the minor was found in violation of this article, soliciting cooperation in the future, and including a warning that any subsequent violation may result in prosecution of the minor or the parent under this section. 
(b)  A police officer, upon finding a minor in violation of this division, who has previously received a written warning for violating this article, shall: 
(1)  Ascertain the name and address of the minor; 
(2)  Ascertain the name and address of the minor's parents; 
(3)  Issue to the minor a municipal court misdemeanor citation; 
(4)  Order the minor to go promptly home by a direct route; and 
(5)  Submit a copy of the citation to the city police department which shall send a letter by certified mail, return receipt requested, to the parent of the minor advising of the fact that the minor was found in violation of this article on a second occasion and received a municipal court misdemeanor citation. 
(c)  Notwithstanding subsections (a) and (b) of this section, a police officer, upon finding a minor in violation of this division, may take the minor into custody and deliver the minor to a holding location if the minor has received both a written warning and a municipal court misdemeanor citation for a violation of this division or reasonable grounds exist to believe the minor has engaged in delinquent conduct or conduct indicating a need for supervision in accordance with V.T.C.A., Family Code § 51.03. 
(d)  When a minor is taken into custody under this section, the police department shall immediately notify a parent to pick up the minor at the holding location. After a parent arrives at a holding location and provides the information required by the chief of police to file an incident report, the minor shall be released into custody of the parent and the police officer may, in his discretion, issue to the parent a municipal court misdemeanor citation for a violation of this division. 
(Code 1973, § 14-24; Ord. No. 1578, § 4, 9-8-1992; Ord. No. 2116, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 28-106. - Penalties. 
    Any minor who violates this division three or more times within a 24-month period is subject to appropriate action by a juvenile court in accordance with V.T.C.A., Family Code chs. 51 and 52. A minor or a parent of a minor who violates this division is, upon conviction, punishable as provided in section 1-15. 
(Code 1973, § 14-25; Ord. No. 1578, § 5, 9-8-1992; Ord. No. 2116, 10-11-2016) 
Chapter 30 - OIL AND GAS WELLS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Injection wells, V.T.C.A., Water Code § 27.001 et seq.; plugging leaking wells, V.T.C.A., Natural Resources Code § 89.043; movement of oversize or overweight oil well servicing and drilling machinery, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 623.141 et seq.; oil and gas generally, V.T.C.A., Natural Resources Code § 81.001 et seq.; mines and mining, V.T.C.A., Natural Resources Code § 131.001 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - GENERAL 

Sec. 30-1. - Definitions. 
(a)  The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    A.P.I. means American Petroleum Institute. 
    Applicant means any person who applies for a permit under this chapter. 
    Drilling operation means the making of a hole in the earth for the purpose of discovery, exploration, or production of oil, gas, or minerals. 
    Operator means every person, and the agents, servants, and employees of the person, engaged in operations for the drilling, reworking, servicing, or plugging and abandonment of any well subject to the provisions of this chapter and the production or transportation of any product therefrom. 
    Permit means a permit granted pursuant to the provisions thereof. 
    Permittee means any person holding a permit granted under this chapter. 
    Well means any excavation or bore downward from the surface intended to extend 200 feet or more into the subsurface, made by any means or manner for the purpose of exploring for, discovering, producing, or injecting hydrocarbons or other mineral. 
(b)  All words used but not defined in this chapter that have accepted meanings in the oil and gas industry shall have the same meaning in this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art I, § 3, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-2. - Administrative enforcement authority. 
    Administrative enforcement of this chapter shall be by a city oil and gas inspector who shall be appointed by the city manager. It shall be the duty of the city oil and gas inspector to enforce the provisions hereof and to that end he is hereby vested with police authority. In the event there is no person filling an office at any time, the city manager shall fulfill the duties or designate some other city officer or employee to do so. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art V, § 1, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-3. - Effect of chapter on other property and drilling rights. 
    Neither this chapter nor any permit issued hereunder shall be interpreted as granting any right or license to the permittee to enter upon or use any land nor shall it limit or prevent the free right of the owners of the land to contract for any payment of any kind of damages or for rights or privileges with respect thereto. Nothing contained in this chapter shall be construed to authorize the drilling of any well where the operator has no legal authority to do so. No well shall be drilled at any location where there are of record valid and legally enforceable restrictions or covenants prohibiting the drilling of the well. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, § 8, 6-10-1980) 
Secs. 30-4-30-24. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DRILLING PERMITS 

Sec. 30-25. - Required. 
    It is unlawful for any person, acting either for himself or as agent, employee, independent contractor, or servant of another person, to commence to drill, or to operate any well or to assist in the drilling, completing or operating of any well for oil or gas within the city unless a permit for the well shall have been first obtained as provided in this article. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, § 1, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-26. - Application. 
(a)  Filing; content generally. An application for a drilling permit shall be filed in duplicate, with all required exhibits attached thereto, in the office of the city clerk for each well to be drilled. Such application shall be signed and the accuracy of the contents thereof shall be sworn to before a notary public by the applicant or some representative of the applicant having legal authority to enter into contracts binding upon the applicant, and shall include the following: 
(1)  Applicant's identifying information. Name and address of the applicant; and, if a corporation, the name and address of the person upon whom process may be served for the corporation; and, if a partnership, the names and addresses of all the general partners. 
(2)  Local agents. The name, address, and telephone number of a person, other than applicant, designated as local agent of the applicant to receive for the applicant all process, citation, notices, and demands hereunder. If appropriate, more than one telephone number shall be furnished. 
(3)  Proposed depth; budget. Proposed total depth of the well; proposed casing and cementing program of the well; and an itemized budget of the applicant's best estimate as to the costs of drilling the well and of completing and equipping the same if it is a producer. 
(4)  Railroad forms and permits. True copies of Railroad Commission Form No. 1 and railroad commission drilling permit, if issued. 
(5)  Drilling near airport notices. A copy of the notice to the federal aviation administration and city airport advisory board of intention to drill, if required. 
(6)  Insurance certificates. An insurance certificate dated not more than ten days prior to filing the application indicating that the applicant has complied with the minimum insurance requirements specified in this article. 
(7)  Bonds. All bonds required by this article. 
(8)  Filing fee. A filing fee in the amount provided in the city fee schedule in cash or bank money order or certified or cashier's check. 
(b)  Certified field notes. In addition, the application shall be accompanied by field notes certified by a licensed surveyor. If the application is for a permit to drill an oil well, the plant and field notes shall designate a 40-acre oil unit; if for a permit to drill a gas well, the plat and field notes shall designate a 320-acre gas unit. 
(c)  Certified plat. In addition, the application shall be accompanied by a plat certified by a licensed surveyor. The plat shall show the proposed surface location of the well, together with the distances from the location to the exterior boundary lines of the drilling block and to all residences, public or parochial schools, hospitals, churches, cemeteries, parks, and public buildings which are located within 400 feet of the surface well location and to all streets and alleys which are located within 50 feet of the surface well location. Such unit designation shall be in as nearly a square or parallelogram as is practicable, taking into consideration existing property lines, boundaries of previously designated oil or gas units, natural boundaries, and availability of surface drill sites. 
(d)  List of parties in interest and property owners. Each application shall be accompanied by a list of the names and last known addresses of all record owners of interests in and to oil, gas, and other minerals under the property located within the drilling block on which the proposed well is to be located. Such list shall specify the fractional share of operating rights within the block owned by each of the owners. The applicant shall indicate separately the percentage of total operating rights within the drilling block owned or controlled by applicant, including those rights acquired by contract from other operating interest owners. 
(e)  Copies of related leases and contracts. There shall be attached to the application photostatic or certified copies of all leases and contracts within the drilling unit which are controlled or owned by the applicant and of all requisite permissions from the owners of the surface and improvements thereon to the end that the application shall show what specified part of the unit the applicant holds under lease or contract with the owners, what specified part of the unit the applicant does not hold under lease or contract with the owners, and that he owns or controls the interest in the unit and the permission from the owners of the surface required by this article. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, § 2, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-27. - Required interest of applicant in unit. 
    No permit shall be granted under this article for the drilling and operation of any well unless the surface site of the well is owned by the applicant or held by the applicant under an oil and gas lease or a drilling contract from the owners of the site giving the owner's permission to drill a well thereon. No permit shall be granted unless the applicant owns or holds under oil and gas lease or drilling contract from the owners thereof at least 51 percent of the total operation rights in the unit. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, § 5, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-28. - Location restrictions. 
    No permit shall be issued under this article for the drilling of an oil and gas well, and no oil or gas well shall be drilled, in the city: 
(1)  Within or at any location nearer than 50 feet from any street, alley, or utility easement. 
(2)  Nearer than 400 feet from any residence or other permanent structure intended for human occupancy, unless the applicant furnishes with his application written waivers executed by all the owners and tenants of the residences and the structures that are located within 400 feet of the proposed. 
(3)  On or within 400 feet of any exterior boundary line of land used by any public or parochial school, hospital, church, or public building; provided, however, that the city council may grant a variance and allow the drilling of a well that does not meet these requirements if the applicant attaches to his application written evidence that the owners or governing bodies of the public or parochial school, hospital, church, or public buildings have consented and agreed in writing to the proposed well location. 
(4)  On or less than 400 feet from the exterior boundary line of lands utilized for cemetery or public park purposes. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, § 7, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-29. - Conflicting applications. 
    If the clerk receives and there is pending at the time of hearing applications by more than one applicant for permits to drill to the same reservoir on any single unit within the corporate limits of the city, the city council shall prefer the application, if otherwise sufficient, which is made by the applicant holding the greater percentage of the total operating rights in the unit be fee ownership, or lease or drilling contract from the fee owner of the rights. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, § 6, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-30. - Notices; hearing. 
(a)  Upon the filing of an application for a permit required by this article, the city clerk shall set a date for a hearing on the application, which date shall be not less than 20 days subsequent to the date of filing the application. 
(b)  Notice of the application and hearing shall be given by the applicant (on the form approved by the city council and available in the office of the city clerk) by certified mail to each owner and each lessee of any lot, block, or tract of land in the unit not owned by applicant or held by him under lease or contract from the owners thereof. The notices shall be addressed to the last known address of the owners and lessees and shall be mailed at least ten days prior to the date set for the hearing. Prior to the hearing, the applicant shall file an affidavit showing the date and the persons to whom and the addresses to which the notice was mailed by the applicant. 
(c)  A copy of the notice shall be posted by the city clerk on the bulletin board in the entrance hall of the city hall and at the Courthouses of DeWitt and Lavaca County, Texas, at least ten days prior to the date set for the hearing. 
(d)  The city clerk shall also cause a copy of the notice to be published at least twice in a newspaper of general circulation in the city, the first publication to be not less than ten days before the date set for hearing. Proof of publication of the notice shall be made by the printer or publisher of the newspaper publishing the same by affidavit filed with the city clerk and the affidavit shall be prima facie evidence of the publication. 
(e)  At the time fixed in the notice, a public hearing on the application shall be held and may be continued at the discretion of the city council from time to time as the council deems appropriate. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, §§ 3, 4, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-31. - Final decision of city council. 
(a)  Granting of application and issuance of permit. If, after the completion of the hearing, an application is found by the city council to comply in all respects with the terms of this article and that the drilling and operation of a well on the designated unit and at the designated site is not prohibited by the terms of this article or state law, the council shall issue a permit for the drilling and operation of the well. 
(b)  Denial of application. The city council shall refuse the application if it is not found by the city council to comply in all respects with the terms of this article. The city council may also refuse any application for a permit to drill and operate a well at a particular location where by reason of the particular location and the character and value of the permanent improvements already erected on or approximately adjacent to the proposed location and the use to which the land and surroundings are adapted for school, hospital, park, or civic purposes, or for health or safety reasons or any of them, the drilling or operation of a well at the particular location is reasonably calculated to be injurious and disadvantageous to the city and to its inhabitants as a whole or to a substantial number of its inhabitants. 
(c)  Issuance of permit subject to conditions. The city council may also elect to grant a permit on the conditions imposed by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, §§ 9, 10, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-32. - Bond required. 
(a)  No permit shall be issued until the permittee files with the city clerk a surety bond signed by the applicant as principal and by a good and sufficient corporate surety company in the amount of $1,000,000.00, conditioned that the principal shall: 
(1)  Comply with all the terms and conditions of this article in the drilling and operations of the well. 
(2)  Remedy and repair any and all damages to streets, curbs, gutters, sidewalks, water lines, fire hydrants, and other public property occasioned in any manner by the principal, his agents, employees, contractors and servants. 
(3)  Reimburse the city for all expenditures made by the city with regard to well control and relief wells as provided in this article. 
(4)  Promptly clear all premises of all litter, trash, waste, refuse, and other substances used, allowed, or occurring in the drilling and producing operations and will grade, level, and restore the property to the same surface condition as near as practicable as existed when operations were first commenced. 
(5)  Indemnify and hold the city harmless from any and all liability growing out of or attributable to the granting of the permit. 
(b)  The bond shall be payable to the city in a form acceptable to the city attorney. Each bond shall become effective on or before the date it is filed with the city clerk and shall remain in force and effect until the times prescribed in this article; provided, however, the surety on any bond shall have the right to cancel the same upon 30 days' notice to the city clerk, but the cancellation shall not affect any liability which may have arisen hereunder up to the time of the cancellation. Any cancellation shall automatically terminate the permittee's right to operate under the permit until such time as permittee shall furnish another bond as required in this chapter.
