(c)  The term "good and sufficient corporate surety company," as used in this section, means a surety company licensed to do business in this state whose name appears on the current list of accepted surety on federal bonds published by the federal government. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, §§ 12, 14, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-33. - Insurance required. 
    Each permittee shall maintain public liability insurance in a minimum amount of $1,000,000.00. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, § 13, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-34. - Termination of permit; return of bond. 
(a)  Permits issued under this article shall terminate and become inoperative without any action on the part of the city at the expiration of 180 days from the date of issuance, unless within that time actual operations for the drilling of a well shall have commenced. 
(b)  After operations shall have commenced, prior to the completion of a well, the cessation of drilling operations for a period of 90 days shall operate to terminate and cancel the permit and it is unlawful thereafter to continue the operation or drilling of the well without the issuance of another permit. 
(c)  If any permit shall terminate or if the permittee shall file with the city clerk written notice of his election to surrender the permit, then if no claims under the bond filed by the permittee are filed with the city clerk within 120 days thereafter, the city clerk shall return the bond furnished by the permittee. If any claims are filed within the time, then upon the satisfaction or final judicial denial of the claims, the bond shall be returned to the permittee or his assigns. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, § 11, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-35. - Reworking operations. 
    If a well shall be completed as a well capable of production and shall thereafter cease to be capable of production, the permittee shall have the right to conduct reworking operations within 90 days after it becomes incapable of production without having to procure a new permit. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art III, § 11, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-36. - Final report. 
    Within 30 days after completion of any well, the permittee shall file with the city clerk a final report including the casing program actually utilized in the well. The final report shall specify any changes in well location, depth, or any other variation from the terms of the application and shall specify the perforated interval and include information pertaining to other perforations, if any. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 14, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-37. - Special relief well permit. 
(a)  Drilling of a relief well may be commenced without first securing a permit if the action is deemed necessary in the good faith opinion of the operator. The operator shall make all reasonable efforts to notify the city oil and gas inspector by telephone as soon as feasible but failure to make the notification shall not be deemed a violation of this article. 
(b)  Within 24 hours after the commencement of operations for the drilling of the relief well, the operator drilling the same shall notify the city oil and gas inspector that the operations have been commenced, stating fully the reasons therefor, and shall within five days after the commencement of operations make application to the city for a special permit to drill the well as a relief well. No filing fee shall be required for a relief well permit but the operator drilling the relief well shall furnish the city any information with respect to the relief well as may be from time to time requested by the city council or the city oil and gas inspector. 
(c)  No well drilled as a relief well shall be completed as a producing well unless a permit therefor shall have been issued in the same manner as is required under this article for the drilling of any other well. 
(d)  A relief well permit will be for a six-month period only, and any relief well not completed as a producing well shall be plugged and abandoned within six months after commencement of drilling operations unless an extension is granted by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 16, 6-10-1980) 
Secs. 30-38-30-62. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - UNITIZATION 

Sec. 30-63. - Purpose. 
    To facilitate the orderly development of oil and gas production in the city and to avoid confiscation of property, all mineral interests in each unit for which a permit is granted shall be unitized as provided in this article. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art IV, § 1, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-64. - Well density restrictions. 
    No more than one completion shall be made in any reservoir on any unit until special field rules have been adopted by the railroad commission for the reservoir. The final well density within each unit shall be no greater than that prescribed by the railroad commission in special field rules which may be adopted for the field. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art IV, § 1, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-65. - Procedure. 
(a)  Not exclusive. The procedure provided in this section for the unitization of oil and gas interests is not intended to be an exclusive method for unitizing the interests. Voluntary unitization is authorized as a substitute for the procedures provided in this section. 
(b)  Options. In the event an application for permit for the drilling, completion, and operation of an oil or gas well is made by a person who does not own in fee or hold by lease or drilling contract from the owners all of the operating rights in the unit as to which the permit is granted, then all of the owners of the operating rights not held or controlled by the permittee shall be entitled to the following options: 
(1)  Mineral fee owners. A mineral fee owner of an oil and gas interest not covered by an existing oil and gas lease shall be entitled to participate as a royalty owner on the basis of one-sixth royalty interest in the property covered by his mineral fee. In addition the mineral fee owner shall be entitled to elect between the options available to the lessees in this section; however, if the mineral fee owner fails to elect between the options available to the lessee within 30 days after the giving of the notice provided for this section, he shall be conclusively presumed to have elected to participate as a royalty owner on the basis of a one-sixth royalty. If any mineral fee owner owns an interest in the oil and gas on, in, and under the land less than the entire fee simple oil and gas mineral estate, then the royalty participation of the mineral fee owner and his share of participation as an operating owner or as a carried owner under Options No. 1 or 2 below shall be reduced in the proportion that his interest bears to the whole and undivided fee and in accordance with the nature of the estate of which he is seized. 
(2)  Oil and gas lessees. An oil and gas lessee shall be entitled to elect between the following options: 
a.  Option No. 1. Lessee may elect within 30 days after the date of posting of the notice to participate in the drilling and production of the well as an active operating interest owner, in which event he shall pay his proportionate part of all drilling and operating costs and shall participate in production in proportion to his ownership in the production unit. If the owner elects to participate as an operation owner, he shall either post bond written by a good and sufficient corporate surety company or deposit cash with the permittee guaranteeing payment to the permittee of the operating interest owner's proportionate share on a surface acreage basis of the following amounts: The estimated monthly operating expenses. If the cost of drilling and completing the well exceeds the estimated cost, the owner shall forthwith on demand pay his proportionate share of the excess to the permittee or, if the actual costs are less than the estimate, the owner's proportionate share of the difference shall be refunded by permittee on demand. Such operating interest owner shall advance to applicant at monthly or other mutually acceptable intervals the owner's share of estimate expenses of operating the production unit, or at the election of the permittee, the owner's share of the operating expenses may be deducted by permittee as they accrue from the revenues from production which otherwise would be payable to the owner. 
b.  Option No. 2. Lessee may elect to become the owner of a carried interest. If lessee elects to be a carried interest owner, he shall not be entitled to receive any revenue from his interest in the drilling block until the time as the participating owners have received from the proceeds of production attributable to the carried interest owner's leasehold interest an amount equal to his proportionate part of the current operating expenses, the cost of purchasing and installing all pipeline, tank batteries, and other equipment installed by the participating owners to facilitate production of oil and gas from the drilling block, and an amount equal to the carried interest owner's proportionate share of the cost of drilling and completing the well within the unit. The interest of the carried interest owner shall be subject to its proportionate share of the unit in accordance with accepted accounting procedures. Any remaining income attributable to the carried interest shall be payable to the owner thereof monthly. If a lessee fails to elect to participate under one of the two options shown herein within 30 days after the date of notice given to him as hereinafter provided, then and in that event the lessee shall be presumed to have elected to participate as a carried interest owner under Option No. 2. 
(c)  Notice to owners. Notice to the owners (whose addresses are known or are ascertainable to use of ordinary diligence) of the oil and gas interests within the affected unit that are not owned or leased by the permittee, and that are not covered by voluntary unitization agreements, shall be given as follows: 
(1)  The permittee shall deliver or send by certified mail to all the owners at their last known address a written notice (in the form approved by the city council, a copy of which is available in the office of the city clerk). The notice shall include: 
a.  A legal description of the unit. 
b.  The type of interest held by the owner being notified (mineral fee, royalty, lessee, overriding royalty, etc.). 
c.  A statement of the options available to the owner being notified as set out in this section, if applicable. 
d.  Notification that if the owner fails to notify the applicant in writing within 30 days from the date of mailing or delivering the notice to the owner of the selection of one of the available options, the owner will be conclusively presumed to have elected to participate as a royalty owner in the case of a fee owner and as a carried interest owner in the case of a lessee. 
(2)  In addition to the individual notification, the applicant shall publish in two issues of a newspaper of general circulation in the city a notice in substantial compliance with the form approved by the city council and available in the office of the city clerk. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art IV, § 2, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-66. - Allocation of production; agreements for alternative allocation. 
(a)  Production from any unit shall be allocated to tracts that are unitized under the provisions of this article in the proportion that the number of surface square feet of each the individual tract has to the total surface square footage in the unit. Owners of interests under the tracts shall share in the production allocated to the individual tracts on the basis of their respective interests therein. Production from the unit in which the owner participates shall be treated as production from all of the tracts within the unit. 
(b)  The permittee and the owners of other mineral interests in any unit may alter the obligations set out in this article by agreement between them, provided that the agreement is not in conflict with the other provisions of this article. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art IV, § 3, 6-10-1980) 
Secs. 30-67-30-90. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - DRILLING AND OPERATIONAL STANDARDS AND SPECIFICATIONS 

Sec. 30-91. - Earthen and steel pits. 
    It is unlawful for any person to use in connection with any drilling or reworking operation within the city any earthen pit. All pits shall be portable steel pits which shall be removed from the city, with their contents, promptly upon the completion or abandonment of the well. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 1, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-92. - Crude oil storage and receiving tanks. 
    After any oil or gas well is brought into production, all crude oil storage or receiving tanks for the well must be located outside the city limits. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 2, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-93. - Derricks and rigs. 
    No operator shall use or operate in connection with the drilling or reworking of any well any wooden derrick or steam powered rig. Motive power for all drilling and other operations shall be diesel electric or gas or gasoline engines. All engines shall be equipped with effective mufflers. No steam-powered rig shall be permitted. No drilling rig or derrick shall be permitted to remain on the drilling site for a period of longer than 30 days after the completion or abandonment of the well. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 3, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-94. - Drilling fluid. 
    The bore holes of all wells while being drilled or reworked shall at all times contain drilling fluid of sufficient weight to exceed the formation pressure anticipated and of the weight and viscosity a reasonably prudent operator would use to keep the well under control. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 4, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-95. - Blow-out preventers. 
(a)  Two dual controlled, fluid operated blow-out preventers with working pressure rating equal to the maximum anticipated well-head pressure shall be used for all drilling or completion operations involving the use of drill pipe or tubing after the surface casing has been set. A hydril type blow-out preventer shall be used in addition to the two dual controlled blow-out preventers above specified. A choke manifold having the same working pressure rating as the preventers shall be installed below the blow-out preventer stack. 
(b)  The mechanical operation of the blow out preventers shall be checked a minimum of every 24 hours and pressure tested prior to installation on each casing string. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 5, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-96. - Drill stem tests. 
    No drill stem test shall be conducted except during daylight hours and then only if the well effluent during the test is produced through an adequate oil and gas separator to storage tanks and the effluent remaining in the drill pipe at the time the tool is closed is flushed to the surface by circulating drilling fluid down the annulus and up the drill pipe. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 6, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-97. - Surface casing. 
(a)  All operators shall be required to set and cement a sufficient amount of surface casing to protect properly all fresh water sands in accordance with the requirements of any governmental agency having jurisdiction. The surface casing shall, however, in no case be set to a depth of less than 1,150 feet. 
(b)  The surface casing shall be of new casing and shall be cemented by the pump and plug method. 
(c)  A volume of cement shall be used that, according to accepted engineering procedures, is calculated to fill the annular space between the surface casing and well bore to the surface of the ground and the cement shall be allowed to stand for a minimum period of 12 hours under pressure and for 24 hours before drilling plug or initiating test. 
(d)  After cementing, the surface casing shall be tested by pump pressure of at least 750 pounds per square inch. If at the end of 30 minutes the pressure shows a drop of 150 pounds per square inch or more, the casing shall be condemned. After corrective operations, the casing shall again be tested in the same manner. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 7, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-98. - Production and protection casing. 
    The producing or protection strings of casing shall be of new pipe meeting API specifications. Cementing shall be by the pump and plug method and a volume of cement which is, according to accepted engineering standards, sufficient to fill the annular space between the casing and the well bore to a point at least 600 feet above the shoe or the highest producing zone, whichever is the shallower depth. Cement shall be allowed to stand for a minimum period of 12 hours before drilling the plug. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 8, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-99. - Formation pressures. 
    No well shall be completed or operated in a zone which is reasonably anticipated to produce shut-in pressures in excess of the working pressure rating of the standard API wellhead equipment on the well. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 9, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-100. - Wellheads. 
    All wells drilled or completed in the city shall be equipped with casing heads, tubing heads, and wellhead connections conforming to API standards. The casing heads on the wells shall have working pressure ratings of not less than 3,000 pounds per square inch. Tubing heads and wellhead connections used on the wells shall have working pressure ratings in excess of the well's shut-in surface pressure. All the wells having a surface shut-in pressure of 3,000 pounds per square inch or less shall be equipped with at least one master valve and one wing valve. All wells having surface shut-in pressures in excess of 3,000 pounds per square inch shall be equipped with at least two master valves and one wing valve and no such well shall have threaded connections between the surface safety valve and the Christmas tree. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 10, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-101. - Multiple and tubingless completions. 
    Multiple completions and tubingless completions are permitted. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 11, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-102. - Surface safety valves. 
    A high-low surface safety valve shall be installed on all wells with a surface shut-in pressure in excess of 3,000 pounds per square inch. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 12, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-103. - Subsurface safety valves. 
    All flowing wells having shut-in well head pressure of 1,500 pounds per square inch or above or which are located within 50 feet of a public street shall be equipped with subsurface safety valve installed in the tubing or production string. The valve shall be pulled and inspected each year between April 1 and August 1 and more often if desired by the operator and a report of the inspection shall be filed with the city clerk. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 13, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-104. - Fences. 
    All wells and production facilities shall be adequately protected by a six-foot chainlink fence with a barbed wire guard at the top and a gate with heavy duty lock. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 18, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-105. - Pumping unit prime movers. 
    Only electric prime movers shall be permitted for the purpose of pumping wells. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 19, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-106. - Vented gas. 
    No operator shall allow gas to escape or be vented into the air except for bleed gas normally vented from standard gas operated controls and normal stock tank vapors. All gas burned shall be burned in a manner which does not create or constitute a fire hazard and the location of the torch, pipe, or other burning device, the construction thereof, the maintenance and operation thereof shall at all times be in compliance with the regulations as may be from time to time issued by the city fire department. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 20, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-107. - Salt water and waste disposal. 
    All salt water produced from any oil or gas well shall be disposed of outside the confines of the city limits. No person shall permit any crude oil, gas, or other petroleum product, salt water, mud, or other effluent to spill over, overflow, leak, drain out, escape or accumulate in or about the premises, on any surface, in any open surface ditch or other exposed surface conduit, or any sewer. No person shall handle any hydrocarbon in any manner or amount which creates a potential fire hazard or permit any condition which may pollute any surface or subsurface water or damage any publicly-owned land. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 21, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-108. - Electrical insulation and isolation. 
    All wells must be electrically isolated from all metallic piping and gathering systems unless the well and the piping are cathodically protected as a system. Electrical isolation of the wells shall be by the use of insulating sleeves and washers in flanges or insulating unions. The effectiveness of the insulating devices must be tested at least every six months and the results of the test reported to the city clerk. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 22, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-109. - Maintenance of premises and surface equipment. 
    All surface areas utilized by an operator for production facilities shall be kept clear of high grass, weeds, and combustible trash and other rubbish or debris; all surface equipment shall be maintained in good condition. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 23, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-110. - Fire hazard and well and operation identification signs. 
    Printed signs with at least two inch letters reading "danger, no smoking or open flames allowed," or similar words shall be posted in conspicuous places on each well and production facility. The signs shall include the drilling block number and the emergency telephone number of the fire department. Well and lease designations required by the railroad commission or any other governmental authority having jurisdiction shall also be displayed. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 23, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-111. - Blocking of streets and alleys. 
    Except when necessary to protect life or property in connection with emergency operations, no street or alley shall be blocked or obstructed by any drilling or producing operations unless prior consent for the blockage is obtained in the form of a resolution by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 24, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-112. - Electrical storms and hurricanes. 
    No well shall be permitted to produce at any time during an electrical storm or hurricane. All drilling and reworking operations shall be shut down during any hurricane and drill pipe shall be either laid down or left in the well bore and drilling and workover masts shall be laid down. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 25, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-113. - Pipelines. 
    Excavation for and installation of pipeline to move oil and gas from any well site across city rights-of-way should be as provided in section 40-1. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 17, 6-10-1980) 
Sec. 30-114. - Loss of control of well. 
(a)  In the event of the loss of control of any well, the operator shall immediately take all reasonable steps to regain control of the well, regardless of any other provisions of this article, and shall notify the city oil and gas inspector as soon as practicable after receipt of notice by the operator of the occurrence of the loss of well control endangering persons or property. 
(b)  If the city oil and gas inspector certifies in writing to the city clerk that, in his opinion, danger to persons or property exists because of the loss or well control (briefly describing the same) and the operator is not taking or is unable to take all reasonably necessary steps to regain control of the well, the city oil and gas inspector may employ any well control experts or other contractors or suppliers of special services or may incur any other expenses for labor or material that the city oil and gas inspector deems necessary to regain control of the well. 
(c)  The city shall have a valid lien against the interest owners in the well to secure the payment of any expenditures made by the city pursuant to any the action in regaining control of the well. However, the lien shall attach to the interest in the well of those persons who have been presumed to have elected to participate as carried interest owners under this article. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 15, 6-10-1980) 
Chapter 32 - PARKS AND RECREATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal parks and other recreational and cultural resources generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 306.001 et seq.; municipal authority to acquire and maintain parks, museums, and historic sites, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 331.001 et seq.; public use of municipal recreational facilities, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 331.007; municipal parks outside municipal limits, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 315.001; municipal recreational programs and facilities, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 332.001 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 32-1. - Scope; purpose. 
    This chapter shall apply to all public parks and recreational facilities within the corporate limits of the city, for the purpose of regulating and maintaining recreational facilities conducive to the good health and well-being of the community, and also for the purpose of encouraging the future civic and cultural development of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 15-31; Ord. No. 1431, 6-10-1986) 
Secs. 32-2-32-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PARKS AND RECREATION BOARD 

Sec. 32-21. - Appointment of members; terms. 
    The city council shall appoint seven members to serve on the parks and recreation board for such terms as may be designated by the board. 
(Code 1973, § 15-32; Ord. No. 1431, 6-10-1986) 
Sec. 32-22. - Jurisdiction; powers and duties. 
(a)  The parks and recreation board is given jurisdiction to provide policy leadership to the operation of city-maintained recreational projects of the city, including all parks and any recreational facilities such as municipal golf course, swimming pool, ball fields, rodeo, tennis courts and playgrounds equipment. 
(b)  The parks and recreation board is empowered to promulgate rules and regulations for operation of programs of the parks and recreation departments as well as recommend fees to be charged. 
(c)  The board shall encourage use of parks and recreational facilities of the city by its citizens as well as recommend capital improvements to be made. 
(Code 1973, § 15-33; Ord. No. 1431, 6-10-1986) 
Sec. 32-23. - Hours. 
    The public parks of the city shall close at 11:00 p.m., and it is unlawful for any persons to be in the park area after 11:00 p.m. and before 6:00 a.m., unless such persons have been granted a permit for use within those hours. 
(Code 1973, § 15-34; Ord. No. 1431, 6-10-1986) 
Sec. 32-24. - Permits. 
(a)  Permit required, exception, conditions. Any persons desiring to use any city park or park facilities between the hours of 11:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m. shall make written application to the parks superintendent for a permit to use such facilities after hours, which application shall contain such information as the parks superintendent may reasonably require. The parks superintendent may grant such permit upon the determination that use by the applicant of the park for the hours requested in such application will not result in loud or excessive noise or disorders, a requirement for additional police protection, and interference with the rights of adjoining property owners, or any condition detrimental to the orderly administration of the affairs of the city. The parks superintendent may choose to have the parks and recreation board make a final determination on the application. 
(b)  Fees. The parks and recreation board may establish such fees for the granting of a permit as may be reasonably necessary to defray expenses incident to issuing such permit. Such fees shall be included in the city fee schedule. 
(c)  Revocation. Any permit granted by the parks superintendent or parks and recreation board may be reviewed by the parks and recreation board at any time, and may be revoked if such use creates any of the conditions outlined above or if such use is contrary to the purposes set forth in the application. 
(Code 1973, § 15-35; Ord. No. 1431, 6-10-1986) 
Secs. 32-25-32-51. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PARK REGULATIONS 

Sec. 32-52. - Glass beverage containers in city parks. 
    It is unlawful to possess glass beverage containers within any city park unless the beverages are served by an authorized concession operator at events authorized by the director of community services and the beverage is served into non-glass containers with the glass dispensing containers being disposed of by the concession operator in approved garbage receptacles. The following types of glass containers are permitted within the city parks: 
(1)  Glass-lined vacuum bottles and glass-lined picnic beverage coolers; 
(2)  Baby bottles or baby food jars containing products for consumption by a baby; 
(3)  Glass bottles containing over the counter or prescribed drugs; 
(4)  Glass containers made for the containment and serving of food; and 
(5)  Any other such similar glass containers as listed above. 
(Code 1973, § 15-3; Ord. No. 1711, §§ 1-3, 12-9-1997) 
Chapter 34 - PERSONNEL 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 34-1-34-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TEXAS MUNICIPAL RETIREMENT SYSTEM[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- In this article, the term "board of commissioners" has been retained for historical accuracy as the governing body when the Texas Municipal Retirement System was adopted. The city's current governing body is the city council. 

Sec. 34-31. - Standard benefits; determination to participate; effective date. 
    On behalf of the city, the board of commissioners exercises its option and elects to have the city and all of the employees of all departments participate in the Texas Municipal Retirement System as provided in Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. art. 6243h; and all of the benefits and obligations of such system are accepted, effective August 1, 1951. 
(Code 1973, § 16-1; Ord. No. 598, § 1, 7-5-1951) 
Sec. 34-32. - Notice of participating departments. 
    The city manager is directed to notify the board of trustees of the Texas Municipal Retirement System that the city has elected to participate and have the employees of the following city departments participate in such system: administrative department, street department, sanitary department, police department, park department, fire department and utility department. This section pertains only to those employees who are regular full-time employees of the departments declared as participating above. 
(Code 1973, § 16-2; Ord. No. 598, § 2, 7-5-1951) 
Sec. 34-33. - Participation by new employees. 
    Each person who becomes an employee of any participating department on or after the effective date of participation of such department shall be included within and subject to the provisions of the Texas Municipal Retirement System beginning on the date such person becomes an employee as defined in subsection 14, section 2 of such system. 
(Code 1973, § 16-3; Ord. No. 598, § 3, 7-5-1951) 
Sec. 34-34. - Refusal to add new departments. 
    The city may in the future refuse to add new departments or new employees to such system but shall never discontinue as to any participants. 
(Code 1973, § 16-4; Ord. No. 598, § 4, 7-5-1951) 
Sec. 34-35. - Remitting to trustees; calculations; reports. 
(a)  The city clerk is directed to remit to the board of trustees of the Texas Municipal Retirement System, at its office in Austin, Texas, the city's proper contributions to the system and the amounts which shall be deducted from the compensation or payroll of employees, all as required by the board under the provisions of Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. art. 6243h. The city clerk is authorized and directed to ascertain and certify officially on behalf of the city the prior service rendered to the city by each of the employees of the participating departments and the average prior service compensation received by each, and to make and execute all other reports and certificates which may be required by the city under the provisions of the act or the rules and regulations of the board of trustees of the Texas Municipal Retirement System. 
(b)  The city clerk is directed to remit monthly to the board of trustees of the Texas Municipal Retirement System at its office in Austin, Texas, as the city's contributions to the supplemental benefits fund of such system, the percentage of earnings of the participating employees of the city as may be fixed by the board of trustees of the Texas Municipal Retirement System; provided that the rate of contribution to the fund shall not exceed one-half of one percent of the earnings of the employees of the city who are covered under the fund; and such official shall make for the city such reports as the board of trustees of the Texas Municipal Retirement System may prescribe. 
(Code 1973, §§ 16-5, 16-9; Ord. No. 598, § 5, 7-5-1951; Ord. No. 763, § 4, 10-8-1959) 
Sec. 34-36. - Texas Municipal Retirement System, supplemental benefits; determination to participate. 
    The city, by its board of commissioners, elects to have the employees of all participating departments of the city participate in and be covered by the supplemental benefits fund of the Texas Municipal Retirement System, as provided by Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. art. 6243h; and all the benefits and obligations of participation in the fund are accepted by the city as to such employees. 
(Code 1973, § 16-6; Ord. No. 763, § 1, 10-8-1959) 
Chapter 36 - SIGNS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Regulation of signs by municipalities generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 216.001 et seq.; authority for municipal regulation of signs, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 216.901; regulation of political signs by municipality, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 216.903; municipal boards on sign control, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 216.004; regulation of outdoor advertising generally, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 391.031 et seq.; licenses and permits for outdoor advertising, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 391.061 et seq.; municipal authority to regulate sign placement, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 393.0025. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 36-1. - Temporary signs for public events. 
(a)  The city manager is authorized to permit temporary installation or placing of banners and signs on or over any public rights-of-way. Such installation shall only be permitted for a public celebration or event considered to be in the best interest of the general public, and shall be subject to all appropriate local and state permits. 
(b)  Installation of banner or other signs on city utility poles will be performed only by authorized city personnel. Such installations shall be subject to fees as set from time to time by the city council in the city fee schedule. The city may provide this service for the Yoakum Area Chamber of Commerce and the Yoakum Heritage Museum at no cost. 
(Code 1973, § 5-7; Ord. No. 619, § 5, 2-5-1953; Ord. No. 1997, § 1, 1-10-2012) 
Sec. 36-2. - Definitions. 
    In this chapter: 
    "On-premises sign" means a freestanding sign identifying or advertising a business, person, or activity, and installed and maintained on the same premises as the business, person, or activity. 
    "Off-premises sign" means a sign displaying advertising that pertains to a business, person, organization, activity, event, place, service, or product not principally located or primarily manufactured or sold on the premises on which the sign is located. 
(Ord. No. 2118, § 1, 12-13-2016) 
Sec. 36-3. - Off-premises signs. 
    This section applies to all off-premises signs placed within the City of Yoakum. This section does not apply to directional signs, on-premises signs, or official signs that are exempted from the application of V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 391.031. 
(1)  Off-premises sign placement. Off-premises sign placement is restricted to property directly adjacent to a state highway, and zoned as commercial - C2 or Industrial - I, or an un-zoned property used for commercial or industrial purposes under the City of Yoakum's Zoning Ordinance. 
a.  A permitted sign may not be erected within five feet of any property line or highway right-of-way line. The distance shall be measured from the end of the sign face nearest the property line. 
b.  A permitted sign may not be erected within ten feet of a power line. 
c.  Sign must be placed on a lot, platted to meet the minimum lot requirement of the city. 
d.  Permitted signs may not be erected closer than 300 of a property used for residential purposes. 
e.  Permitted signs on the same side of a highway outside the incorporated boundaries of a municipality, may not be erected closer than 750 feet apart. 
f.  Permitted signs on the same side of a highway and within the incorporated boundaries of a municipality may not be erected closer than 750 feet apart. 
g.  For the purposes of this section, the space between signs is measured between points along the right-of-way of the highway perpendicular to the center of the signs. 
h.  No other sign, on-premises or off-premises, shall exist on the same property. 
(2)  Off-premises sign size. A sign face may not exceed 336 square feet in area, 14 feet in height; and 24 feet in length. A sign, including its support system, may not exceed an overall height of 28 feet. 
a.  For the purposes of this section, border and trim are included as part of the sign face. 
b.  The base, apron, supports, and other structural members, are excluded as part of the sign face. 
c.  A sign may have two or more sign faces that are placed back-to-back, or in "V" type construction with not more than one sign face presented in each direction. If such an arrangement is used, the sign structure or structures are considered to be one sign for all purposes. 
d.  A sign may not have a moveable protrusion. 
e.  For the purposes of this section, height is measured from the centerline of the main-traveled way closest to the sign face, at a point perpendicular to the sign location. 
f.  In the event that the main-traveled way that is perpendicular to the sign structure is below grade, sign height will be measured from the base of the sign structure. 
g.  The height measurement does not include any renewable energy device such as solar panels or wind turbines that are attached to the sign structure above the sign face to improve the energy efficiency of the sign structure. 
(Ord. No. 2118, § 2, 12-13-2016) 
Secs. 36-4-36-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DESIGN, CONSTRUCTION AND LOCATION SPECIFICATIONS 

Sec. 36-21. - Signs on or over public space. 
    No billboard or sign shall be erected in or project over any street, alley or public space except as otherwise specifically permitted by this article. 
(Code 1973, § 5-3; Ord. No. 619, § 1, 2-5-1953; Ord. No. 1997, § 1, 1-10-2012) 
Sec. 36-22. - Distance from residence, obstructing light, creating hazard. 
    No billboard or sign shall be erected or installed within 50 feet of the boundaries of any premises used for residence, nor so placed as to obstruct the lighting of any street, alley or public space, nor to interfere with any public utility service, nor to create a traffic hazard by obstructing the view. 
(Code 1973, § 5-4; Ord. No. 619, § 2, 2-5-1953) 
Sec. 36-23. - Setbacks. 
    In areas where billboards and signs are permitted, none shall be erected or installed within six feet of any building, nor within six feet of the sideline of any lot, nor closer than 15 feet of any street line. 
(Code 1973, § 5-5; Ord. No. 619, § 3, 2-5-1953) 
Sec. 36-24. - Wood construction. 
    No billboard or sign framed with or constructed of wood or other combustible material shall be erected in the fire limits or within 50 feet of any frame building; provided, however, that the use of wood posts as means of support of such billboard or sign is permitted. 
(Code 1973, § 5-6; Ord. No. 619, § 4, 2-5-1953) 
Sec. 36-25. - Size. 
    If a business is lawfully pursued on premises either in the business or residential areas, signs limited to ten square feet in area may be used pertinent to such business, even when such sign is within 50 feet of the boundary of other residence premises. 
(Code 1973, § 5-8; Ord. No. 619, § 6, 2-5-1953) 
Chapter 38 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal powers relating to public health, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 122.006; minimum standards of sanitation and health protection measures, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 341.001 et seq.; local regulation of sanitation, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.001 et seq.; Solid Waste Disposal Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 361.001 et seq.; Solid Waste Resource Recovery Financing Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 362.001 et seq.; Comprehensive Municipal Solid Waste Management, Resource Recovery, and Conservation Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 363.001 et seq.; Texas Litter Abatement Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 365.001 et seq.; environmental quality, 30 Tex. Admin. Code; waste minimization and recycling, 30 Tex. Admin. Code ch. 328; municipal solid waste, 30 Tex. Admin. Code ch. 330; composting and mulching, 30 Tex. Admin. Code ch. 32. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 38-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Dry kitchen refuse means the solids remaining after liquid or slop has been drained off. 
    Kitchen garbage means dry kitchen refuse, all meat, vegetable and fruit refuse, small dead animals and dead fowls. 
    Premises means all business and residential premises, vacant lots and all other places within the city where garbage, trash or rubbish accumulates. 
    Rubbish means tin cans, bottles, glass, scraps of iron, tin, wire or any other metals. 
    Trash means paper of all kinds, rags, old clothing, paper containers, old rubber, pieces of wood, boxes, barrels, crates, feathers, weeds, grass and tree limbs and other disposable and disposed of materials. 
(Code 1973, § 10-1; Ord. No. 470, § 1, 7-5-1946) 
Secs. 38-2-38-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - COLLECTION 

Sec. 38-21. - Containers. 
(a)  Portable garbage containers. It shall be the duty of every person, firm or corporation that is a bona fide customer of the hand pickup solid waste collection services of the city to utilize the portable garbage containers provided by the city. 
(b)  Placement of containers of trash, rubbish, etc. Containers of trash, rubbish, tree limbs and leaves shall be placed inside the curbline of the street. 
(c)  Placement of dumpsters. Mechanized containers must be placed in locations approved by the sanitation department of the city. 
(d)  Maintenance. All receptacles shall be kept in a sanitary condition and tightly closed. 
(Code 1973, §§ 10-2-10-4; Ord. No. 470, §§ 12, 13, 7-5-1946; Ord. No. 1501, § I, 1-10-1989) 
Sec. 38-22. - Wholesale accumulations. 
    The places of wholesale accumulations, such as killing and dressing plants for fowls, wholesale fruit and vegetable houses and storage and other places where the daily accumulation of kitchen garbage, trash and rubbish is more than the ordinary quantities, are not included in the service furnished by the city garbage department and such places are required to remove such accumulations at their own expense in the manner and by the method directed by the city. 
(Code 1973, § 10-5; Ord. No. 470, § 3, 7-5-1946) 
Sec. 38-23. - Heavy accumulations. 
    Heavy accumulations, such as bricks, broken concrete, ashes, clinkers, cinders, dirt and plaster, sand or gravel, automobile frames, trees and other bulky, heavy material, shall be disposed of at the expense of the owner or person controlling such accumulations under the direction of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 10-7; Ord. No. 470, § 5, 7-5-1946) 
Sec. 38-24. - Manure and waste oil. 
    Manure from cow lots, horse stables, poultry yards and pigeon lofts, and waste oils from garages or filling stations, shall be disposed of at the expense of the party responsible for same, under the direction of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 10-8; Ord. No. 470, § 6, 7-5-1946) 
Sec. 38-25. - Unauthorized use of containers and collection prohibited. 
    It is unlawful for any person that is not a bona fide customer of city sold waste collection services to: 
(1)  Place any garbage, trash, rubbish, dead animals or other types of solid waste into a commercial container or dumpster, or to otherwise interfere with or pilfer therefrom. 
(2)  Place refuse, trash, rubbish or other solid waste at any locations in any street or alley within the city. 
(3)  Place kitchen garbage, trash, rubbish or any article, thing or material in any street or alley within the city, except as permitted in this chapter. 
(4)  Collect garbage, trash and rubbish or of any kind of junk within the city unless authorized to do so by the provisions of this chapter or otherwise by the city council. 
(Code 1973, §§ 10-9, 10-11; Ord. No. 470, § 11, 7-5-1946; Ord. No. 1501, § I, 1-10-1989) 
Sec. 38-26. - Disposal at transfer station. 
    The disposal of any kind of rubbish in any place within the city is prohibited except at the City of Yoakum transfer station. 
(Code 1973, § 10-10; Ord. No. 470, § 8, 7-5-1946) 
Sec. 38-27. - Collection fees; billing; delinquency. 
    Persons utilizing city water, electric power and sewer inside the city limits automatically become customers of the sanitation department of the city and liable for payment of charges for garbage collection service. Solid waste collection service fees are as provided in the city manual of fees and service charges and billed monthly with charges for water, electric power and sewer service. All charges in the billing become delinquent on the same date. 
(Code 1973, §§ 10-12, 10-13.1; Ord. No. 470, § 15, 7-5-1946; Ord. No. 601, 11-7-1951; Res. No. 1045, 9-12-1972; Ord. No. 1252, § 1, 10-2-1979; Ord. No. 1296, § 1, 7-14-1981; Ord. No. 1359, § 1, 7-12-1983; Ord. No. 1378, § 1, 7-11-1984; Ord. No. 1408, 8-13-1985; Ord. No. 1435, 7-8-1986; Ord. No. 1583, § 4, 10-13-1992) 
Chapter 40 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- General authority of home rule municipalities concerning highways, streets and alleys, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 311.001; general authority of home rule municipality regarding sidewalks, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 311.004; use of municipal streets and sidewalks for public convenience and amenities, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 316.001 et seq.; municipal streets generally, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 312.001 et seq.; drainage on public roads, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 254.001 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 40-1. - Pipeline excavations. 
(a)  Before any excavation or construction work is commenced on any pipeline to move oil, gas, water, or other product to or from any well site on, over, under, along, or across any city street, sidewalk, alley, or other city property, the operator proposing to construct the pipeline shall file with the city clerk a plat showing the proposed location and size of the pipeline. 
(b)  Upon the payment to the city of the sum specified in the city fee schedule for each foot of pipeline proposed to be laid on, over, under, along, or across any city street, sidewalk, alley, or other city property, the operator shall be granted an easement to construct the pipeline. Such easement shall remain in effect so long as production or operations may be continued under any permit issued pursuant to this chapter. 
(c)  No operator shall interfere with or damage any existing storm sewer, drainage facility, water line, sewer line, gas line or facility of any public utility located on, under, or across, the course of any the pipeline. 
(d)  All crossings for pipelines under paved or black-topped streets, alleys, or sidewalks, shall be bored or jacked. 
(e)  All pipelines shall be buried beneath the surface of the streets, alleys, and sidewalks to such depth as shall be safe for the pressure carried. 
(f)  The operator shall, at his own expense, at all times restore and repair any injury or damage to the streets, sidewalks, and alleys caused by laying or removing or repairing the pipeline. 
(Ord. No. 1266, art II, § 17, 6-10-1980) 
Secs. 40-2-40-19. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - STREETS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 40-20. - Modifications to existing streets. 
(a)  Applicability. All modifications to existing streets and sidewalks in the city shall conform to all existing features, dimensions, and construction as approved by the city manager or as follows: 
(1)  Sixty-foot wide streets. All streets that are 60 feet in width shall have the roadway thereof reduced to a minimum width of 34 feet, leaving a space of 13 feet on either side of the roadway between the curbline and the property line to be divided and arranged as follows: 
a.  There shall be a space of one foot left between the property line and the sidewalk or walkway; 
b.  There shall be a space four feet in width on which to construct a sidewalk; 
c.  There shall be a space eight feet in width extending to the curbline and roadway, to be called a parkway, and such parkway shall be subject to the use of the abutting property owner for the purpose of more effectually beautifying his property. 
(2)  Fifty-foot wide streets. All streets that are 50 feet shall have a roadway of 28 feet in width in the center thereof, a parkway on either side six feet in width, a space for a sidewalk four feet in width on either side and a space of one foot in width between the sidewalk and property line, all to be similarly arranged and devoted to the same purposes as mentioned in subsection (a)(1) of this section. 
(3)  Forty-foot wide streets. All streets that are 40 feet in width shall have a roadway in the center thereof 24 feet in width, a parkway on either side three feet in width, with four feet of space for sidewalk construction, and one foot of space between the sidewalk and property line, thus placing the curbline on such streets eight feet from the property line. 
(4)  Streets less than 40 feet wide. All streets that have a width of less than 40 feet, the entire street shall be left as a roadway and there shall be no parkways on the sides of such streets, but all sidewalks shall be four feet in width and a space of one foot shall be left between the four-foot sidewalk and the property line. 
(b)  All sidewalks constructed along any of the streets mentioned in this section shall be four feet in width and constructed on the established grade furnished by the city engineer. 
(Code 1973, § 18-5; Ord. No. 1071, § 1, 3-3-1913) 
Sec. 40-21. - Obstruction prohibited; notice and removal. 
(a)  Upon a finding by the city council that there is an obstruction, encroachment or encumbrance of any public street, alley or ground, the city manager is authorized to notify, by certified mail, the party causing such obstruction, encroachment or encumbrance that unless same is removed within ten days, that the city will have same removed. 
(b)  If the party responsible for the obstruction, encroachment or encumbrance of any public street, alley or ground has not removed same within ten days, city employees under the direction of the city manager shall remove any such obstruction, encroachment or encumbrance. 
(c)  The cost of removal of any obstruction, encroachment or encumbrance shall be a personal charge against the party causing same, payable to the city after such removal. 
(Code 1973, § 18-8; Ord. No. 1143, §§ 1-3, 8-12-1975) 
Secs. 40-22-40-45. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - MOVING HEAVY OBJECTS 

Sec. 40-46. - Moving heavy objects; injury to pavement prohibited. 
    No heavy object that would endanger the surface of any street in the city shall be moved over, upon or across any such street. Heavy objects include buildings, houses, structures and portions thereof, motor vehicles equipped with pneumatic tires, ordinary farm wagons and buggies. 
(Code 1973, § 18-1; Ord. No. 314, §§ 1, 2, 8-5-1937) 
Sec. 40-47. - Permit, conditions. 
    When a necessity arises for the moving of any such heavy object over, upon or across a city street as is hereinabove prohibited, upon application made to the city manager showing such necessity, giving the name of the owner of such object, the location of same at the time of application and the destination, and accompanied by a fee as set from time to time by the council in the manual of fees and service charges of the city, and such other bond as is necessary to protect the city from loss or damage on account of injury to city streets, the amount and sufficiency of such other bond to be determined by the city manager, the city manager shall permit the moving of such object over, upon or across city streets, the moving to be done at such hours and along such route as the city manager shall specify. The proposed method of moving such object shall be subject to the approval of the city manager. 
(Code 1973, § 18-2; Ord. No. 314, § 3, 8-5-1937) 
Sec. 40-48. - Moving city wires. 
    In the event any electric line of the municipal utilities needs to be raised, moved, or handled in any manner during the moving of such object and to facilitate such moving, a fee shall be charged as set from time to time by the council in the city fee schedule for equipment charges. The cost of any material necessary to be used in such moving of wires shall be paid by the mover. The charges provided for in this section shall be made jointly and severally against the owner of the object and the contractor moving the object, and shall be covered and guaranteed by the bonds the same as damages. Damage or injury to any city property, including municipal utility property, shall be covered by the bonds. 
(Code 1973, § 18-3; Ord. No. 314, § 4, 8-5-1937; Ord. No. 1964, 12-8-2009) 
Secs. 40-49-40-69. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - STRUCTURAL AND VEGETATIVE INTRUSIONS 

Sec. 40-70. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Curbline means the boundary of that portion of any street which is improved, designed or ordinarily used for vehicular traffic. 
    Plant means any hedge, bush, shrub, vine, palm or other vegetation, except trees. 
    Street means the entire width of every way or place of whatever nature when any part thereof is open to the use of the public as a matter of right for purposes of traffic. 
    Traffic means pedestrians, riders of animals, and drivers of vehicles while using any street for purposes of travel. 
    Vehicle means every device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a street, except devices moved by human power. 
(Code 1973, § 18-20; Ord. No. 719, § 1, 11-6-1957) 
Sec. 40-71. - Visibility at residential district intersections. 
(a)  Obstructions prohibited. On a corner lot in any residential district nothing should be erected, placed, planted or allowed to grow in such a manner as to materially impair vehicle drivers' vision at intersections. 
(b)  Fences, walls and hedges. Notwithstanding other provisions of this section, fences, walls and hedges may be permitted in any required yard, or along the edge of any yard, provided that such fences, walls or hedges along lot lines at street intersections do not impair visibility at the intersection within an area defined by lines of joining points located 20 feet back from the intersection of all curblines extended, 
(Code 1973, § 18-23; Ord. No. 719, § 2(b), 11-6-1957; Ord. No. 1184, 4-12-1977) 
Sec. 40-72. - Maximum plant, fence, wall and structure height in and near corner triangles. 
(a)  It is unlawful for any person to place or cause to be placed any plant having a height of greater than three feet above the level of the center of the nearest abutting street, on or in any portion of any corner lot in the city, which portion is included in a triangle on the street corner of the lot formed by a diagonal line intersecting the property lines at points 20 feet from the street corner intersection of the property lines. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to construct or replace, or cause to be constructed or replaced, on the portion of a corner lot described in section (a) any non-opaque fence, wall, or other structure having a height greater than three feet above the level of the center of the nearest abutting street. 
(c)  It is unlawful for either the owner or the occupant of any corner lot in the city to place, maintain or permit or cause to be placed or maintained, any plant having a height greater than three feet above the level of the center of the nearest abutting street or in that area which lies between the property line of such corner lot and the curblines of streets abutting such property lines and which area extends for a distance of 50 feet back from the intersection of the curblines of such abutting streets. 
(d)  The invalidity of any section or provision of this section shall not invalidate other sections or provisions thereof. 
(Code 1973, §§ 18-21, 18-22; Ord. No. 719, §§ 2(a), 3(a), 11-6-1957; Ord. No. 2084, § I, 4-14-2015) 
Sec. 40-73. - Tree or other plant between property line and curbline. 
    It is unlawful for either the owner or the occupant of any lot in the city to place, maintain or permit, or cause to be placed or maintained, any tree or other plant on or in the area between the property line thereof and the curbline of any street abutting such property line in such a way as to obstruct the free passage on and use of that area by the public. 
(Code 1973, § 18-24; Ord. No. 719, § 3(b), 11-6-1957) 
Sec. 40-74. - Tree or other plant near fire hydrant. 
    It is unlawful for either the owner or occupant of any property in the city to place, maintain or permit, or cause to be placed or maintained thereon, any tree or other plant within five feet of any fire hydrant in the city. 
(Code 1973, § 18-25; Ord. No. 719, § 3(c), 11-6-1957) 
Sec. 40-75. - Minimum vegetation height above street; pruning required. 
    It is unlawful for the owner or occupant of any property in the city to maintain or permit limbs of trees growing thereon to overhang or grow above the area between the property line and the curbline of any abutting street, unless such limbs and all branches and foliage thereon are kept trimmed and pruned to a minimum of eight feet above the street level at the nearest curbline. 
(Code 1973, § 18-26; Ord. No. 719, § 3(d), 11-6-1957) 
Sec. 40-76. - Enforcement. 
(a)  Authority of city inspector to identify visibility obstructions. Obstruction of visibility at an intersection and other violations of this division shall be determined by the city inspector. 
(b)  Appeal of inspector's determination. Any person who does not agree with the decision of the city inspector shall have an appeal to the zoning board of adjustments and appeals. If the board determines that there is no obstruction of visibility or other violation, the person shall not be required to remove any fences, walls, or hedges or remove or trim vegetation as required in this division. If the board determines that there is an obstruction, the party shall be considered in violation of this section and subject to charges being filed in municipal court unless the object is immediately removed. 
(c)  Duty of chief of police to serve notice of violation. It shall be the duty of the chief of police to cause a written notice to be served upon the owner or occupant of any property upon which there exists a violation of this division. The notice shall advise the owner or occupant of the nature of the violation and that the violation must be corrected within ten days after serving of the notice. The notice shall further advise the owner or occupant that if such condition is not corrected or remedied within the ten-day period, the city manager may cause the violation to be removed or corrected at the owner's expense. 
(d)  Failure of owner to correct violations. The owner or occupant of any property who shall fail within ten days after service of such written notice by the chief of police to trim, prune or remove any such tree, plant, hedge, wall fence or other structure or vegetation that violates the provisions of this division shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be punished as provided in section 1-15. A separate offense shall be deemed to have been committed on every day that any such violation is permitted to remain after the expiration of the period of ten days after the service of the notice. The property owner shall also be responsible for all costs of correction of the violation. 
(e)  Authority of city manager to trim or remove vegetation. The city manager is authorized to remove, or cause to be removed, any tree or plants found between the opposite curblines in any street in the city, and to trim branches, limbs or foliage of any tree or plant which overhangs or grows above the area which lies between the opposite curblines of any street, so as to provide a minimum clearance of eight feet above the street level at the curbline and so as to be graduated toward the center of the street to a clearance of 12 feet above the street level at the center of the street. 
(Code 1973, §§ 18-23, 18-27-18-29; Ord. No. 719, §§ 2(b), 3(e), 3(f), 4(a), 11-6-1957; Ord. No. 1184, 4-12-1977) 
Secs. 40-77-40-95. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - SIDEWALKS 

Sec. 40-96. - Obstruction prohibited. 
    It is unlawful for any person to place or cause to be placed, or allow to remain, on any street or sidewalk in the city, any box, barrel, crate, merchandise, fuel or any other article which in any way obstructs the free passage along such street or sidewalk; provided, however, this section shall not apply to merchandise or other articles on sidewalks which are actually being received or sent out, if the same do not occupy more than half of the sidewalk and do not remain thereon for more than one hour. 
(Code 1973, § 18-4; Ord. No. 1124, § 1, 10-9-1925) 
Sec. 40-97. - Uniform width and specified grade required in business districts. 
    In the business districts, sidewalk construction shall be of a uniform width of ten feet and on the grade established by the city engineer. 
(Code 1973, § 18-6; Ord. No. 1071, § 2, 3-3-1913) 
Sec. 40-98. - Crosswalks to be constructed by property owners. 
    When the city constructs crosswalks over the streets or roadways of the city, it shall be the duty of the abutting property owner to construct a crosswalk of like character as his sidewalk, to connect such sidewalk at the curbline with the crosswalk constructed by the city. 
(Code 1973, § 18-7; Ord. No. 1071, § 3, 3-3-1913) 
Chapter 42 - SUBDIVISIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal and county authority to regulate subdivisions, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 242.001 et seq.; municipal zoning authority generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 211.001 et seq.; municipal planning and development generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 371.001 et seq.; municipal zoning boards of adjustment, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 211.008; issuance of local permits, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 245.001 et seq.; municipal comprehensive plans, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 213.001 et seq.; authority for municipal regulation of signs, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 216.001 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 42-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Approved plat means a plat of a subdivision which has been approved in accordance with the requirements of this chapter and regulations and which has been filed for record with the county clerks of DeWitt or Lavaca counties. In instances where a lot lies in both counties, the approved plat must be filed in both counties. 
    Easement means a right granted for the purpose of limited public or semipublic use across, over or under private land. 
    Lot means land occupied or to be occupied by a building and its accessory buildings and including such open spaces as are required by ordinances of the city and having its principal frontage upon a public street or officially approved place. 
    Lot of record means a lot which is part of a subdivision, the plat of which has been recorded in the offices of the county clerks of DeWitt or Lavaca counties, or parcel of land, the deed for which was recorded in the offices of the county clerks of DeWitt or Lavaca counties prior to the passage of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived. 
    Plat means a complete and exact subdivision plan submitted to the city council for final approval and which, if approved, will be submitted to the county clerks of DeWitt or Lavaca counties. 
    Standards means the official maps, comprehensive master plans, ordinances and specifications of the city. 
    Street means a way for vehicular traffic, whether designated a street, highway, thoroughfare, parkway, throughway, road, avenue, boulevard, alley, land, place, or however otherwise designated, including: 
(1)  Street, primary or arterial, means a street used primarily for fast or heavy traffic designated in the major street plan as a primary street, expressway or freeway. 
(2)  Street, secondary or collector, means a street that carries traffic from minor streets to the major system of arterial streets and highways, including the principal entrance streets of a residential development and streets for circulation within such a development, designated in the major street plan as secondary streets. 
(3)  Street, minor, means a street used primarily for access to abutting properties. 
(4)  Street, marginal, means a minor street that is parallel to and adjacent to arterial streets and highways and that provides access to abutting properties and protection from through traffic. 
(5)  Street, cul-de-sac, means a short minor street having but one vehicular service access to another street and terminated by vehicular turnarounds. 
(6)  Street, dead-end, means a street other than a cul-de-sac with only one outlet. 
(7)  Alley means a minor way used primarily for vehicular service access to the back or the side of properties otherwise abutting on a street. 
    Subdivider and developer are synonymous and include any person, partnership, firm, association, corporation or any officer, agent, employee, servant and trustee thereof who does or participates in the doing of any act toward the subdivision of land within the intent, scope and purview of this chapter. 
    Subdivision means the division of a parcel of land into two or more lots or tracts for the purpose of transfer of ownership, dedication of streets, alleys or easements, or for use for building development; provided, a division of land for agricultural purposes into lots or tracts of five acres or more and not involving a new street or alley shall not be deemed a subdivision. The term "subdivision" includes resubdivision and, when appropriate to the context, shall relate to the process of subdividing or to the land subdivided. 
(Code 1973, § 19-1; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. II, 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-2. - Purpose and intent. 
    The purpose and intent of this chapter is to provide procedure and standards for the development, layout and design of subdivisions of land within the city, and for such other areas as may be authorized by state law, and to: 
(1)  Promote and develop the utilization of land to ensure the best possible community environment in accordance with the master plan of the city. 
(2)  Guide and assist and expedite the developers in correct procedures to be followed and to inform them of the standards which shall be required. 
(3)  Protect the public interest by controlling the location, design, class and type of streets, sidewalks, utilities and essential areas and services required. 
(4)  Protect and promote the health, safety and general welfare. 
(Code 1973, § 19-3; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. I, 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-3. - Chapter provides minimum standards. 
    In the interpretation and application of the provisions of these regulations, it is the intention of the city council that the principles, standards and requirements provided for herein shall be minimum requirements for the platting and developing of subdivisions in the city, and, where other provisions of this Code are more restrictive in their requirements, such other provisions shall control. 
(Code 1973, § 19-2; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. I, 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-4. - Fees. 
    All fees related to this chapter shall be established from time to time by the council as provided in the city fee schedule. Fees shall be collected by the city in advance, and no action of the city council shall be valid until the applicable fees have been paid to the city. These fees shall be charged on all plats, regardless of the action taken by the city council, whether the plat is approved or denied. The money collected shall defray the cost of administrative, clerical and inspection services necessary to properly investigate the plats, replats and subdivisions. 
(Code 1973, § 19-18; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. VII, 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-5. - Variances. 
(a)  The city council may authorize a variance from these regulations when in its opinion undue hardship will result from requiring strict compliance. In granting a variance, the city council shall prescribe only conditions that it deems necessary or desirable to the public interest in making the findings required in this section. 
(b)  In determining whether to grant a variance, the city council shall take into account the nature of the proposed use of land involved and existing uses of the land in the vicinity, the number of persons who will reside or work in the proposed subdivision and the probable effect of such variances upon traffic conditions and upon the public health, safety, convenience and welfare in the vicinity. No variance will be granted unless the city council finds that: 
(1)  There are special circumstances or conditions affecting the land involved, such that the strict application of the provisions of this chapter would deprive the applicant of the reasonable use of his land. 
(2)  The variance is necessary for the preservation and enjoyment of a substantial property right of the applicant, that the granting of the variance will not be detrimental to the public health, safety or welfare or injurious to other property in the area. 
(3)  The granting of the variance will not have the effect of preventing the orderly subdivision of other lands in the area in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. 
(c)  Such findings of the city council together with the specific facts on which such findings are based shall be incorporated under the official minutes of the city council meeting at which such variance is granted. 
(d)  Variances may be granted only when in harmony with the general purpose and intent of this chapter so that the public health, safety and welfare may be secured and substantial justice done. Pecuniary hardship to the subdivider, standing alone, shall not be deemed to constitute undue hardship. The city council may not authorize a variance that would constitute a violation of any other valid ordinance of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 19-20; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. X, 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-6. - Violations declared public nuisance; enforcement authority of city manager. 
    Any subdivision of land being developed in violation of the terms and provisions of these regulations is declared to be a public nuisance and the city manager is authorized to institute any action which may be necessary to restrain or abate such violation. 
(Code 1973, § 19-21; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-7. - Withholding city services and facilities for noncompliance. 
(a)  The city defines its policy to be that the city will withhold all city improvements and facilities of whatsoever nature, including the maintenance of streets and the furnishing of sewerage facilities and water services, from all additions, the platting of which has not been approved by the city planning commission. 
(b)  The city may withhold the issuing of a street number or building permit for the erection of any building in the city on a newly subdivided parcel of land until all the requirements of these subdivision regulations have been complied with, including installation of and acceptance by the city of all waterworks, sewerage and paving improvements for the area designated. 
(c)  No construction work shall begin on the proposed improvements in any proposed subdivision prior to approval of the final plat by the city and the filing of such plat with the county clerks of the DeWitt or Lavaca counties. 
(Ord. No. 1017, § 17, art. VI(D), 9-8-1971) 
Secs. 42-8-42-32. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PLAT PROCEDURE 

Sec. 42-33. - Preapplication consultation. 
    The subdivider shall avail himself of the advice and assistance of the city manager before preparing the preliminary plat and before formal application for its approval in order to save time and money and to make the most of his opportunities. 
(Code 1973, § 19-4; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. III(A), 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-34. - Preliminary plat submission and review. 
(a)  Application filing. On reaching conclusions informally as recommended above regarding the general program and objectives, the subdivider shall prepare a preliminary plat together with improvement plans and other supplementary material as applicable in other sections of this article. Five copies of the preliminary plat and supplementary materials specified shall be submitted to the city with the filing fee as provided in the city fee schedule and written application for conditional approval at least ten days prior to the city council meeting at which it is to be considered. 
(b)  Size; scale; paper. All preliminary plats shall be printed on good grade processed paper blue line or direct black and white. Copies or prints of the proposed subdivision shall be drawn on sheets a maximum size of 24 inches by 36 inches and drawn to a scale of 90 feet to the inch (one inch equals 90 feet). In cases of large developments which would exceed the dimensions of the sheet of 90 foot scale, the preliminary plat may be at a scale of 200 feet to the inch (one inch equals 200 feet). Each subdivision consisting of three acres or more shall be prepared on a topographic base map showing contours at intervals not greater than five feet. Any subdivision smaller than three acres which, in the opinion of the city manager, would be affected by the topographical features of the terrain shall also show contours at two foot intervals. All topographical maps shall be based on sea level data. 
(c)  Content. The application for proposed subdivision shall show the following: 
(1)  The title of the subdivision or addition, name of subdividers and engineer, surveyor or planner platting the tract. 
(2)  Boundary lines, bearings and distances sufficient to locate the exact area proposed for subdivision. 
(3)  The name and location of all adjoining subdivisions shall be drawn to the same scale and shown in dotted lines adjacent to the tract proposed for subdivision in sufficient detail to show accurately the existing streets and alleys and other features that may influence the layout of development of the proposed subdivision. Adjacent unplatted land shall be so designated. If there is no adjacent subdivision, then a map on a smaller scale must be presented to show the nearest subdivision and how the streets, alleys or highways in the subdivision submitted may connect with those in the nearest subdivision. 
(4)  Recorded lot lines, survey abstract lines, corporation lines and the location of existing utility easements, streets, highways, expressways and freeways traversing, abutting or within a reasonable distance. 
(5)  The proposed locations and widths of streets, alleys, easements, walkways, open channels and lots. 
(6)  The location of all existing property lines, buildings, sewer or water mains, gas mains or other underground structures, easements or other existing features within the area proposed for subdivision. 
(7)  Lot or tract numbers or city block numbers, addition names and dates recorded. 
(8)  Proposed arrangement of lots and proposed use of same; however, approval of a preliminary plat or final plat with uses so indicated does not constitute approval of such uses. 
(9)  Proposed building lines showing conformance with this article and city zoning regulations. 
(10)  The title under which the proposed subdivision is to be recorded, the name and address of the owner with the name of the land planner, licensed land surveyor or registered professional engineer platting the tract. 
(11)  Sites, if any, to be reserved or dedicated for parks, playgrounds or other public uses. 
(12)  Scale, north arrow, date and other pertinent data and so drawn that the north direction is to the top or left side of the map. 
(13)  Contours with intervals of five feet or less shall be shown for the area. All elevations on the contour map shall be referenced to the latest U.S. Coast and Geodetic Survey data. 
(14)  All physical features of the property to be subdivided, including locations of all watercourses, ravines, bridges, culverts, existing structures and other features pertinent to subdivision. The outline of wooded areas or the location of important individual trees may be required. 
(d)  Plats to be marked as preliminary. The following notice shall be placed on the face of each preliminary plat by the developer: "Preliminary Plat." 
(e)  City manager review of application. The city manager shall make a study of the plat and give a report to the city planning commission before its final action on the preliminary plat. 
(f)  Planning commission review. The planning commission shall examine application, plat and related material submitted for conformity to these regulations and may, if necessary, enter into negotiations with the subdivider on changes deemed advisable and the kind and extent of improvements to be made by him. The commission shall thereafter submit its recommendation to the city council. 
(g)  Action by city council. The city council shall, within 30 days after the filing of such preliminary plat, act thereon as submitted or modified, and, if approved, the city council shall express its approval as conditional approval and state the conditions of such approval, if any, or if disapproval, shall express its disapproval and its reasons therefor. The action of the city council shall be noted on two copies of the preliminary plat, referenced and attached to any conditions required by the city council. Action of the city council shall be certified by the city clerk. One copy shall be returned to the subdivider and the other retained in the files of the city. 
(h)  Effect of conditional approval by city council.
