Conditional approval of a preliminary plat by the city council shall be deemed an expression of approval of the layouts submitted on the preliminary plat as a guide to the installation of streets, water, sewer and other required improvements and utilities and to the preparation of the final or record plat. Except as provided for herein, approval of the preliminary plat shall constitute conditional approval of the final plat when all conditions of approval noted as provided in this section have been met. No work shall be done on the subdivision before the final plat is accepted and recorded except with the written approval of the city council. 
(i)  Term of conditional approval; expiration. Conditional approval of a preliminary plat shall be effective for one year unless reviewed by the city council in the light of new or significant information which would necessitate the revision of the preliminary plat. If no development or change in requirements has occurred which would affect the proposed plat at the end of the year of an effective approval, the city council may extend its approval another year without the submission of a new preliminary plat by reapproving the original preliminary plat. No filing fee is required for such reapproval. 
(Code 1973, § 19-14; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, arts. III(B), VI(A), 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-35. - Final plat submission, review and recording. 
(a)  Size, scale, paper. All final plats shall be printed on good grade processed paper blue line or direct black and white. All final plats shall be submitted on sheets 24 inches by 36 inches, and to a scale of not less than 90 feet to the inch or larger. Where more than one sheet is required to encompass the subdivision, an index sheet 24 inches by 36 inches shall be filed showing the entire subdivision, together with the complete dedication, attests, dates, titles and seals on one sheet. 
(b)  Required markings and permitted tables. The exterior boundary of the subdivision shall be indicated by the distinct dash line and corner markers by individual symbols. The length and bearing of all straight lines, radii, area lengths, tangent lengths and central angles of all curves shall be indicated along the boundary line of the subdivision and each block. All dimensions along the lines of each lot shall be shown. The curve data pertaining to the block or lot boundary may be placed in a curve table at the base of the plat and prepared in the following manner: 
CURVE TABLE 
Curve 
Number Description Elements Outer 
Property 
Line Center Line Inner 
Property 
Line  
(c)  Title and owners, adjoining properties, lots and blocks, streets, and utility easements. The final plat shall show: 
(1)  A title including the name of the addition or subdivision, the names of the owner and engineer or surveyor, the scale and location of the subdivision with reference to the original land grant or survey and the abstract number and north point with true or magnetic north. 
(2)  The names of all adjoining subdivisions, the dimensions of all abutting lots, lot and block numbers and accurate reference ties to courses and distances of at least two recognized land corners. 
(3)  The names and accurate locations of all streets adjoining, abutting or within not more than 500 feet of the subdivision. 
(4)  The location and dimension of any utility easement adjoining or abutting the subdivision or proposed within the subdivision. 
(d)  Survey monuments. The description and location of all survey monuments placed in the addition or subdivision shall be shown. 
(e)  Relationship to preliminary plat. The final plat shall conform to the preliminary plat as approved and shall incorporate all changes, directions and additions imposed by the city council. If so desired by the developer, the final plat may constitute only that portion of the approved preliminary plat which he proposes to record and then develop; provided, however, that such portion conforms to all the requirements of these regulations. 
(f)  Engineering plans. Engineering plans showing details of streets, alleys, culverts, bridges, storm sewers, water mains, sanitary sewers and other engineering details of the proposed subdivision shall be submitted to the city manager along with the final plat of the subdivision. Such plans shall be prepared by a registered professional engineer and shall conform to the design standards established by the city. The final plat will not be released for filing until detailed engineering plans have been approved by the city council. 
(g)  Certificates. The following certificates must be submitted as indicated: 
(1)  Ownership. A certificate of ownership giving a metes and bounds description of the property, dedication of all streets, alleys, parkways and parks, where donated to the city and dedication or reservation of all easements and drainage ways to the public use, signed and acknowledged before a notary public by the owner of the land, shall appear on the face of the plat or index sheet of the plats where two or more sheets are required. 
(2)  Survey. The certificate of the licensed professional engineer or licensed public surveyor who surveyed, mapped and monumented the land, which certificates shall be attested before a notary public, shall be placed on the face of the plan on index sheets of the plats together with the seals of the engineer or surveyor and notary public. Printed seals and signatures are prohibited except for extra prints that the owner or developer may need certified for other purposes. The certificate of the engineer or surveyor to be placed on the plat shall be in the form approved by the city council from time to time, a copy of which is on file in the office of the city clerk. 
(3)  Taxes. At the time the developer files the final plat with the city manager, he shall also file a certificate showing that all taxes have been paid on the tract to be subdivided and that no delinquent taxes exist against the property. 
(h)  Review by city manager and approval by city council. Upon receipt of the final plat, accompanied by a final filing fee in the amount provided in the city fee schedule, the city manager shall check the plat to ascertain its compliance with these regulations and the action of the city council. When the copy of the final plat has been checked and found to meet all general requirements and design standards, the developer or his engineers shall submit six copies of the final plat to the city manager. The city manager shall stamp on each of the six copies the certificate of approval of the city council attested by the chairperson of the city council when such final plat has been approved. 
(i)  Recording of final plats. The developer or his authorized agent will secure the required number of plats and record them with the county clerks of DeWitt or Lavaca counties, within 30 days of the date of the final approval; otherwise the approval of the city council becomes invalid. Two copies of the recorded final plat shall be returned immediately to the city manager. 
(Code 1973, § 19-6; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, arts. III(C), VI(B), 9-8-1971) 
Secs. 42-36-42-58. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DESIGN AND CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS 

Sec. 42-59. - Streets. 
(a)  The arrangement, character, extent, width, grade and location of all streets shall conform to the city major thoroughfare plan and shall be considered in their relation to existing and planned streets, to topographical conditions, to public safety, and in their appropriate relation to the proposed uses of the land to be served by such streets. 
(b)  When such streets are not on the major thoroughfare plan, the arrangement of streets in a subdivision shall either provide for the continuation of appropriate projections of existing streets in surrounding areas or conform to a plan for the neighborhood approved or adopted by the city planning commission to meet a particular situation where topographical or other conditions make continuance or conformity to existing streets impracticable. 
(c)  Minor streets shall be so laid out that their use by through traffic will be discouraged. 
(d)  If the subdivision abuts or contains an existing or proposed arterial street, the city planning commission may require marginal access streets, reverse frontage, deep lots with rear service alleys or such treatment as may be necessary for adequate protection to residential properties and to afford separation of through and local traffic. 
(e)  Reserve strips controlling access to streets shall be prohibited except where their control is definitely placed in the city under conditions approved by the city planning commission. 
(f)  Street jobs with centerline offsets of less than 125 feet shall be avoided. 
(g)  Arterial street intersections shall be at 90-degree angles. Other street intersections shall be laid out so as to intersect as nearly as possible at right angles, and no street shall intersect at less than 75 degrees. 
(h)  Street right-of-way widths shall be as shown on the master thoroughfare plan and if not shown therein shall be not less than as follows: 
(1)  Primary or arterial thoroughfares: Maximum 90 feet, depending upon the location and the city street plat with which the primary thoroughfare is to be connected. 
(2)  Secondary thoroughfares: 60 feet. 
(3)  Minor residential streets: 50 feet. 
(4)  Access or service roads: 40 feet. 
(5)  Minor streets in apartment, commercial or industrial areas: 60 feet. 
(i)  Half streets are prohibited except when essential to the reasonable development of the subdivision in conforming to the other requirements of these regulations, and where the city council finds it will be practical to require the dedication of the other one-half when the adjoining property is subdivided. Whenever a partial street exists along a common property line, the other portion of the street shall be dedicated. Where part of a street is being dedicated along a common property line and the ultimate planned width is 50 feet, the first dedication will be 30 feet; where the ultimate planned width is 60 feet, the first dedication will be 35 feet. 
(j)  A cul-de-sac shall not be longer than 600 feet and at the closed end shall have a turnaround having an outside roadway diameter of at least 80 feet and a street property line diameter of at least 90 feet. 
(k)  New streets of like alignment shall bear the names of existing streets and shall be dedicated at equal or greater widths than the existing streets. No street name shall be used which will duplicate or be confused with the names of existing streets. Street names shall be subject to approval of the city council. 
(l)  All new streets dedicated within a subdivision shall be improved in accordance with specifications of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 19-7; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. IV(A), 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-60. - Alleys. 
(a)  Alleys shall be provided in commercial and industrial districts except that the city council may waive this requirement where other definite and assured provision is made for service access such as off-street loading, unloading and parking consistent with and adequate for the use proposed. Service alleys in commercial and industrial districts shall be a minimum of 25 feet in width. 
(b)  In residential districts, alleys, if provided, shall be parallel or approximately parallel to the frontage of the street. Alleys in residential districts shall be a minimum of 20 feet in width and must be covered by six inches of gravel. 
(c)  Where the deflection of alley alignment exceeds 30 degrees, a cutback of a minimum of 15 feet or of such greater distance as to provide safe vehicular movement shall be established on the inside property line and the alley, if paved, shall have the paving cut back in the same manner. 
(d)  Dead-end alleys shall be avoided where possible, but if unavoidable shall be provided with adequate turnaround facilities at the dead-end as determined by the city council. 
(Code 1973, § 19-8; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. IV(B), 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-61. - Easements. 
(a)  Easements shall be provided at the rear of lots not served by alleys, running parallel or approximately parallel to the frontage of the street. All easements in residential districts shall be a minimum of 20 feet in width. 
(b)  Easements across lots or centered on side lot lines shall be provided for utilities where necessary and shall be of such widths as may be reasonably necessary for the utility using same. 
(c)  Where a subdivision is traversed by a watercourse, drainage way, channel or street, there shall be provided a storm easement or drainage right-of-way conforming substantially with such course and of such additional width as may be designated by the city manager that will be reasonably adequate for the purpose. Parallel streets or parkways may be required in connection with this. 
(Code 1973, § 19-9; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. IV(C), 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-62. - Blocks. 
(a)  The lengths, widths and shapes of blocks shall be determined with due regard to provision of adequate building sites suitable to the special needs of the type of use contemplated, zoning requirements as to lot sizes and dimensions, and needs for convenient access, circulation, control and safety of street traffic. 
(b)  In general, intersecting streets, which determine the blocks' lengths and widths, shall be provided at such intervals as to serve cross traffic adequately and to meet existing streets or customary subdivision practices. Where no existing subdivision dictates, the block length shall not exceed 1,600 feet and shall generally be 1,000 to 1,200 feet in length. Where no existing subdivision dictates, the block shall not be less than 500 feet in length; however, in cases where physical barriers or property ownership creates conditions where it is appropriate that these standards be varied, the length may be increased or decreased to meet the existing conditions having due regard for connecting streets, circulation of traffic and public safety. 
(c)  Where blocks in the vicinity of a school, park or shopping center are platted 1,000 feet or longer, the city council may require a walkway near the middle of the block or at a street that terminates between the streets at the ends of the block. The walkway shall not be less than four feet or more than eight feet in width, shall have a four-foot concrete walk through the block from sidewalk to sidewalk, or to the rear property line if no street. Where no existing subdivision controls, the block width or depth shall be platted to give lots with a depth to width ratio of generally not more than 21/2 to one and in no case more than four to one, and the platting shall be such that the block width or depth generally shall not exceed 350 feet or be less than 215 feet. When possible, the block width and length shall be such as to allow two tiers of lots back to back to an alley. 
(d)  Pedestrian walks not less than four feet wide shall be provided around the perimeter of all blocks. 
(Code 1973, § 19-10; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. IV(D), 9-8-1971). 
Sec. 42-63. - Lots. 
(a)  Lots shall conform to the minimum requirements of the established zoning district. 
(b)  Each lot shall face on a public street. 
(c)  Where corner lots are key lots, that is where lots face the frontage street and also other lots face the side street, the corner lot shall have a front building line on both streets. 
(d)  Key lots or irregularly shaped lots shall have sufficient width at the building line to meet frontage requirements of the appropriate zoning district. Also, the rear width shall be sufficient to provide access for all utilities including garbage collection, but not less than ten feet. 
(e)  No lot shall be platted less than 90 feet in depth except in cases where an irregularly shaped tract is platted into lots and the remnant piece of property is of sufficient area to plat one or more lots. The city council may waive the depth requirement to prevent a hardship on the developer. 
(f)  Side lot lines shall be substantially at right angles or radial to street lines. 
(g)  Double frontage and reverse frontage lots should be avoided except where essential to provide separation of residential development from traffic arteries or to overcome specific disadvantage of topography and orientation. Where lots have double frontage, a front building line shall be established for each street. 
(h)  Lot sizes may be increased from that originally platted, provided that there is no remaining portion of a lot smaller than the original lot and that the final plat is submitted in accordance with the requirements of this article. 
(i)  In areas where the city sewer is not immediately available, a lot shall be platted of such area as to meet the minimum requirements of the city pertaining to septic tank operation or applicable county health office standards. The minimum area of any lot not served by the city sewer shall be 12,000 square feet. 
(j)  No lot shall be replatted to reduce the size of the lots originally platted by a common dedicator, unless the consent of all the property owners in the same addition has been obtained. No lot will be reduced in width below a 50-foot frontage with an area of 5,000 square feet, except for property having a local retail, commercial or manufacturing zoning classification and not for residential use. 
(k)  When an applicant exhibits a duly executed and recorded deed covering a lot having dimensions of 50 feet by 90 feet or more, which has been sold by metes and bounds prior to the passage of the ordinance from which this article is derived, and such lot is being assessed for school taxes and conforms to the established lot pattern and zoning classification in the block where located, then a building permit may be issued, provided the requested use of such property conforms to the permanent zoning of the property covered by the application. 
(l)  Subdivision plats for housing projects, apartment areas, shopping centers and industrial districts will not be required except in cases where dedications for streets, street widening, alleys or easements are required. Site plans shall be filed with the city for approval by the city council. 
(Code 1973, § 19-11; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. IV(E), 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-64. - Survey monuments. 
    In all subdivisions and additions, corner monuments shall be established at the corner of each block in the subdivision consisting of an iron rod or pipe not less than three-quarters inch in diameter and 24 inches deep set flush with the top of the sidewalk. Lot corner monuments shall be placed at all lot corners except corners which are also block corners, consisting of iron rods or pipes of a diameter of not less than one-half inch and 18 inches deep set flush with the top of the sidewalk. In addition, curve point markers shall be established of the same specifications as lot corner monuments. 
(Code 1973, § 19-15; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. VI(B), 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-65. - Building lines. 
    Building lines shall be as shown on the final plat on all lots intended for business and residential use and shall provide the minimum setback as required by the zoning ordinance. 
(Code 1973, § 19-12; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. IV(F), 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-66. - Public sites and open spaces. 
(a)  The subdivider may give consideration to suitable sites for schools, parks, playgrounds and other areas for public use so as to conform to the recommendations of the city council. Any provision for schools, parks, etc., may be indicated on the preliminary plat. 
(b)  No individual, partnership, firm or corporation shall deepen, widen, fill, reroute or change the course or location of any existing ditch, channel, stream or drainage way without first obtaining written permission of the city or other agency having jurisdiction. 
(c)  In cases where a subdivision contains or abuts a school, park or playground, the subdivider shall dedicate one-half a normal residential street, 25 feet, and provide for one-half the cost of paving and the full cost of all the utilities necessary. The interested agency shall provide the necessary right-of-way to make the street 60 feet in width (which is 35 feet), and provide one-half the cost of the paving. 
(Code 1973, § 19-13; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. V, 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-67. - Improvements required prior to acceptance. 
(a)  Monuments. Monuments shall be placed as required by this article. 
(b)  Storm drainage. An adequate storm sewer system consisting of inlets, pipes and other underground drainage structures with approved outlets shall be constructed where runoff of storm water and the prevention of erosion cannot be accomplished satisfactorily by surface drainage facilities. Areas subject to flood conditions, as established by the city, will not be considered for development until adequate drainage has been provided. 
(c)  Water. All subdivisions shall be provided with an approved water system. In the corporate limits of the city, subdivisions shall be connected with the city water supply distribution system. Without cost to the city, the subdivider shall install all water and sewer lines, including customer services. The engineer representing the subdivider shall prepare the plans and specifications for the water and sewer lines and present them to the city for approval before construction. All construction shall be paid for by the subdivider. Meters will be installed by the water department in accordance with established tapping fees. 
(d)  Street, alley and sidewalk improvements. 
(1)  Before approval and acceptance of any final plat, the developer shall prepare, or have prepared, and submit three copies of the complete engineering plans of streets, alleys, curbs and gutters, storm sewers and drainage structures, and water and sanitary sewer improvements for the area covered by the final plat. The developer shall have these plans prepared by his own engineers subject to approval of the plans by the city. The city manager shall review the plans and specifications and, if approved, two sets shall be marked with the objections noted and returned to the developer for correction. 
(2)  After approval of the plat and of the plans and specifications, the developer shall cause his contractor to install the facilities in accordance with the approved plans and specifications and these regulations. The developer shall cause his engineer to design, stake and supervise the construction of such improvements and shall cause his contractor to construct the improvements in accordance with these regulations. The city will inspect the installation of the improvements. 
(3)  When found to be installed in accordance with the plans and specifications, and after the improvements have been completed and upon receipt of the city of a one-year maintenance bond from each separate contractor in the amount of ten percent of the contract price, along with three sets of as-built plans and one set of as-built sepias, and upon receipt of a letter of the contractor's compliance with these regulations, the city manager shall receive and approve for the city the title, use and maintenance of the improvements. As used in this section, the term "as-built plans" means the developer or his engineer shall present the city with a reproducible (sepia) complete as-built set of plans and three sets of blue line or black line prints on paper of as-built plans for all paving, drainage structures and water mains within 60 days after completion of each contract. 
(4)  Minor residential streets shall be paved 31 feet wide from back of curb to back of curb. Minor apartment streets and secondary collector streets shall be paved 41 feet wide from back of curb to back of curb. The minimum street improvements which shall be made by the developer shall be six-inch curb and 24-inch gutter of 2,500 psi concrete with adequate drainage inlets and structures to drain the area properly. Street surfacing consisting of 11/2-inch thickness cold or hot mix asphaltic concrete on six inches compacted thickness gravel base with a separate curb and gutter or five inches reinforced concrete (2,500 psi) pavement with either separate or integral curb and gutter. 
(5)  Sidewalks shall be four feet wide, four inches thick and shall be of 2,500 psi concrete. 
(6)  Alleys when provided shall have a minimum surfacing of six inches of gravel. 
(e)  Sewer improvements. 
(1)  All subdivisions shall be provided with an approved sewage disposal system and where the subdivision is inside the city limits shall be connected to the city sanitary sewer system. The developer shall furnish and install the complete sewerage system, including the mains, manholes, cleanouts, Y branches and service laterals for all lots, lift stations and appurtenances. The sewerage system shall be designed and constructed in accordance with the master plan and standard specifications of the city. 
(2)  In locations where sanitary sewers are not available and where there is no immediate prospect for installation of sanitary sewers, septic tanks of an approved type may be installed in conformity with the rules, regulations and ordinances of the city pertaining to public health; provided, however, that in no case shall septic tanks be installed without the express approval and inspection of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 19-16; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. VI(C), 9-8-1971) 
Sec. 42-68. - Street signs. 
(a)  Within the corporate limits of the city, street signs will be installed by the city at each intersection and the subdivider shall pay to the city the amount per street sign set forth in the city fee schedule toward the cost of installation of each street sign. The developer shall pay such sum as computed by the city manager for street signs as set out herein at the time at which he submits his final plat for approval, and this sum shall be in addition to the filing fee set forth hereinabove. 
(b)  In subdivisions lying beyond the corporate limits of the city, street name signs shall be placed by the subdivider at all intersections within or abutting the subdivision. Such signs shall be of a type approved by the city and shall be installed in accordance with the standards of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 19-19; Ord. No. 1017, § 1, art. IX, 9-8-1971) 
Chapter 44 - TAXATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal Sales and Use Tax Act, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 321.001 et seq.; Development Corporation Act, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 501.001 et seq.; real and tangible personal property taxable, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 11.01; intangible personal property taxable, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 11.02; freeport exemption of tangible personal property, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 11.251; homestead exemption, V.T.C.A., Property Code § 41.001; municipal hotel occupancy taxes, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 351.001 et seq.; tax abatement in municipal reinvestment zones, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 312.201 et seq.; authority to levy certain occupation taxes, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 101.008. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 44-1. - Sales and use tax. 
    The city council officially and affirmatively declares that the one per cent local sales and use tax within the city has been properly and lawfully adopted in accordance with state law. 
(Code 1973, § 7-14; Ord. No. 1603, 8-10-1993) 
State Law reference- Municipal Sales and Use Tax Act, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 321.001 et seq. 
Secs. 44-2-44-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PROPERTY TAXES 

Sec. 44-21. - Certificate of taxes due; issuance; fee. 
    Upon application to the tax assessor and collector of any property owner of the city, his agent or attorney, and the payment of a fee hereinafter mentioned, the tax assessor and collector of the city shall as soon as practical issue a certificate showing the amount of taxes due, if any, on any piece of real estate in the city and shall properly seal and attest same. The tax assessor and collector shall collect a fee as set by the city council for the certificate covering each piece of property, which shall be credited to the general fund of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 7-13; Ord. No. 1603, 8-10-1993) 
Sec. 44-22. - Tax delinquency penalties and interest. 
    If any person fails to pay taxes imposed on him or his property by the city on or before January 31 of the next succeeding year for which such taxes are assessed, the penalty and interest as set out in the state property tax code, is due and payable. 
(Code 1973, § 7-15; Ord. No. 1603, 8-10-1993) 
Secs. 44-23-44-47. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - HOTEL OCCUPANCY TAX[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal hotel occupancy taxes, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 351.001 et seq.; levy of tax authorized, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 351.002; tax rates, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 351.003. 

Sec. 44-48. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Hotel means any building, trailer or other facility in which the public may, for a consideration, obtain sleeping accommodations. The term "hotel" shall include hotels, motels, tourist homes, houses or courts, lodginghouses, inns, roominghouses, trailer houses, trailer motels, or dormitory space where bed space is rented to individuals or groups, but shall not mean apartments occupied by permanent residents, and shall not include hospitals, sanitariums, or nursing homes. 
    Occupancy means the use or possession or the right to use or possession of any room, space, or sleeping facility in a hotel for any purpose. 
    Occupant means anyone who, for a consideration of at least $2.00 per day, uses, possesses, or has a right to use or possess any room or sleeping space or facility in a hotel or other accommodations defined as a hotel. 
    Permanent resident means any occupant who has or shall have the right of occupancy of any room or sleeping space or facility in a hotel for at least 30 consecutive days during the calendar year or preceding year. 
    Person means any individual, company, corporation, partnership or association owning, operating, managing, or controlling any hotel. 
    Quarterly period means the regular calendar quarters of the year, the first quarter being composed of the months of January, February, and March; the second quarter being the months of April, May, and June; the third quarter being the months of July, August, and September; and the fourth quarter being the months of October, November, and December. 
    Tax assessor-collector means the tax collector-assessor of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 7-16; Ord. No. 1202, § 1, 9-13-1977) 
Sec. 44-49. - Levy of rate; exceptions. 
(a)  There is levied a tax upon the occupant of any room or space furnished by any hotel where such cost of occupancy is at the rate of $2.00 or more per day; such tax to be equal to a percentage, pursuant to the manual of fees and service charges of the city, of the consideration paid by the occupant of such room, space, or facility to such hotel, exclusive of other occupancy taxes imposed by other governmental agencies and exclusive of any sales taxes. 
(b)  No tax shall be imposed hereunder upon a permanent resident. 
(c)  No tax shall be imposed hereunder upon an occupant of any room or space rented from a corporation or association organized and operated exclusively for religious, charitable, or education purposes, no part of the net earnings of which inures to the benefit of any private shareholder or individual. 
(d)  All revenue derived from the occupancy tax imposed in subsection (a) of this section shall be used for the following: 
(1)  The acquisition of sites for and the construction, improvement, enlarging, equipping, repairing, operation and maintenance of convention center facilities, including, but not limited to, civic center convention buildings, auditoriums, coliseums and parking areas or facilities for the parking or storage of motor vehicles or other conveyances located at or in the immediate vicinity of convention center facilities. 
(2)  The furnishing of facilities, personnel and materials for the registration of convention delegates or registrants. 
(3)  For advertising of general promotional nature and tourist advertising of the city and its vicinity, and conducting a solicitation and operating program to attract conventions and visitors either by the city or through contracts with persons or organizations selected by the city. 
(Code 1973, § 7-17; Ord. No. 1202, § 2, 9-13-1977) 
Sec. 44-50. - Collection. 
    Every person owning, operating, managing, or controlling any hotel, as herein defined, shall collect the tax imposed herein for the city. 
(Code 1973, § 7-18; Ord. No. 1202, § 3, 9-13-1977) 
Sec. 44-51. - Reports. 
    By the last day of the month following each quarterly period, every person required herein to collect the tax imposed by this article shall file a report with the tax assessor-collector showing the consideration paid for all room occupancies in the preceding quarter, the amount of the tax collected on such occupancies and any other information as the tax assessor-collector may reasonably require. Such persons shall pay the amount of tax collected from occupants during the period of the report at the time of the filing of such report. 
(Code 1973, § 7-19; Ord. No. 1202, § 4, 9-13-1977; Ord. No. 1287, 4-14-1981) 
Sec. 44-52. - Rules and regulations. 
    The tax assessor-collector shall have the power to make such rules and regulations as are necessary to effectively collect the tax levied herein, and shall upon reasonable notice have access to books and records belonging to such hotels as herein defined necessary to enable him to determine the correctness of any report filed as required by this article and the amount of taxes due under the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1973, § 7-20; Ord. No. 1202, § 5, 9-13-1977) 
Sec. 44-53. - Penalties. 
    If any person owning, operating, managing, or controlling any hotel as herein defined shall fail or refuse to collect the tax imposed herein, or shall fail or refuse to file a report as required herein, or shall fail or refuse to pay to the tax assessor-collector the tax as imposed herein when the report for payment is due, or shall file a false report, then such person shall be determined guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, be punished by a fine not to exceed $200.00. In addition, such person who fails to remit the tax imposed by this article within the time required shall forfeit five percent of the amount due as a penalty, and after the first 30 days shall forfeit an additional five percent of such tax; provided, however, that the penalty shall never be less than $1.00. Delinquent taxes shall draw interest at the rate of six percent per annum, beginning 30 days from the date due on the tax imposed by this article. 
(Code 1973, § 7-21; Ord. No. 1202, § 6, 9-13-1977) 
Sec. 44-54. - Reimbursements. 
    The person shall have the right to retain one percent of the amount of the tax collected as reimbursement for the cost of collecting the tax. In the event the person fails to file reports as required in section 44-51, then the one percent reimbursement shall be forfeited. 
(Code 1973, § 7-22; Ord. No. 1312, 12-8-1981) 
Chapter 46 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Rules of the road, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 541.001 et seq.; powers of local authorities regarding regulation of traffic, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.202; limitations on local authorities, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 42.203; municipal authority to regulate parking, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 601.001; municipal streets generally, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 312.001 et seq.; railroad and roadway crossings, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 471.001 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 46-1. - Use of engine brake prohibited. 
    It is unlawful to use or operate an auxiliary or compression engine brake that produces any noise in addition to the normal operating engine noise within the city except when such use is required due to the failure of a vehicle's service brakes or for the avoidance of imminent danger. This provision shall not be construed to prohibit the use of such braking mechanism by emergency vehicles while in the performance of their official or normal duties. 
(Code 1973, § 14-3; Ord. No. 1923, § 1, 7-10-2007) 
Sec. 46-2. - Repairing or washing vehicle in street. 
    No person shall repair or wash any vehicle in any street in the city. 
(Code 1973, § 21-1; Ord. No. 1121A, § 3, 8-4-1925) 
Sec. 46-3. - Driving on new pavement or closed street. 
    It is unlawful for any person to drive upon newly laid or constructed city pavement or any other closed street in the city so long as there are barriers or notices posted along or across such street, and until such time as the street is officially opened for public use. 
(Code 1973, § 21-2; Ord. No. 107, § 1, 12-5-1929) 
Sec. 46-4. - Turning around. 
    It is unlawful for any person operating any vehicle within the city to turn such vehicle on any city street so as to proceed in the opposite direction. 
(Code 1973, § 21-9; Ord. No. 1014, § 1, 8-9-1971) 
Secs. 46-5-46-26. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - WEIGHT LIMITS AND TRUCK ROUTES 

Sec. 46-27. - Truck routes designated; heavy trucks required to use. 
    Except as otherwise specifically provided in this chapter, truck routes shall be those routes designated as state or federal highways including farm-to-market highways as marked in the city. It is unlawful for any person to operate or permit operation of any motor truck with a carrying capacity of more than two tons on any street in the city other than certain listed streets designated in this article as truck routes. 
(Code 1973, §§ 21-3, 21-4; Ord. No. 923, §§ 1, 2, 6-12-1967; Ord. No. 1241, 4-10-1979) 
Sec. 46-28. - Deviation for certain purposes. 
    Truck route restrictions shall not apply to the operation of a motor truck of more than two tons carrying capacity to locations to secure fuel or repairs or to load or unload cargo or for the purpose of parking an unloaded vehicle on private property. Any such operation away from the designated truck routes shall be by the most direct route and return thereto. 
(Code 1973, § 21-5; Ord. No. 923, § 5, 6-12-1967; Ord. No. 1241, 4-10-1979) 
Secs. 46-29-46-59. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PARKING[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Stopping, standing and parking generally, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.301; parking, towing and storage of vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 681.001 et seq. 

Sec. 46-60. - Manner of parking. 
    No person shall park the vehicle in a street other than parallel with the edge of the street, headed in the direction of the traffic, and with the curb-side wheels of the vehicle within 18 inches of the edge of the curb or the edge of the roadway, except upon those streets which have been marked or signed for angle parking as approved by the chief of police and city manager, in which case vehicles shall be parked at the angle to the curb indicated by the mark or sign. Whenever parking spaces are marked by lines on the pavement, whether for parallel or angle parking, a vehicle must be parked entirely within the lines of the parking space. 
(Code 1973, § 18-53; Ord. No. 1915, § 3, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 46-61. - Parking near intersections restricted. 
    Parking is prohibited within 15 feet from the intersection of curblines or edge of the roadway at an intersection, except at alleys where parking shall be prohibited within ten feet from the edge of the intersection of the alley with the roadway unless otherwise marked. 
(Code 1973, § 18-53; Ord. No. 1915, § 3, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 46-62. - Parking in alleys prohibited. 
    It is unlawful for any person to use the alleys within the city for the purpose of parking vehicles except for temporary use for loading and unloading. 
(Code 1973, § 18-54; Ord. No. 1915, § 4, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 46-63. - Parking prohibited on designated streets. 
    Parking is prohibited on the following streets or portions thereof: 
(1)  The south side of the 300 block of West Grand Avenue; 
(2)  On the north side of the 300 block of West Grand Avenue as marked; 
(3)  The east side of Irvine Street for a distance of 55 feet, eight inches in a southerly direction beginning at the southern right-of-way of West Grand Avenue; 
(4)  The west side of Irvine Street for a distance of 60 feet, six inches in a southerly direction beginning at the south curbline of West Grand Avenue; 
(5)  The east side of Irvine Street for a distance of 70 feet in a southerly direction beginning at the south curbline West May Street; 
(6)  The west side of Irvine Street for a distance of 47 feet in a southerly direction beginning at West May Street; 
(7)  The 100 block of Irvine Street; 
(8)  The south side of West Gonzales for a distance of 150 feet in a westerly direction beginning at the west right-of-way line of Irvine Street; 
(9)  The north side of West Gonzales for a distance of 950 feet in an easterly direction beginning at the curbline of Capitol Street; and 
(10)  The south side of West Gonzales Street between Irvine and Hopkins Streets. 
(Code 1973, § 18-55; Ord. No. 1915, § 5, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 46-64. - Truck and trailer parking. 
(a)  Parking of any two-ton rated truck or larger with or without trailers, and all trailers pulled by the trucks is prohibited along both sides of all streets and highways on publicly owned rights-of-way within the corporate limits of the city. 
(b)  Parking of any trailer, motor home, or recreational vehicle whether pull behind or motorized is prohibited along both sides of all state marked thoroughfares on publicly owned rights-of-way within the corporate limits of the city except to perform maintenance or service activities. 
(c)  Parking of any vehicle, trailer, motor home, or recreational vehicle may be prohibited on any street within the corporate limits of the city by law enforcement officers as deemed necessary to maintain adequate traffic flow or to avoid any traffic hazard. 
(d)  No person shall stop, stand, or park a vehicle regulated under this section except: 
(1)  For temporary use for loading and unloading; 
(2)  When necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic; 
(3)  At the direction of a police officer; or 
(4)  In obedience to a traffic control device. 
(Code 1973, §§ 18-56, 18-57, 21-5; Ord. No. 923, § 5, 6-12-1967; Ord. No. 1241, 4-10-1979; Ord. No. 1915, §§ 6, 7, 12-12-2006) 
State Law reference- Overnight parking of commercial motor vehicles in or near residential subdivisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.307. 
Secs. 46-65-46-86. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - PLAY VEHICLES AND DEVICES 

Sec. 46-87. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Central business district shall be defined as that portion of the city bounded by West Gonzales Street on the north, West Street on the south, McCarty Street on the west and the railroad lines on the east. 
    Unsafe manner means to operate a vehicle or device in such a manner that may endanger the health and safety of the rider or any member of the public. 
(Code 1973, § 18-81; Ord. No. 1933, § 1, 1-8-2008) 
Sec. 46-88. - Use on sidewalks in central business district prohibited. 
    No person shall ride in, upon or in any manner operate any skateboard, roller skates, rollerblades, foot-operated scooter, bicycle or similar device upon any public property, including streets, alleys and sidewalks, within the central business district. 
(Code 1973, § 18-82; Ord. No. 1933, § 2, 1-8-2008) 
Sec. 46-89. - Use in unsafe manner prohibited. 
    No person shall ride or in any manner operate any skateboard, roller skates, rollerblades, foot-operated scooter, bicycle, or similar devices in an unsafe manner on any street, sidewalk, walkway, or on any public property at the entrance or exit used for passage of persons or vehicles to which the public or substantial group of the public has access. 
(Code 1973, § 18-82; Ord. No. 1933, § 2, 1-8-2008) 
Sec. 46-90. - Ramps, jumps or similar devices prohibited. 
    No person will construct any ramp, jump or similar device intended for use by a person with a skateboard, roller skates, rollerblades, foot-operated scooter, bicycle or similar device on any public property, including, but not limited to, street, alley, sidewalk, walkway, waterway or the locations used for passage of persons or vehicles. 
(Code 1973, § 18-83; Ord. No. 1933, § 3, 1-8-2008) 
Sec. 46-91. - Deposit of wax or similar substances prohibited. 
    It is unlawful for any person to place any wax or other similar substance used to provide a lubricated surface for the purpose of easing the movement of skateboards, roller skates, rollerblades, foot-operated scooters or similar devices on any public property, right-of-way or any other place that has been or may be prohibited or which contains any sign prohibiting the riding of skateboards, skates, rollerblades or similar devices. 
(Code 1973, § 18-84; Ord. No. 1933, § 4, 1-8-2008) 
Sec. 46-92. - Authority to prohibit operation on private property. 
    Owners or managers of restaurants, businesses, professional buildings, churches, schools, or shopping centers may prohibit persons from riding in, upon, or in any manner operate any skateboard, roller skates, rollerblades, foot-operated scooters, bicycles or similar devices upon sidewalks and parking lots of the premises. Owners or managers of these types of establishments may prohibit such activity by posting a sign bearing one of the following legends: 
(1)  "Use of skateboards, roller skates, rollerblades, foot-operated scooters, bicycles or similar devices on these premises is unlawful per Yoakum City Code." 
(2)  "It is unlawful to use skateboards, roller skates, rollerblades, foot-operated scooters, bicycles or similar devices on these premises during business hours per Yoakum City Code." 
(Code 1973, § 18-85; Ord. No. 1933, § 5, 1-8-2008) 
Secs. 46-93-46-112. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - GOLF CARTS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Golf carts and utility vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 551.401 et seq.; requirements for slow-moving vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 547.703; vehicle equipment, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 547.001 et seq. 

Sec. 46-113. - Applicability. 
    This article pertains only to golf carts that are not registered by or titled in this state. 
(Code 1973, § 18-103; Ord. No. 1962, § 1, 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 46-114. - Operation permitted during daylight hours only; maximum speed. 
    Persons possessing a valid driver's license may operate a golf cart on roadways within the city limits unless otherwise prohibited by the state department of transportation. Such golf carts may only be operated at speeds of 35 miles per hour or less and only during daylight hours (from 30 minutes before sunrise to 30 minutes after sunset). 
(Code 1973, § 18-101; Ord. No. 1962, § 1, 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 46-115. - Required equipment and safety features. 
    Except as otherwise specifically provided in this section, any golf cart operated in the city must be equipped with all safety features required by state law, including, without limitation, functional safety belts, headlamps, tail lamps, parking brake, side-view mirrors, reflects and slow-moving vehicle emblem; provided, however, that golf carts operated not more than two miles from the location where the golf cart is usually parked and for transportation to and from a golf course are not required to have safety belts or side-view mirrors. The operator and all occupants of the golf cart are required to utilize all safety equipment and features. 
(Code 1973, §§ 18-101, 18-102; Ord. No. 1962, § 1, 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 46-116. - Maximum number of occupants. 
    Golf carts operated in the city may not carry more occupants than the number of seats provided by the cart. Each occupant must occupy a proper seat. 
(Code 1973, § 18-101; Ord. No. 1962, § 1, 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 46-117. - Liability insurance. 
    Any golf cart operated in the city must be covered by appropriate liability insurance as required for motor vehicles by state law. 
(Code 1973, § 18-101; Ord. No. 1962, § 1, 12-8-2009) 
Chapter 48 - UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal water and utilities generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 551.001 et seq.; municipal utility systems, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 552.001 et seq.; agreement with conservation and reclamation districts, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 552.903; Texas Water Quality Act, V.T.C.A., Water Code § 21.001 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 48-1. - Prohibiting the sale of water. 
    It is unlawful for any person other than the city to barter, give away, or offer for sale water originating from any source within the city. This section shall not prohibit the sale of bottled or distilled water. 
(Ord. No. 2037, § 5, 3-12-2013) 
Sec. 48-2. - City manager in charge. 
    The city utilities, consisting of all the properties of the sewer, water and electricity plants, and systems of the city shall be under the control, management and maintenance of the city manager, who shall at all times be responsible to the city council for the proper and legal conduct of all the affairs of the city utilities. Among his other duties, he shall, subject to the approval of the city council, employ and fix wages and salaries of all employees of the department. 
(Code 1973, § 22-1; Ord. No. 695, § I, 3-13-1957) 
Sec. 48-3. - Referendum required before sale of system. 
    The city utilities system shall never be sold by the city unless and until such sale shall have been authorized at an election held to decide on the propriety of such sale, in which election a majority of the votes cast shall have been in favor of such sale. 
(Code 1973, § 22-2; Ord. No. 695, § II, 3-13-1957) 
Secs. 48-4-48-24. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - RATES, CHARGES, BILLING AND COLLECTIONS 

Sec. 48-25. - No free service. 
    No free service shall be rendered by the waterworks, sewer or electric system to any customer except institutions operated by the city. 
(Code 1973, § 22-10; Ord. No. 715, § 5, 9-10-1957) 
Sec. 48-26. - Fees, rates and charges provided in city fee schedule. 
    Fees, rates and charges associated with this chapter shall be in the amounts established from time to time by the city council as provided in the city fee schedule, including, but not limited to, water service rates, electric service rates, sewer service rates, connection and reconnection charges, tap charges, pavement cutting and restoration fees, fire sprinkler fees, fog system fees, late fees and interest. Industrial sewer use surcharges are subject to the provisions of article III of this chapter. 
Sec. 48-27. - Payment of water connection charges. 
    Water tapping fees will be paid at the time the taps are requested unless the meter is larger than one inch. If meter is larger than one inch, the customer will be billed the actual cost plus 25 percent. In existing additions where a developer is opening up several lots and new street work is to be done, the developer will be required to have the taps put in place and pay for the taps at the existing rates before any street work is completed. In new additions where we require taps to be put in by the developer, or where there is an existing tap on a vacant lot, there will be a meter setting charge. 
(Code 1973, § 22-4; Ord. No. 929-A, § 1, 6-28-1967; Ord. No. 1257, 12-11-1979; Ord. No. 1388, 12-11-1984; Ord. No. 1433, 7-8-1986) 
Sec. 48-28. - Payment for other city utility service charges; late payment penalty. 
    Rates and charges provided in the city fee schedule shall be paid by users of the waterworks, sewer or electric system to the city clerk in advance of the tenth day of each month, which shall be the date such service rates or charges shall become due and payable. If any user or customer of such system does not pay the amount due on the tenth day of the month, it shall be the duty of the city clerk to add a ten percent penalty to the amount past due and unpaid. 
(Code 1973, § 22-8; Ord. No. 715, § 3, 9-10-1957; Ord. No. 929-A, § 1, 6-28-1967) 
Sec. 48-29. - Cut off for delinquency; reconnection charge. 
    In the event any user or customer of the waterworks, sewer or electric system does not pay matured service rates and charges within eight days from the date they become due and payable, it shall be the duty of the city clerk to disconnect the water service or the electric service; whenever the amount past due and delinquent is paid by such user or customer, such service may be resumed upon payment of a reconnect fee in the amount provided in the city fee schedule. After hours is defined as on weekends, and after 5:00 p.m. and before 8:00 a.m. on weekdays. No disconnects shall be made on Fridays, nor on days preceding a holiday. 
(Code 1973, § 22-9; Ord. No. 715, § 4, 9-10-1957; Ord. No. 1063, 4-10-1973; Ord. No. 1388, 12-11-1984) 
Sec. 48-30. - Discontinuance of utility and garbage service for delinquency. 
    Failure to pay any charges for water, electric power, sewer or garbage service within the time specified for payment shall entitle and empower the city to discontinue service for all such utilities. 
(Code 1973, § 22-12; Res. No. 1045, 9-12-1972) 
Secs. 48-31-48-48. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - INDUSTRIAL SEWER USE 

Sec. 48-49. - Prohibited discharges; types of water. 
(a)  No person shall discharge, or cause to be discharged, any stormwater, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, downspouts, yard drains, yard fountains and ponds, lawn sprays, water from swimming pools or unpolluted industrial water into any sanitary sewer in the system. 
(b)  No person shall discharge, or cause to be discharged, into any public sewer any of the following described substances, materials, waters, or wastes: 
(1)  Any liquid or vapor having a temperature greater than 122 degrees Fahrenheit (50 degrees Centigrade). 
(2)  Any toxic, corrosive, flammable or explosive liquid, solid or gas, such as gasoline, kerosene, phenols, benzene, naphtha, etc. 
(3)  Any waters or wastes which contain wax, greases, oil, cleaning solvents, mineral oils or other substances which will solidify or become discernible viscous at temperatures between 32 degrees to 150 degrees Fahrenheit. 
(4)  Any garbage that has not been properly comminuted or shredded (the installation and operation of any garbage grinder equipped with a motor of three-fourths horsepower or greater shall be subject to the review and approval of the city manager). 
(5)  Any solid or viscous substances, such as, but not limited to, ashes, cinders, sand, mud gravel, straw, tar asphalt, ceramic wastes, shavings, sawdust, metal, glass, rags, feathers, plastics, whole blood, paunch manure, hair and fleshings, entrails, lime residues, lime slurries, slops, chemical residues, paint residues, or bulk solids. 
(6)  Any material which may cause excessive discoloration, such as, but not limited to, dye wastes and vegetable tanning solutions where the coloration will not be removed by the sewage treatment process. 
(7)  Any heavy metals, such as those listed below: 
Antimony Lead Arsenic Manganese Barium Mercury Beryllium Molybdenum Bismuth Nickel Boron Rhenium Cadmium Selenium Chromium (Hexa) Silver Chromium (Tri) Strontium Cobalt Tellurium Copper Tin Iron Uranylion Zinc  
Discharge of these materials into the sewer system shall be prohibited. 
(8)  Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half life or concentration that exceeds limits established by the U.S. Public Health Service for Public Drinking Water Standards. 
(9)  Any waste or substance which exerts an excessive chlorine requirement which will cause a chlorine demand greater than that which is considered normal, based on the past history of chlorine demand. 
(10)  Any waste or substance causing an excessive chemical oxygen demand (COD). 
(11)  Any wastes or waters containing substances which are not amenable to treatment or reduction by the sewage treatment processes employed, or are amenable to treatment only to such degree that the sewage treatment plant effluent cannot meet the requirements of the state, federal, or other public agencies having jurisdiction over discharge to the receiving waters. 
(Code 1973, §§ 22-20, 22-21; Ord. No. 1502, §§ A, B, 1-10-1989) 
Sec. 48-50. - Permissible discharges. 
    Discharge into the city sewerage system shall consist only of domestic sewage, properly shredded garbage, industrial wastes and other wastes which are free from the prohibited constituents listed in section 48-49, and limited in BOD, suspended solids, dissolved sulfides, pH grease, fats, and oils as follows: 
(1)  Biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) of such wastes delivered shall not exceed 200 ppm., as determined by standard methods. 
(2)  Suspended solids delivered shall not exceed 200 ppm., as determined by standard methods. 
(3)  Hydrogen ion concentration (pH) of the sewage delivered shall be no lower than 6.0 nor higher than 9.0 and any acid wastes shall not be discharged unless neutralized to a pH of 6.0 or more, and any alkaline waste shall not be discharged until neutralized to a pH of 9.0 or less. 
(4)  Dissolved sulfides in the wastes delivered to the system shall not exceed 0.1 ppm. 
(5)  Alkalinity shall not exceed 400 ppm. 
(6)  Dissolved oxygen content shall be at least 2.0 ppm through 3.0 ppm minimum. 
(7)  Fats, oil, and grease shall not exceed 90 ppm. 
(Code 1973, § 22-22; Ord. No. 1502, § C, 1-10-1989; Ord. No. 1757, 7-11-2000; Ord. No. 1921, § 1, 5-8-2007) 
Sec. 48-51. - Volume and rate of flow. 
    The volume and rate of flow of wastes to the sewerage system shall not be in excess of the capacity of the facility provided as determined and regulated by the city utility department. 
(Code 1973, § 22-23; Ord. No. 1502, § D, 1-10-1989) 
Sec. 48-52. - Pretreatment; inspection facilities; interceptors. 
(a)  Pretreatment required; control manhole. Any persons or owners discharging industrial wastes into the sewerage system which exhibit any of the prohibited wastes set out in this article shall pretreat or otherwise dispose of such industrial waste in a manner that meets all federal, state, local, or other public agency requirements, to make the remaining wastes meet the requirements of this article, and be acceptable to the city utility department. Any such person or owner shall provide and maintain, in a suitable accessible position on his premises, an inspection chamber or control manhole near the outlet of such sewer prior to the discharge into the city system. Every such chamber shall be of such design and construction which will prevent infiltration of any water or foreign matter into the city system and shall be so maintained by the person discharging wastes so that any authorized representative of the city may readily and safely measure the volume and obtain samples of the flow at all times. 
(b)  Design and installation of plant, equipment of pretreatment or equalization facilities. Where pretreatment or equalization of waste flows is practiced prior to discharge to the city's sewer system, the design and installation of the plants and equipment of the pretreatment or equalization facilities shall be subject to the review and approval of the city manager and subject to the requirements of all applicable codes, ordinances, and laws. 
(c)  Grease, sand, oil interceptors; type; capacity; location; construction. Grease, oil, and sand interceptors shall be provided for the proper handling of liquid wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, lint, or any flammable wastes, sand, and other harmful ingredients. All interceptors shall be of a type and capacity approved by the city utilities superintendent and plumbing inspector, and shall be located as to be readily accessible for cleaning and inspection. Grease and oil interceptors shall be constructed of impervious materials capable of withstanding abrupt and extreme changes in temperatures. They shall be of substantial construction, watertight, and equipped with easily removable covers which when bolted in place shall be gastight and watertight. Such interceptors shall be maintained by the user at his expense, in a continuously efficient operation at all times. 
(d)  Waste of unusual strength. No statement contained in this article shall be construed as preventing any agreement or arrangement between the city and any industrial concern whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or character may be accepted by the city for treatment, subject to payment therefor by the industrial concern for any portion of the excess cost to the city of handling and treating such industrial wastes, as may be established by the city council. 
(Code 1973, § 22-24) 
Sec. 48-53. - Damaging, uncovering, defacing structures, equipment, etc. 
    No unauthorized person shall maliciously, willfully, or negligently break, damage, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance, or equipment which is a part of the municipal sewage works. Any person violating this provision shall be subject to immediate arrest under the charge of disorderly conduct. 
(Code 1973, § 22-25; Ord. No. 1502, § E, 1-10-1989) 
Sec. 48-54. - Industrial discharge into storm sewers prohibited. 
    The discharge of industrial sewage wastes into the storm sewer system or stormwater drainage system of the city is prohibited. 
(Code 1973, § 22-26; Ord. No. 1502, § I, 1-10-1989) 
Sec. 48-55. - Industrial sewer charge schedule. 
(a)  Generally. Industrial sewage waste is more costly and more difficult to process due to the injurious material and biochemical oxygen demand contained in the sewage. To ensure that industrial users pay their fair, reasonable and just cost for use of the city's sewer system, all persons using any portion of the city sewer system and either directly or indirectly discharging sewage waste into the system shall be charged the current rate in the manual of fees and service charges of the city or a charge set by the city council. 
(b)  Surcharge. In the event any person, firm, or corporation who is an industrial user of the sewer system and sewer lines of the city, and whose wastes discharged to the city sewer system exceed the values set out in section 48-50, then the person, firm, or corporation shall pay a surcharge for waste treatment in addition to the customer charges as listed in the utilities section of the manual of fees and service charges. 
(c)  Surcharge determination factors. The surcharge shall be calculated as follows: 
ISc = V [a(BOD - 200) + b(S.S. - 200) + c(FOG - 100)] 
where: 
(1)  ISc = Industrial surcharge. 
(2)  V = Volume discharge in thousands of gallons as based upon metered water consumption as recorded in meter reading records, unless discharger installs a meter, at his expense, to determine the volume discharged. Metering device to be approved by the city. 
(3)  a = BOD surcharge factor (dollars per 1,000 gallons, per milligram, per liter) based on the treatment costs attributable to BOD. 
(4)  BOD = Five day biochemical oxygen demand at 20 degrees Celsius, of the industrial waste, in parts per million measured on composite samples. 
(5)  b = S.S. surcharge factor (dollars per 1,000 gallons, per milligram, per liter) based on the treatment costs attributable to the removal of S.S. 
(6)  S.S. = suspended solids in the industrial waste in parts per million, measured on composite samples. 
(7)  c = FOG surcharge factor (dollar amount per 1,000 gallons, per milligram, per liter) based on treatment cost. 
(8)  FOG = Fats, oil, and grease measured in parts per million, measured on composite samples. 
(9)  Composite samples = A sample composed of a series of not less than three samples taken over a period of time not exceeding 24 hours. 
(10)  Grab sample = Taken on a one-time basis with no regard to flow or time. 
(11)  The factors "a," "b," and "c" shall be evaluated as follows: 
a = 0.0034 
b = 0.0017 
c = 0.0005 
These factors shall be subject to review with each increase in domestic sewer service charges so that industrial users will carry their fair share of the costs for construction and operation of sewage treatment within the city. 
(d)  Users whose water is not wholly supplied by city. In the event any person, firm or corporation who is an industrial user of the sewer system and sewer lines of the city and whose water is not supplied wholly by the city, and where the bill for the water used thereon or therein in this event would not clearly show the amount of sewage the industrial user was putting into the city's municipal sewer system, then in each case the amount of water so used shall be otherwise measured and determined by the city manager in order to determine the fair and reasonable charge to be made for sewer services provided in this section and these users shall be billed accordingly. 
(e)  Industrial sewage waste discharge. The discharge of industrial sewage wastes into the storm sewer system or stormwater drainage system of the city is prohibited. 
(Code 1973, § 22-27; Ord. No. 1502, § I, 1-10-1989; Ord. No. 1757, 7-11-2000; Ord. No. 1921, § 1, 5-8-2007) 
Sec. 48-56. - Powers and authority of enforcing agents. 
    The city manager and other duly authorized employees of the city bearing proper credentials and identifications shall be permitted to enter upon all properties for the purposes of inspection, observations, measurement sampling, and testing, in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1973, § 22-28; Ord. No. 1502, § F, 1-10-1989) 
Sec. 48-57. - Testing procedures. 
(a)  Generally. All measurements, tests, and analyses of the characteristics of waters and wastes to which reference is made in this article shall be determined in accordance with the latest edition of "Standard Methods for the Examination of Water and Wastewater," published by the American Public Health Association or, if the city deems it necessary, sampling shall be performed in accordance with the procedures set forth in the most current edition of EPA publication, "Sampling and Analysis Procedures for Screening of Industrial Effluents for Priority Pollutants," or with other sampling and analytical procedures approved by the EPA. The measurements and test shall be determined at the control manhole provided, or upon suitable samples taken at the control manhole. In the event that no special manhole has been required, the control manhole shall be considered to be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to the point at which the building sewer is connected. Sampling shall be carried out by customarily accepted methods to reflect the affect of constituents upon the sewage works and to determine the existence of hazards of life, limb, and property. The particular analyses involved will determine whether a 24-hour composite of all outfalls of a premises is appropriate or whether a grab sample shall be taken. 
(b)  Sampling, testing, measurements to be made by city. All sampling, testing and measurements shall be made by the city. The city may select an independent firm or laboratory to perform the measurements, sampling or testing. All cost incurred by the city shall be at the expense of the person, firm, or corporation discharging into the sewer system. 
(Code 1973, § 22-29; Ord. No. 1502, §§ J, K, 1-10-1989) 
Sec. 48-58. - Penalties for violation. 
(a)  Generally. Any person found to be violating any provision of this article shall be served by the city with written notice stating the nature of the violation and providing a reasonable time limit for the satisfactory correction thereof. The offender shall, within the period of time stated in such notice, permanently cease all violations. If the offender continues violation after the expiration of the time stated, the city council may prohibit the further use of the sewage system by the offender and may remove or close the offender's sewage and water connections. 
(b)  Continuing violations. Any person who shall continue any violation beyond the time limit provided shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished as provided in section 1-15 for each violation. Each day in which any such violation shall continue shall be deemed a separate offense. 
(c)  Liability. Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall become liable to the city for any expense, loss or damage occasioned by the city by reason of such violation. 
(Code 1973, § 22-30; Ord. No. 1502, § G, 1-10-1989; Ord. No. 1757, 7-11-2000) 
Secs. 48-59-48-89. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - BACKFLOW PREVENTION AND CROSS-CONNECTION CONTROL 

Sec. 48-90. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Air gap means a physical separation between the free flowing discharge end of a potable water supply pipeline and an open or nonpressure receiving vessel. An approved air gap shall be at least double the size of the supply pipe measured vertically above the overflow rim of the vessel, in no case less than one inch. 
    Approved air gap, a double check valve assembly, a reduced pressure principle backflow prevention assembly, or other backflow prevention assemblies or methods means any assembly judged by the water purveyor to be in conformance with this article and the AWWA standards. 
    Approved water supply means a water supply that is in compliance with the state rules and regulations for public water systems and is approved by this state and the city. 
    Auxiliary water supply means any water supply on or available to the premises other than the city's approved public water supply. These auxiliary waters may include water from another purveyor's public potable water supply or any natural sources, such as a well, spring, river, stream, harbor, etc., or used waters or industrial fluids. These waters may be contaminated or polluted or they may be objectionable and constitute an unacceptable water source over which the city is not afforded complete access and control. 
    Backflow means the undesirable reversal of flow of water or mixtures of water and other liquids, gases, or other substances into the distribution pipes of the potable supply of water from any source. 
    Backflow preventer means an assembly or means designed to prevent backflow. 
    Backpressure means any elevation of pressure in the downstream piping system (by pump, thermal expansion, elevation of piping, or steam or other gaseous pressure) above the supply pressure at the point of consideration which would cause, or tend to cause, a reversal of the normal direction of flow. 
    Backsiphonage means a form of backflow due to a reduction in system pressure which causes a subatmospheric pressure to exist at a site in the water system. 
    Consumer means the owner of the property and private plumbing system, and any person responsible for initiating or maintaining an active or inactive water or sewer service with the water purveyor. 
    Contamination means an impairment of a potable water supply by the introduction or admission of any foreign substance that degrades the quality and creates a health hazard. 
    Cross-connection means any unprotected actual or potential connection or structural arrangement between a public or a consumer's potable water system and any other source or system through which it is possible to introduce into any part of the potable system any used water, industrial fluid, gas or substance other than the intended potable water with which the system is supplied. Bypass arrangements, bumper connections, removable sections, swivel or change-over devices and other temporary or permanent devices through which or because of which backflow can or may occur are considered to be cross-connections. 
    Cross-connection, control by containment, means the appropriate type or method of backflow protection at the service connection, commensurate with the degree of hazard of the consumer's water system. 
    Cross-connection, control by isolation, means the appropriate type or method or backflow protection, providing internal system control at the cross-connection or point of potential entry into any potable water system, commensurate with the degree of hazard. 
    Cross-connection, controlled, means a connection between a potable water system and a nonpotable water system with an approved backflow prevention assembly properly installed and maintained so that it will continuously afford the protection commensurate with the degree of hazard. 
    Direct cross-connection means a cross-connection which is subject to both backsiphonage and backpressure. 
    Double check valve backflow prevention assembly means an assembly composed of two independently acting, approved check valves, including tightly closing resilient seated shutoff valves attached at each end of the assembly and fitted with properly located resilient seated test cocks. This assembly shall only be used to protect against a non-health hazard (i.e., pollutant). 
    Hazard, degree of, means either a pollutional (non-health) or contamination (health) hazard and is derived from the evaluation of conditions within a system. 
    Hazard, health, means a cross-connection, potential cross-connection, or other situation involving any substance that could cause death, illness, spread of disease, or has a high probability of causing such effects if introduced into the potable drinking water supply. 
    Hazard, plumbing, means an internal or plumbing type cross-connection in a consumer's potable water system that may be either a pollutional or a contamination type hazard. Such a connection, if permitted to exist, must be properly protected by an appropriate type of backflow prevention assembly. 
    Hazard, pollutional, means an actual or potential threat to the physical properties of a water system or the potability of the public or consumer's potable water system but which would not constitute a health or system hazard as defined. The maximum degree of pollution to which the potable water system could be degraded under this definition would cause a nuisance or be aesthetically objectionable or could cause minor damage to the system or its appurtenances. 
    Hazard, system, means an actual or potential threat of severe danger to the physical properties of the public or consumer's potable water system or of a pollution or contamination which would have a protracted effect on the quality of the potable water in the systems. 
    Indirect cross-connection means a cross-connection which is subject to backsiphonage only. 
    Industrial fluids means any fluid or solution which may be chemically, biologically or otherwise contaminated or polluted in a form or concentration which would constitute a health, system, pollutional, or plumbing hazard if introduced into an approved water system. This may include, but not be limited to: polluted or contaminated used waters, all types of process and used waters, chemicals in fluid form, acids and alkalies, circulated cooling waters, auxiliary water supplies, oils, gases, glycerin, paraffins, caustic and acid solutions, and other gaseous fluids used industrially, for other purposes, or for firefighting purposes. 
    Pollution means the presence of any foreign substance in water that tends to degrade its quality so as to constitute a non-health hazard or impair the usefulness of the water. 
    Reduced pressure principle backflow prevention assembly means an assembly containing two independently acting approved check valves together with a hydraulically operating, mechanically independent pressure differential relief valve located between the check valves and below the first check valve. The unit shall include the properly located resilient seated test cocks and tightly closing resilient seated shutoff valves at each end of the assembly. This assembly is designed to protect against a non-health (i.e., pollutant) or a health hazard (i.e., contaminant). This assembly shall not be used for backflow protection of sewage, radioactive or reclaimed water, or any other potentially lethal contamination. 
    Water, nonpotable, means a water supply which has not been approved for human consumption by this state and the city or which may be of unknown or questionable quality. 
    Water, potable, means any public water supply which has been investigated, approved, and is in compliance with state rules and regulations for public water supplies, and the city. In determining what constitutes an approved water supply, the water purveyor has final judgment as to its safety and potability. 
    Water, service connection, means the terminal end of the service connection from the city's potable water system (where the city may lose jurisdiction and sanitary control of the water at its point of delivery to the consumer's water system). If a water meter is installed at the end of the service connection, then the service connection means the downstream end of the water meter. 
    Water, used, means any water supplied by a water purveyor from a public potable water system to a consumer's water system after it has passed through the service connection and is no longer under the complete control of the city. 
(Code 1973, § 22-41; Ord. No. 1673, § 2, 4-9-1996) 
Sec. 48-91. - Penalties for violations. 
(a)  Any person who shall fail or refuse to comply with any provision of this article shall be guilty of a Class C misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be punished as provided in section 1-15. Each day of violation of this article shall be considered a separate offense. 
(b)  Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall become liable to the city for any expense, loss or damage occasioned by the city by reason of such violation. 
(Code 1973, § 22-43; Ord. No. 1867, 3-8-2005) 
Sec. 48-92. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this article is: 
(1)  To protect the public potable water supply of the city from the possibility of contamination or pollution by isolating within the consumer's internal distribution systems or the consumer's private water systems such contaminants or pollutants which could backflow into the public water system; 
(2)  To promote the discovery and elimination or control of existing cross-connections, actual or potential, between the consumer's potable water systems and nonpotable water systems, plumbing fixtures and industrial piping system; and 
(3)  To provide for the maintenance of a continuing program of cross-connection control which will systematically and effectively prevent the contamination or pollution of all potable water systems. 
(Code 1973, § 22-40(a); Ord. No. 1673, § 1, 4-9-1996)
